# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 21

759

B"H, Sunday, 15 Teves, 5685
Yekaterinoslav

To the honorable Gaon, Sinai and remover of mountains, sharp and incisive, a pillar of Torah, a man of many talents, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav R’ Y. Rozin, shlita,

Greetings and peace to his Torah!

Your brief letter has reached me. Although who am I to disagree with you, nevertheless, it is Torah, and I must learn; I shall be like a student before the wise, especially since you were brief in your words.

And this is the matter:

If we say that a *treifah* cannot return to a state of *kashrus*, it is difficult to reconcile with the case of *sircha* (adhesion) in the place of their growth (*rabbisaihu*), according to Rashi in *Chullin* 46a and 47a, where the perforation is formed first and the *sircha* afterwards. And even though the Ran explains this difficulty by saying that a perforation capable of developing a *sircha* is not considered a *treifah* from the outset, and we only deem all perforations *treifos* due to a lack of knowledge—which is a somewhat forced explanation—it is still difficult to reconcile with the case of a lung that was perforated and the wall seals it (*Chullin* 48a). According to Rashi and the Rambam (*Hilchos Shechitah*, ch. 7), if it is sealed by flesh, it is kosher, whereas if it is sealed by bone, it is *treifah*. Since the *treifah* status is due to the perforation, and this—on the face of it—does not depend on whether it adheres to the rib or between the ribs, and the *sircha* is formed subsequently, and since it does not depend on the perforation, one cannot apply the Ran’s reasoning here, nor can one categorize this as a clarification retroactively. Furthermore, the language of the Gemara proves that a *sircha* is a disqualification that returns to a state of *kashrus*. Also, from Rashi (*Chullin* 46b, 47b, 48a, and *Yevamos* 76a), it is implied that a membrane that grew due to a wound is not a membrane that will eventually tear, and the sealing of the wall is a superior seal. (Therefore, one must also say regarding Rashi on 43a that his primary intent is as he stated at the beginning of his words.) The Rambam (*Hilchos Shechitah*, ch. 3, halacha 21) also implies this to some extent. If a *treifah* cannot return to a state of *kashrus*, then an essential element is missing from the book, as is understood. From all this, one can bring proof that it does return to a state of *kashrus*.

Indeed, according to this, the Gemara in *Chullin* 68b, which you, your honor, cited, requires study. Perhaps it can be explained that it refers to the verse, and the *treifah* mentioned in the Torah is a *derusah* (preyed upon)—as per Rambam (*Hilchos Ma'achalos Asuros* 4:6 and *Hilchos Shechitah* 5:1, 3)—and its *treifah* status is not due to being perforated (*Tosafos, Chullin* 42b). If so, we can say that the Sages were certain that it is impossible to find a cure for a *derusah*, and "a *treifah* has no remedy" means there is no cure in reality for a *derusah*, not that it cannot return to a state of *kashrus*. With this, we can also resolve the source of the law that a *treifah* itself has no remedy, as it is compared to meat that has gone outside its boundary, and it depends on whether it is taught (*Tosafos* there, s.v. *HaKol*).

If the law is that it returns to a state of *kashrus*, then in my case, where it is a superior seal, the animal is kosher.

One should not raise an objection from *Chullin* (54a) and (57b), for one must say that the fact that a *treifah* does not live is only if they did not provide it with a cure; otherwise, there is a cure even for a *pesik reishei* (*Bava Basra* 74b). And even if we force the argument that it is like a miracle (*Chullin* 43a), it is stated there (*Bava Basra* 74b) that *samtrei* (herbs) are effective, and likewise in *Yevamos* (114b)—and see *Tosafos Yevamos* (120b). There is also slight proof from *Bava Metzia* (107b, 113b), and also from *Pesachim* (56a), according to the version of the Babylonian Talmud and Rashi’s commentary (as opposed to the Rambam’s commentary in *Moreh Nevuchim*), one can infer this. In *Chullin* (54, 57), it must be said that it is not a complete cure, as *Tosafos* distinguishes in *Bechoros* (38b), which you, your honor, cited (and regarding the version of the Rashbam (*Bava Basra* 74b), who reads *samtrei* in *Chullin* instead of *sami*, it requires study). One can also say this regarding *Tosafos Gittin* (69b).

Regarding what you, your honor, cited from the Yerushalmi and Sifri, I could not reconcile it with our Talmud in *Yevamos* 76a, which reads the opposite (and see Rashi, *Chullin* 48a). In *Nimukei Yosef*, I found the version in the Yerushalmi that it *does* return, and *Perek Daled* of *Even HaEzer* (and the *Korban Eida*’s commentary on the Yerushalmi is puzzling). It requires study.

In my previous letter, I asked you if there is a source for what is written in letters, "B"H" or "BeEzras Hashem," and there is some proof to the contrary in *Rosh Hashanah* (18b), and in Rashi there, "with difficulty they were able to abolish, etc." Also in *Sanhedrin* (11b), it is implied as such. One cannot bring proof from *Sanhedrin* (96a) and *Chullin* (95b), as is understood. In all versions of legal documents, this is not found. It should also be noted from *Yevamos* (96b), "Elazar teaches anonymously and everyone knows, etc.," and more. It is surprising that you, your honor, did not answer me at all regarding this.

All this seems correct to my humble opinion, and my hope—after requesting your forgiveness—is that you will inform me of your opinion, the opinion of Torah, regarding the law in all of this.

I am the one waiting with longing for your response, and I honor you according to the greatness and height of your stature.

After writing this, it occurred to me while passing through the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Rambam that he rules there that one is only liable for lashes from the Torah for a *derusah*, and not for the accepted *treifos*. I could not examine it properly, as I only saw it in passing.

The address:
(The address in Russian)

The letter was delayed, and they told me here that you, your honor, moved your residence to Dvinsk. Although I do not know your address exactly, the letter will surely be delivered to you as I have written.

## 7760

7760

Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5689

Riga.

To my dear friend, the distinguished and exalted, wise and understanding, G-d-fearing and zealous for His word, the eminent and renowned Rabbi, R' Y. [may he live and be well],

Blessings and abundant peace!

As we approach the coming year, I wish to express my blessings that you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year—a year of happiness and honor, a year of life, peace, and abundant success in all your endeavors. May Hashem grant that the coming days bring with them an abundance of goodness and kindness, and may we all, together with all of Klal Yisrael, merit the true and complete Geulah.

With the blessings of one who wishes you well and is your friend who esteems you,

**Menachem Schneerson**

7660*

B"H, 16th of Iyar, 5690
Berlin.

To my esteemed friend, the distinguished avreich, Mr. Chadakov, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the maamar of Chassidus, "Anochi, etc.," which I promised to send you. Please fulfill your promise as well and return it to me as soon as possible.

I remember what we discussed regarding a maamar on the subject of Shabbos, and if I find a free moment, I will attempt to do as discussed. However, I do not know if the opportunity will arise, as the burdens are many, etc.

I remain your friend, who respects you and wishes you well,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7660\****

A facsimile of the original handwriting of the two letters before us was printed in *Di Yiddishe Heim*, issue 115 (Av-Elul 5753). They are addressed to Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Avraham Chadakov, who years later was appointed to be his personal secretary, and who remained by his side for nearly fifty years.

**Enclosed is the maamar of Chassidus, "Anochi, etc.":** This was said on Parshas Yisro 5690 in Chicago, and is printed in *Sefer HaMaamarim 5707*, p. 208.

Regarding this maamar, the Rebbe Rayatz writes in his diary (*Yemei Melech*, Vol. 1, p. 328): "30 Adar, Rosh Chodesh Adar. A letter to my son-in-law, R' Menachem Mendel, may he live, a long one, accompanied by the maamar 'Anochi Hashem Elokecha' which was said on Parshas Yisro."

## 7760

B"H, 22 Elul, 5690
Berlin

To my dear friend, the distinguished and excellent avreich, Mr. M. Chadakov, may he live.

Greetings and peace!

I received your letter regarding the calendar. I inquired about it today, and as it turns out, they do not have it currently, because there is little demand for a calendar from Russia of that type. They suggested ordering it from Russia, but that is a matter that would take an eternity, and therefore I did not agree to it.

They gave me an address in Warsaw where it **might** be available for purchase. Perhaps you could try that.

However, I will repeat once again what I told you last year: You will **certainly** find calendars in the university library in Riga, in the astronomical yearbook, and similar sources, by the dozens. In them, you will find everything necessary to calculate the sunset calendar for the horizons of Moscow, L.N. [Leningrad], and so on. For example, the *Berliner Astronomisches Jahrbuch* for the years 1930–1931 has already been published, and based on it, you will be able to calculate the sunset calendar easily, within a day or two. I spared your money—the price of each is a mark—and did not buy it, because they will surely lend it to you for a few days, and afterward, you will no longer need it.

In a few days, I will come to Riga, but I am rushing this letter in case the matter is urgent.

I will conclude with a blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* and all the best.

Your friend, who seeks your welfare and honors you,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**7760**

See the note to the previous letter.

**Calendar from Russia:** In order to print, based on it, the times for lighting candles on Erev Shabbos for the towns of Russia.

**L.N.:** Leningrad.

## 7761

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5696

To my esteemed and distinguished friend, the Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing man,
Rabbi Eliyahu, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to the telegram regarding our friend R' M.D. Friedman, may he live: enclosed herewith is a letter from the Rebbe shlita.

As I write to you, I do not know you personally, but from what I have heard of your praise—that you are one of the veteran *talmidei hatmimim*, among the most distinguished, and that you are connected to the Rebbe shlita and it is precious and dear to you to provide *nachas ruach* to the Rebbe shlita—I am writing to you that the Rebbe shlita is very interested in acquiring books for his library. Therefore, *anash* shlita should send him books. That is to say, one should endeavor to have the Rabbis who are authors send their books as a gift to the library of the Rebbe shlita.

It will cause great *nachas ruach* to the Rebbe when he acquires old books that were printed in America, regardless of the content—whether they are *Chumashim*, *Siddurim*, *Haggados*, *Selichos*, *Kinos*, *Machzorim*, and the like, or books of *Halacha*, *Chiddush*, and *Drush*. Even an old calendar, or a *Seder Hoshanos*, or a *Sefiras HaOmer* booklet would be considered a good thing.

It would be appropriate for you to inquire and investigate regarding booksellers located in New York and obtain their addresses and catalogs, and send them to the director of the library of the Rebbe shlita, Mr. H. Lieberman, so that he may determine what is missing from the library, and then they will endeavor to acquire them.

With appropriate respect,

The Secretary / M.S.

#### ***7761***

From a photocopy of the letter.

2Rabbi Eliyahu: Simpson.

Regarding... Friedman: See also Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 4, letter 814.

## 7762

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5700
Paris.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, wise and understanding man of fine character, etc., etc.,
Rabbi D.B. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hope that in the time since your last letter to me, you have already settled into your livelihood, and I would be pleased if you would inform me about this explicitly. Likewise, [please let me know] if your family members, may they live, are already with you in peace.

It causes me distress that there is a lack of detail in the letters to us regarding the health of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita. I am therefore turning to you with a great request to write to me regarding this in detail, [describing] the situation as it truly is. My confidence is strong that you will not turn my request away empty-handed, so I will not elaborate further on this.

My warm thanks are extended to you in advance.

Surely you are making notes of the sichos of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, now in your camp. Perhaps there is a possibility to send a copy of them to me here? Likewise, a record of what he said regarding the blessing of *HaGomel* at the time of the meeting at the port? And the account of the days of the *chag ha-pesach*?

I will conclude with wishes for all the best, and I remain awaiting your letter in response to all of the above, and I thank you in advance for this.

**M. Schneerson**

***

## 7764

*[Spring 5702]*

**Introduction**

It has been a custom from ancient times that at certain intervals—particularly at the beginning and end of a "zman"—the students of the yeshiva gather, joined by former students, or their acquaintances and friends from other yeshivos. They invite one of the mashpi'im, a rosh yeshiva, or another suitable individual to speak before them on matters pertaining to the tractate they are currently studying—whether through the lens of logic and pilpul, or through remez and drush, or regarding the avodah of Hashem, based on foundations drawn from seforim and the words of our sages.

Naturally, not all such gatherings and discussions are alike. The content is delivered at greater or lesser length, with more depth or more expansive explanation, depending on the general level of understanding of those gathered, and specifically on what they are accustomed to—whether pilpul, logic, remez, drush, or the like.

As we now come to publish some of these sichos, at the request of many students, we have chosen the following sicha as a starting point, for several reasons:

1) It concerns the beginning of Maseches Bava Metzia, as this tractate is being studied in many yeshivos during this "zman."

2) It is a sicha whose subject is the explanation of an entire sugya and the method of applying it to the life of the soul. This approach is still new to most students, even though it is an ancient, established way of interpreting matters of Torah within the life of the soul—a concept that permeates the Midrashim of our Sages and the works of the great leaders of Israel. See also the Yad Hachazakah, Hilchos Teshuvah, chapter 3, halachah 4, and the end of Hilchos Mikvaos.

3) It is a sicha that, given the state of those gathered at the time, explains all its points in a manner understandable even to those who are beginners in this approach, and even to those encountering the concepts of the life of the soul and its matters for the first time.

Our prayer is that every student of the yeshivos will conduct a true accounting with himself regarding the dire state of Bnei Yisrael in general, and his own state in particular.

And according to what our Sages have said (Kiddushin 40b) and as codified in Hilchos Teshuvah (chapter 3, halachah 4), one should view the entire world as half-meritorious and half-guilty. If one commits a single sin, he tips the scale for himself and for the entire world toward guilt, causing destruction. If he performs a single mitzvah, he tips the scale for himself and for the entire world toward merit, bringing salvation and rescue to himself and to them.

May he begin to occupy himself, with the appropriate focus, in the study of the *Chovos HaLevavos* (Duties of the Heart). As is known, there are six mitzvos that are an obligation **for every person, at every time, and in every place**, and all of them are duties of the heart. They are: to believe in Him, not to believe in any other, to unify Him, to love Him, to fear Him, and not to stray after the thoughts of the heart and the sights of the eyes.

And may we merit very soon the fulfillment of the prophecy (Yechezkel 36): "I will take you from among the nations... and I will sprinkle pure water upon you... and I will give you a new heart... and I will place My spirit within you... and you shall be My people, and I will be your G-d."

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

The Publisher

## 7765

B"H, Thursday, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, Malchus shebiYesod, 5702
Newark, N.J.

To the Directors of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch,

Greetings and blessings,

It was with great pleasure that I read your letter dated the 23rd of Iyar, and the interest you showed in my comments regarding the *sichos* you publish. I was even more pleased that you enlightened me with your note regarding the matter of "Yaakov Avinu did not die." Since your words are very dear to me, I will note a few points here. It is not my intention to initiate a correspondence or to wait for a reply, but rather to offer these as a point of Torah study to be examined at your leisure.

1) You suggest that the *Chiddushei Aggados* (Maharsha) who says he did not die refers to the *neshamah*, and that seemingly the *Tosafos* do not say this. However, it is possible that the words of *Tosafos* reflect the initial assumption (*kas'd*) and not the conclusion after the difficulty is raised—i.e., "Was it for nothing that they eulogized him, etc.?"

At the beginning of his commentary, the *Chiddushei Aggados* brings the words of *Tosafos* and cites *Rashi* regarding the embalming (*chantu chantiya*), noting that it appeared to them that he had died, but he was actually alive. Regarding this, the *Chiddushei Aggados* says, "The matter is forced, etc., and I heard an explanation, etc.," and he proceeds to give his own interpretation. Thus, it is explicitly clear that the *Chiddushei Aggados* found the explanations of *Rashi* and *Tosafos* to be forced—for why should we multiply disputes between *Rashi* and *Tosafos* where their disagreement is not explicitly stated? It is for this reason that he writes the explanation he heard, and there is no need to force the idea that *Tosafos* wrote according to an initial assumption. In *drush*, it is not unusual to offer an interpretation that contradicts *Rashi* and *Tosafos*, as is brought in the *Tiferes Yisrael* (on *Nazir* 8:4), which states: "Since it is a matter of practical law (*l'nafka minah*), one is permitted to interpret." I see no difference between interpreting the *Mishnah* and interpreting the *Chumash*, as we are permitted to interpret the verses, just as we see in the many commentaries written since the days of the *Gemara*. One must only ensure that one does not decide a law in a way that contradicts the opinion of the masters of the *Gemara*. This is brought in many books, and we see it tangibly: verses and statements of *Chazal* are interpreted in various ways.

2) You write in your letter: "This will clarify the change of names in the verse (Yeshayahu 41:14), 'Fear not, worm of Yaakov, men of Yisrael,' based on the words of *Chazal* in *Bereishis Rabbah* (ch. 81), that *mei-tei* implies death." 
a) See the *Etz Yosef* there on the *Midrash*, which brings in the name of the *Yefeh Toar*: "Since it doubles 'worm of Yaakov, men of Yisrael,' it alludes to Yaakov himself." He means that it was a sign for his children that just as the worm did not consume him, so too the nations of the world would not consume Yisrael. 
b) If we accept the words of the holy *Alshich* literally, that there was death among Yisrael, then the words of the *Midrash Rabbah* there would be difficult: "Why did Yosef die before his brothers? ... Did I not say to him, 'Fear not, worm of Yaakov'?" If there was death among Yisrael, perhaps it was necessary to embalm him because of that. This requires further study.

3) You write that the words of *Chazal* regarding the interpretation of the holy *Alshich* require study (*tzarich iyun*) (see *Zohar Chadash* 50:3, *Rashi*, and *Bereishis Rabbah* 96). After all, the *Gemara* brings the verse, "And you, fear not, My servant Yaakov... and be not dismayed, Yisrael," implying that he was alive in both states—both as Yaakov and as Yisrael. This is how the *Baal Akeidah* understood it in *Parshas Vayechi*, Gate 32, where he writes: "For in any case, he should have said, 'Yisrael our father did not die,' etc." Also, the verse cited mentions him as "My servant Yaakov" and "Yisrael." Thus, the *sugya* we are discussing implies that Yisrael did not die either.

In the commentary *Be'er Mayim Chayim* on *Parshas Vayechi* (and similarly in the *Ohr HaChayim*), he brings that a "slumber" seized him, and it appeared as if he had died, but in truth, he ascended alive to *Gan Eden*. He also brings in the name of the *Yalkut* on the verse, "And the days of Yisrael drew near to die," that the *Ribono shel Olam* said to him, "By your life, you are hidden and you do not die, etc." (See also *Baal HaTurim* on *Bereishis* 50:5 on the verse "I shall die": "There are three in the *Masorah*... even though they said Yaakov did not die, since Moshe said 'I shall die,' he said it as well, etc.")

In truth, I am surprised that in your letter you did not mention at all the words of the *Baal Akeidah* in Gate 32, which contains a long discourse on this matter. The *Malbim* in *Parshas Vayechi* explains it in the same way.

Incidentally, I will note that I saw in the *Hagahos HaShas* printed in the Vilna *Shas* for *Maseches Taanis*, by the *Chochmas Manoach*, that his opinion is that Yaakov Avinu did not die immediately in Egypt, but rather in Eretz Yisrael, and this is the hint in "Behold, I die in my grave." See his words there.

[a] One cannot raise a difficulty from the *Etz Yosef* against the *Alshich*.
[b] It is impossible to embalm if there was no death in Yaakov, because the body is **one**.
One cannot raise a difficulty from the *Akeidah* against the *Alshich*.
And in the *Shas* he will explain that since the body remained alive (except that it lacked the vitality added when his name was called Yisrael), it is similar to his seed. This is simple.

I have written all this only as a general *pilpul*, and I do not request a reply to these words, as I have written them only as a sign that your words are dear to me.

Regarding your request to exert effort in disseminating the *sichos*, as you know, I am extremely busy. Nevertheless, I will not refrain from doing so and will act in this matter according to my ability, with the help of the *Hashem*—may He be exalted.

With great respect and appreciation,

Moshe Pinchas Katz

## 7766

7766

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5702

To our esteemed friends, the G-d-fearing, diligent activists, lovers of Torah and pursuers of charity, etc., the Chabad Ladies Auxiliary in the city of Newark, N.J.,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

We acknowledge with great thanks the receipt of your esteemed contribution of $10.00, which we received through our friend, the distinguished Torah scholar and Chassid, a man of many talents and accomplishments, Rabbi Moshe Pinchas Katz, may he live and be well.

It gives us great pleasure to see your good and warm interest in our important work, and we hope that you will continue to demonstrate your interest and assistance in this work, not only through your esteemed contribution, but also by distributing the "Shmuessen" that are published monthly by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, in order to bring a great spiritual influence into your city. May a blessing come upon you. Being familiar with your capable work in the field of Torah and Chinuch, we are firm in the hope that, with the help of Hashem, you will accomplish much by distributing the "Shmuessen" among the youth of your city.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7767

7767

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5702
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, wise and understanding, etc.,
The Tamim, R' Sh. [may he live],

Greetings and blessings!

Your two letters—from the 21st and 22nd of Tammuz—have duly arrived, along with the application of Smechov [may he live], the twelve dollars, and the list of the shul. Many thanks for all of this.

Surely you have received more applications in the meantime, as you requested, and you are doing everything in your power to distribute them. I am certain you will keep me updated from time to time regarding this.

Is the list of the shul for the purpose of sending the *Machaneh Yisrael* publication regarding Tehillim?

Please inform me, after settling the matter with our friend, etc., the esteemed R' M.L. [may he live], whether you will be able to print an article in the Chicago newspaper regarding the work of the *Mifleget Ha-Lochamim* or *Machaneh Yisrael* that was sent to you. Naturally, this should be **free of charge**, as it is possible to do such a thing from here by paying.

Enclosed, as I promised you, is the *Reshimah* from the 13th of Tammuz that came into my possession. It is **prior to editing**. Since this is the only copy I have, please hasten to copy it and return it to me **as soon as possible**. Give my regards to our friend, the esteemed R' M.L. [may he live]. It is surprising that he has not yet replied to the letter written to him quite some time ago.

With wishes for all the best and with the blessing of "Immediately to Redemption."

**M. Schneerson**

Regards from his son [may he live], whom I just saw now.

## 7768

7768

B”H, 10 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

To our esteemed and highly respected friend, a man of fine character and great accomplishments, a man of many virtues, active in many fields, etc.,
R’ Shlomo Palmer
Chicago

Peace and blessing!

Surely you have heard of the great spiritual work being conducted by **Machne Israel**, which was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and which has been spoken of at length and in brief in *HaKria VeHaKedusha*.

One of the matters of this holy work of Machne Israel is the founding of Tehillim groups in synagogues, and the strengthening of existing Tehillim groups. Foremost among all Tehillim groups is the global Tehillim society established in Jerusalem through the inspiration of the Rebbe, which carries song and prayer on behalf of all Tehillim groups throughout the world and their members.

Before we proceed with the campaign to disseminate this lofty idea and to stir the synagogues in Chicago to establish Tehillim groups—for which purpose we also intend to place an advertisement in your newspaper—it is necessary that our brethren, the children of Israel residing in Chicago, receive a general concept of the work of Machne Israel.

Therefore, I come with a great request to my friend, that he would kindly endeavor to have the article that appeared in the *Morgen Journal* (which I am enclosing herewith) appear also in the *Courier* as soon as possible.

Knowing his affection and dedication to everything holy to us, and on the other hand, his significant influence on the editorial staff of the *Courier*, I am full of hope that he will succeed, with the help of Hashem, in this endeavor, and he will be among those who bring merit to the many, and blessing will come upon him.

Time is pressing, as we intend to send the list of all the Tehillim groups to Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt speedily) before Hoshana Rabbah. I am certain he will act quickly in this, and our thanks are extended to him in advance.

I am his friend, who wishes him well and blesses him with a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

## 7744

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5703

To our esteemed friend, the distinguished avreich, G-d-fearing and scholarly,
Rabbi Menachem Zev Gringlas, may he live,
Montreal

Peace and blessing!

Due to the shortage of time, we are replying to your letters to "Machne Israel" and "Melach" together — from Motzaei Shabbos Haazinu and Erev Yom Kippur.

1) Regarding the shipment of *Kriah* and *Kedushah*: It is evident from those handling this that no packages were lost, and they have promised to send everything requested there as soon as possible.

2) We hereby acknowledge receipt of ten Canadian dollars from you, via R' Tz. P., may he live.

3) In accordance with the new regulations regarding the shipment of printed materials overseas, we are concerned that it may become difficult to ship such items to Canada as well. Therefore, our advice is that you immediately order all printed materials that we have published in the largest quantity that you find will be necessary for you over time.

4) Please inform us how many booklets of "Megillas 19 Kislev" to send you in Yiddish and how many in English.

5) We wish to inform you, as the primary representative of Machne Israel in Canada, that in the interest of peace, we wrote yesterday specifically to the Shochet R' Karakowski, may he live, in Montreal, and requested that he take an interest in the affairs of Machne Israel and discuss this with you.

However, we feel that for the benefit of the cause, it is best that all matters of Machne Israel be conducted under one administration. Therefore, please speak with the aforementioned and arrange the work in the best possible way, B'Ezras Hashem.

6) Regarding the shipment of *Shmuessen*, we have already written in our previous letter that it will be arranged, I"H.

7) We are surprised that even after our warning not to print in *Heichal* any material from the *Shmuessen* of that same month, you nevertheless printed in *Heichal* of Tishrei material from the *Shmuessen* of Tishrei.

Therefore, we are informing you again that you do not have permission to do such a thing, and we hope that you will be careful about this in the future.

8) We have published an "Aleph-Beis," its price is 10 cents, and we have sent you a sample.

With the blessing of a happy holiday, for immediate Teshuvah, for immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

The 5 copies of *Heichal* have just arrived, and thank you for them.

## 7757

B"H, 3rd day of Chanukah, 5705

To our dear friend, the outstanding avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc.,

Rabbi Menachem Zev Greenglass,
Montreal

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letters of the 13th and 16th of Kislev:

1) You have surely already received my reply letter via our friend, the Chossid, etc., R’ Y. Weinberg. Please assist him in whatever way you can regarding the editing of the reshimot and providing the necessary impetus.

2) The weight sent by her husband, "Pardes," was received and delivered according to instructions. The receipts for the Sefer Torah fund will reach us in the coming days.

3) The printing materials you requested were sent to you some time ago.

4) You have surely already received the *Reshimos* for Shemini Atzeres and the notices for Mr. Feller. Enclosed is a copy of the two letters to the *Talmudei Torah*. No response has been received from them as of yet.

5) Upon receiving the *Reshimos* for Shemini Atzeres back, I will send them the *Reshimos* for Simchas Torah and 10 Kislev, if they do not have them already.

6) Your request regarding the *Kuntres* has been submitted, and they will answer you in detail.

7) We read with great pleasure about your activities and the activities of all the *Temimim* regarding the matters of *Machne Yisrael* and *Mifleget L’Chaim*. But what can we do? The Rebbe Shlita demands from each and every one to increase in strength, each day more than the day before. He quoted the Rebbe Maharash n.e.: "If 'good' is good, is 'better' not better?" Surely you and your colleagues will conduct yourselves in this manner.

8) At the next opportunity, we will send the *Likutei Torah* and *Tanya* for Rabbi Hirshhorn, as requested.

9) When we write to the "Nesher" and the rabbis you mention in your letter, we will inform you. For several reasons, it is delayed for now.

10) You will surely inform us about the Yud-Tes Kislev celebration held by you.

[The conclusion is printed above in Vol. 1, letter 45.]

## 7758

B"H, 19 Shevat, 5705

To the honored and distinguished, G-d-fearing and Torah-observant, etc.,
Rabbi Reuven Feitelberg, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Our dear and distinguished friend, the Torah scholar and Chassid, Rabbi Moshe Leib Rotstein, may he live and be well, wrote to us that he met with you. He shared with us, to our great joy, that you are active in the field of chinuch and that you are seeking every possible means to educate your students, may they live and be well, in yiras shamayim. He also requested that we send you certain guidance regarding chinuch.

In connection with this, we would ask you to inform us of more details regarding your educational institution, such as the number of classes, the number of students in each class and their ages, what their level of knowledge is, how much time you are able to dedicate to learning with each class, and so on.

Based on the aforementioned information, it would be easier, b’ezras Hashem, to develop a curriculum for your educational institution.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

Surely you have received our sample benchers, and you will certainly see their benefit for children. The price is 15 cents. For a larger number of copies, 10 cents.

## 7779

B"H, 3 Adar I, 5705

Our dear friend, the G-d-fearing man of action, learned and wise, etc.,
The Tamim, R' Y.L.
HaLevi,
Dorchester

Shalom u’Bracha!

We acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your letters from 5 Shevat and 2 Yisro, along with a check for eight dollars and 84 cents, and one dollar for his account.

Due to circumstances beyond our control, we were delayed in sending the *luchos* [tablets/calendars] to your community.

We have sent the remaining items you requested, and they have surely reached you by now.

We thank you for your interest in distributing our booklets until now, and there is no doubt that in the future you will add strength, to be among those who are meritorious and bring merit to the many, even more than this.

An explanation of the great value of these matters is superfluous. It is known from our Sages — Kiddushin 40a — that "a merit produces fruit." This means that just as a small seed grows into a large tree that produces fruit, so too, by causing an acquaintance to perform an action that appears small **at first glance** — such as studying a *sicha* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, or telling his son a story about our Sages, and the like — it is possible that over time it will bring about good results that cannot be estimated in advance. And one *mitzvah* leads to another *mitzvah* until *Ein Sof*.

**M. Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7782

7782

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Parah, 5705

Our dear friend, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, wise and understanding, etc.,
The Temim, R' Yehuda Leib שי' Halevi

Shalom u'Bracha!

Following our conversations on several occasions regarding your efforts concerning the financial means for the printing of the Tanya.

You will surely inform us of the results of your efforts in this matter. It is unnecessary to elaborate on the great necessity of this matter and its lofty value, **and my hope is strong that you will do everything in your power regarding this,** and one brings about merit—

The refinement of the atmosphere of the world through the letters of Torah and Tefillah, the worm and the crimson thread of the Parah [Red Heifer] ritual, as explained in Likutei Torah, in the maamar beginning with the words "Zos Chukas" (Section 4).

And it can be said that in the study of Tanya, which is a collection of advice for the avodah of the heart, there are two aspects—through the meritorious (and one should note the distinction between Kohanim and Leviim, where the Leviim are the level of purity).

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**M. Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7783

B"H, Wednesday, 7th of Iyar, 5705

To the esteemed and distinguished, occupied in the work of Hashem, [Name], may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

We are sending you, in a separate envelope, the album that was published on the occasion of the "Misibos Shabbos" gathering (which took place this past Purim).

This booklet, with the help of Hashem, exerts a positive influence on the youth who read it, strengthens the observance of Shabbos in their personal lives, and inspires them to participate in the work of "Misibos Shabbos" as members or counselors.

We are confident that you will take this opportunity to strengthen the spirit of the youth who are under your influence, and that you will endeavor to distribute the aforementioned booklet among them. And since your influence also extends to a large circle of educators, you will surely act with your wisdom so that they, too, will follow your lead and distribute the booklet in their educational institutions.

The price of the booklet is 25 cents; for educational institutions purchasing a significant number, the price is 15 cents per booklet.

In continuation of the above, we would like to suggest that you attempt to organize "Misibos Shabbos" circles among the boys and girls in the schools under your influence; the great benefit of this requires no explanation.

And in accordance with the words of the Rebbe shlita to the counselors of the *misibos*, that one must strive for the day of Shabbos to be the source from which all days are blessed—as he explained his words—these were printed in the first report of the *misibos* and appear in the aforementioned album in an English translation.

Hoping to receive good news from you regarding all of the above, and with blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7784

B"H, Thursday, 19th of Tammuz, 5705

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Haulin, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Nissan of this year, we would like to point out that since the income from the sale of printed materials is necessary for us to print other materials, it is impossible for us to distribute them for free. Only in consideration of the fact that our representatives must, for the purpose of outreach and the like, distribute at least a portion of the booklets sent to them for free, and that there are other expenses involved in this, are we prepared to agree to grant them a discount of twenty percent (20%) off the fixed price. If you see a need to distribute more for free, it is necessary to find donors on the spot who will provide set sums for the purpose of the aforementioned distribution; however, we, for our part, cannot waive more than the 20% mentioned above.

Undoubtedly, as in the past, you will surely exert yourself to the best of your ability, as a lack of income from sales hinders the printing of several items.

We are prepared to send from the holy publications, etc., according to the number you will indicate in response to this letter of ours, and according to the aforementioned conditions. Please be so kind as to confirm receipt of the packages each time, indicating the number of copies of each. The *Hayom Yom* compilation has surely arrived.

I inquired regarding the *Kuntres U'Maayan* (as I heard it said that it was printed in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt, before the First World War), and I wished to clarify this, and whether it is possible and easy to obtain a copy from that edition.

We are currently publishing the first *Tzava'ah* (Will) of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the *Kuntres U'Maayan* with additions from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. We are preparing for print: the *sicha* of the festival of this year, and the *reshimos* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, regarding the life of the Alter Rebbe—details hitherto unknown.

With blessings for *l'altar l'teshuva l'altar l'geula* (immediate repentance, immediate redemption).

Perhaps it would be worthwhile to establish a special committee in your camp for the sale and distribution of printed materials.

***

## 7785

B"H, Friday, 20th of Tammuz, 5705

To the honorable Rabbi and distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and esteemed, etc., etc., Rabbi A. Karasik, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

We are surprised that you have not confirmed receipt of the printing materials we sent you several times, nor have you informed us of anything regarding the settlement of their cost during all this time. We would appreciate it if you could clarify the matter.

In general, the withholding of income from the books that have already been printed hinders our ability to publish the *kuntreisim* and books that are ready for print.

It would be appropriate for there to be a special committee in Tel Aviv that would take upon itself the sale and distribution of the publications sent from here (the *Kovetz*, *kuntreisim*, *sichos*, *shmuessen*, etc.). If they find it necessary to distribute a certain number of them for free, we are willing to deduct twenty percent from the set price (with shipping costs also on our account). If this is not sufficient, a source for this must be found locally in your camp.

Please do your utmost to settle the account for the books you have already received, and there is no doubt that you will do so in the future. The payment should be delivered to Yeshivas Toras Emes.

Please inform us how many of each type we should send from here on out.

We are sending you samples of textbooks for the Holy Tongue for schools. It would be worthwhile to inform the Charedi schools in Tel Aviv and its surroundings about this, as they surely feel a great need for such books. The price of the first volume is 60 cents, and the price of the fifth volume (for those who have already studied for 6–7 years) is one dollar. When they order a large quantity, we are prepared to offer them quite good discounts. The other volumes are also almost ready for print.

I would be grateful if you could inform me of the details regarding the printing of the Tanya—whether it is a photographic reproduction, newly typeset, or something similar.

I also request that you send here 1–2 copies of everything published by you—whether by copier or in print.

In the future, it would be appropriate to consult with us regarding such matters beforehand. For example: the Rebbe, my father-in-law, may he live, is currently entrusting us with the *kuntres* "U’Maayan" to be printed with the addition of an introduction, explanations, etc., and I have heard that in your camp, you have already issued it via copier!

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

I have also written regarding the distribution of our publications to the G-d-fearing and esteemed, etc., Rabbi M. Gurary, may he live.

It is possible that a Tanya with *marei mekomos* and the like will be published here. Perhaps you or your acquaintances have stories, traditions, notes on the text, etc., regarding the Tanya; please inform me. Thank you in advance.

## 7787

B"H, 5th of Kislev, 5704

To the distinguished avreich, G-d-fearing and wise, etc.,
Rabbi, the temim, our teacher Rabbi Y.T. shlita,
Buffalo

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the 20th of last month:

1) Regarding the question of the language of instruction: As you describe the situation, our advice is that the children should temporarily learn everything in English. At the same time, you should strive that over time they also learn Yiddish, and then they will be able to transition to Yiddish as the language of instruction as well.

According to your judgment, you can accustom the students to Yiddish either by having the review of the lessons conducted in Yiddish (which will also make the review more interesting, even for those students who already remember well what they learned the first time), or by setting aside a specific time to study the Yiddish language (it is possible to do both simultaneously).

2) This week, G-d willing, the curriculum will appear from the press, which also includes the order of study for the subjects.

3) Regarding a book for studying grammar on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*: If you intend for the students to use it, such a book is almost non-existent here at the moment. If you want it for yourself, let us know and we can search for a book from which you could study, at the very least in a time of need.

4) We have given instructions to send you everything you requested regarding printing matters, as well as the *simanim* for the Shabbos *mesibos*.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

## 7793

7793

*[5704]*

B"H

To our dear friends, the Temimim and Anash in the city of Tel Aviv,

Shalom u’vracha!

It has been three years since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, established the Kehot Publication Society, the purpose of which is to engage in the publishing of various books and booklets, such as sefarim on Nigleh, Chassidus, matters of strengthening Yiddishkeit, as well as educational books and reading material of a pure and holy nature.

Through Kehot, the following series are published: "Otzar HaChassidim - Lubavitch," "Machne Israel," and the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch."

Surely you are aware of those sefarim and booklets that, with the help of Hashem, have already been published by Kehot, and it is impossible to estimate the immense benefit that these printing efforts have brought to the strengthening of Torah and Yiddishkeit.

However, just as the obligation here is to endeavor to publish the sefarim with the greatest possible hiddur, so too is there a holy obligation upon all the Temimim and Anash, shiyichyu, who observe the holy instructions of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, in all that he commands, to endeavor in all their places of residence to distribute these sefarim. This distribution means: a) to enable more and more people to merit studying and reading these sefarim, and b) to increase financial revenue, thereby facilitating the possibility of publishing further sefarim.

And although each and every one of Anash is obligated to do this individually according to his ability, the greatest success in distribution is possible only through organized work in every city and district.

Therefore, we are turning to you with the proposal to gather together to discuss this matter and to organize a special committee that will endeavor to distribute the aforementioned sefarim in Tel Aviv and its surroundings in the best possible order, in such a way that the sefarim will not fail to reach even one person who has any possibility of being influenced to read the sefarim appropriate for him, each according to his level.

We are confident that you, like us, recognize the necessity of this matter, and that you will soon inform us of its implementation from potential into action.

The details of shipping from here are known to our dear friend, the Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing man, etc., Moreinu HaRav Aharon, shiyichyu, Karasik.

May Hashem grant us all the merit to be among those who participate in spreading the wellsprings outward, and to see through this the complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

## 7795

B"H, 5 Teves, 5705
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter, along with the checks from Mr. P. Rottenberg, has been received. Many thanks for your efforts in this matter.

It is my strong hope that from now on, you, as well as your esteemed brothers (may they live and be well), will take an interest in the work of **Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch** in all its details, and will provide us with your assistance in every way possible and within your means.

For this work is multifaceted, and there is no doubt that several of its branches will be of particular interest to you, and you will be able to participate in them yourselves, as well as through your influence on others.

In the parsha of the week, regarding the verse (*Bereishis* 46:28), "And he sent Yehudah before him," Rashi explains: "to establish a house of study for him." For before Yaakov arrived in Mitzrayim—a new place—he had already prepared a beis medrash there, and concerned himself with the chinuch of his sons and daughters.

Just as this applies to place, so too does it apply to time: anyone who desires that there be a "generation of the upright who are blessed" among the sons and daughters of Yisrael in the future must strive to make all the necessary preparations in good time. This is the essence of chinuch—guiding young boys and girls from their earliest years in the good and upright path.

The role of "Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch," and the goal set for it by my father-in-law, the Rebbe (shlita), when he founded the "Merkaz" and placed the burden of managing the executive committee upon my shoulders, is to strive to ensure that this guidance is conducted in accordance with the purity of holiness and without partisan division. For the Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch takes an interest in all circles of the Jewish people—Chassidim, those who are not, those of Hungarian descent, those of Polish descent, and so on. Anyone who participates in this work is among the founders and builders of the younger generation, who will be a source of pride and glory for our people, the children of Yisrael.

Hoping to hear from you regarding practical matters frequently, and with blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

#### ***7795***

Published in the booklet *Tzadik L’Melech* I, p. 46, and completed according to a copy.

## 7797

B"H, 22 Adar, 5705

To the honorable Rabbi, renowned for his praise, Moreinu HaRav Sh. Sheinfield, London

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter dated January 8th reached me, and I was pleased to hear of your fruitful work in strengthening the faith among Jewish soldiers. Rabbi Heschel, who recently arrived here from London, also spoke at length in praise of your honor as the driving spirit behind this lofty work.

"Machne Israel," which was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita of Lubavitch, is dedicated to strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit, and naturally, we are prepared to assist your honor in every way possible.

As a practical matter, I would suggest that your honor get in touch with Rabbi Benjaminson in London. He has several copies of everything we have published in print, and based on them, you will be able to estimate the details of the weight and size of the books and booklets necessary for submitting the application for a license.

On our part, we are prepared to send you our books and booklets at a special discount of one-third of the price. If you are able to obtain the license on the spot, that would be excellent; however, should we need to send them at our own expense, we are also prepared to cover half of the shipping costs. In our opinion, it would suffice for the first time to send 20 to 25 copies as samples, and if there is a need, we will send more, G-d willing.

Regarding the transformer for the check-writing machine, we inquired at the central office in New York, and they informed us that only a few are available for sale, as they have not been manufacturing them for some time due to the war; it is only possible to obtain two or three at $2.75 each.

With blessings for success in your work, and for a kosher and happy holiday, for immediate teshuvah, for immediate geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem M. Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7800

7800

*[5702-5705]*

In response to your letter in which you tell me about one of your acquaintances who is in the vicinity of Eretz Yisrael, and who travels on Shabbos to a city where other Jews are located, in order to eat—at the very least on Shabbos Kodesh—kosher meat and to spend a few hours in the company of our fellow Jews.

You ask whether your acquaintance is doing the right thing by desecrating Shabbos in order to eat kosher food and to strengthen his connection to a Jewish environment.

The rule stated by our Sages of blessed memory—who plumbed the depths of every person’s soul, even though no two people are alike—is: "Do not sit and weigh the mitzvos of the Torah." They also said, "Be as careful with a minor mitzvah as with a major one," even when discussing mitzvos where one is considered minor and the other major.

This is especially true in the case of your acquaintance, where both matters carry great weight.

For it is known that regarding forbidden foods, aside from the severity of the punishment in the future, they possess a quality even now—though it is not something that can be grasped by the intellect in every instance—that dulls the heart and mind of the person who eats them. This continues until the matters of Torah and mitzvos become "distant and foreign" to him; he becomes increasingly coarse and materialistic, to the point where he may be drawn, due to the traits that forbidden foods have implanted in his body, toward forbidden matters to which he was never previously inclined, and which are despicable in his eyes even from the perspective of basic humanity and moral ethics.

As for the immense value of the holiness of Shabbos, it is superfluous to elaborate on what is explicitly stated in the Tanach and the words of our Sages: that it is a sign between Hashem and us, and its observance is a declaration and proclamation that Hashem created the world and all that fills it, and that He sustains and leads it at every moment and every second, even now. This is why our Sages said that one who desecrates Shabbos and an idolater are considered equal in weight to all the other mitzvos of the Torah.

The conduct of your acquaintance is comparable to someone whose house has caught fire, Heaven forbid, to the point where his life is in danger, and he "extinguishes" the fire by pouring naphtha and petroleum upon it!

You must open your acquaintance’s eyes and make him aware of his own personal situation, and the situation of the entire Jewish people—for all of Israel are responsible for one another—in general.

The situation of our fellow Jews across the sea is terrible, and may Hashem in His great mercy say "enough" to their troubles, and may He not allow the evil to spread, Heaven forbid.

However, we must know our obligation to Hashem, our obligation to ourselves, to our families, and to all our fellow Jews: to stand firm in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, and to overcome every obstacle and hindrance to their observance.

And even if it seems to your acquaintance that the observance of this or that mitzvah is impossible in his current situation, if he were to contemplate this like a person delving into a matter that concerns his very life, he would certainly find a way and a method to fulfill the mitzvah and to guard the purity of his body and soul throughout all seven days of the week, and not by establishing a routine of desecrating Shabbos every single Shabbos.

And one mitzvah leads to another, to be connected to oneself, to one's religion, and to one's Torah; the Torah is holy, and Israel is holy.

## 7803

7803

B”H, Rosh Hashanah La’Ilanos, 5706

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, energetic activist, man of many accomplishments, etc., Moreinu Harav A. Abramson, may he live, London.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a great pleasure for us to hear news of you, and of your great interest in all the affairs of the Rebbe, shlita, and especially in the affairs of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch, which is one of the primary enterprises of the Rebbe, shlita. I wish to thank you for your important participation in the work of plowing and planting to establish a branch of our office in London during the visit of our esteemed friend, the G-d-fearing, G-d-conscious Mr. Nissan Mindel, may he live. As our friend R’ N.M. reported to us, you were one of the pillars of this endeavor.

We are now awaiting good fruits. Indeed, the time has arrived for the work to be put into actual practice, now that we have already sent a fair number of books and booklets of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch to various addresses in England.

Since we did not wish to burden you with technical work—especially knowing that you are a busy man—we placed the task of organizing the office and all the work involved upon our friend Mr. Avraham Kagan, may he live, who volunteered to handle this as much as possible. He also offered one of his rooms to serve as an office for the time being, until the matter is arranged in the best possible way. However, it was not our intention that this work be done without compensation, but Mr. Avraham insisted on this. In any case, we have authorized him to hire an assistant to write the letters, prepare book lists, wrap packages, etc., as is necessary for the distribution of our publications outside of London. If you wish to organize the distribution in London, as you originally intended through one of your trusted associates, you will surely endeavor to do so in the best possible way. If you find it necessary to place this work upon Mr. Avraham, he will surely be of assistance to you as much as possible. And since "one does not urge except those who are already eager," you will surely see to it to awaken and encourage Mr. Avraham, and together with our friend the Rabbi, the Chassid, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. Benjaminson, may he live, you will be of help and assistance to him as much as possible, serving as the living spirit and the driving force of the entire enterprise.

Establishing an office in London is a fundamental matter. It is worthwhile to consult with a lawyer on how to organize the matter officially. If it is not yet possible to organize it officially, it must be organized in any case. Because of the great importance of the matter, we have taken upon ourselves the responsibility for the office’s expenses, but surely Anash in England will endeavor to fulfill their commitment to bear the office expenses, in accordance with their decision at the meeting of Anash in Manchester on 26 Tishrei of this year.

To conclude with a topic of the day: Our Sages have said (Sifri Bamidbar 36) that the days of Moshiach, and especially the time of the Resurrection of the Dead, are the ultimate purpose and perfection of the creation of this world, for which it was created from the outset. This is also necessitated by the plain meaning of Scripture, which recounts that the laws of nature have changed for the worse from how they were created, due to the curse that came in the wake of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. It is understood that in order for them to return to their perfection—as they were when they were created, and as it is written, "And they were finished and perfected"—the curse must be removed; that is, through the atonement for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. This is what will happen in the days of Moshiach, when the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the land."

(Note: See Moreh Nevuchim, Part 1, Chapter 2, and at the end of Hilchos Melachim: "The entire world will be occupied only with knowing Hashem.")

Bringing about the days of Moshiach and meriting them is achieved through our current avodah, the essence of which is to cause the Shechinah to dwell in this world. This means that the world will be in the state it was in before the sin, when the Shechinah was in the lower realms, and in the future to come, it will be even more so. As our Sages said (Bereishis Rabbah 19:7), the primary dwelling of the Shechinah was in the lower realms; once Adam HaRishon sinned, it departed, etc., and the Tzaddikim cause it to dwell on earth. We learn this from the verse, "The Tzaddikim shall inherit the land and dwell [therein] forever," which refers primarily to the future to come.

Now, one of the changes caused by the curse of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge is that, initially, all trees bore fruit (Bereishis Rabbah, end of Chapter 5). As mentioned above, in the future to come, it must be that even barren trees will bear fruit, as our Sages said explicitly (Toras Kohanim, beginning of Bechukosai; cf. the end of Kesuvos).

This concept applies to a person’s avodah to his Creator. The verse states, "For man is the tree of the field," and our Sages explain the matter of fruits—in a Jewish person—as "What are the fruits? Mitzvos" (Sotah 46a). The creation was such that all created beings would fulfill their purpose according to the will and command of the Creator; every tree would bear fruit. It was only through the sin—which, within the soul, is the state of a tree that does not produce fruit—that this occurred in the physical realm as well.

The avodah now, as mentioned, is to bring the **entire** world to its perfection as it was before the sin. This means the effort, in particular, that **one’s entire environment** should produce fruits—the fruits of Mitzvos. Then we will all merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And the tree of the field shall give its fruit," and "I will lead you upright," both spiritually and physically.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7809

7809

B"H, Sunday, 13 Sivan, 5707
Paris

To the esteemed Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Nissan, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

Thank you for confirming receipt of one package of Chassidic discourses and two packages of Siddurim (in addition to what was sent by R' B. Gorodetzky, may he live). Although I find it strange, as we sent them much more during that time, addressed directly to their camp or to the names of the soldiers and in Prague.

Regarding your writing that you sent several letters to the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch—as of now, not a single letter from them has been received.

Concerning the shipment of books in the future: Upon my arrival in the United States, I will endeavor to arrange this as best as possible. However, one of the main points is missing from your letter, as you do not specify how the shipment should be handled or to which address, so that it may be received in its entirety, with the lowest possible expenses, and as quickly as possible.

I intend to travel, G-d willing, to New York at the end of this week or the middle of next week. Naturally, I desire to clarify and arrange the matters entrusted to my portion of the work, to the extent that it depends on me, even before my departure. One of these matters is the subject of *ha'maamad* (though, naturally, my participation in this is in a manner that is not known publicly, for *shatnez l'genez*).

Although I have inquired and sought to understand what is being done regarding this in your camp and in the camps of *Anash* over whom you have influence, I do not know anything clearly: whether there are individuals or a committee dealing with this consistently, whether it is done by way of a monthly *maamad*, whether they are aware that the situation is strained, etc., etc.

I said here at a *farbrengen* with *Anash* and the *temimim* that *hiskashrus* must be with all possible strengths. First and foremost, for Chabad Chassidim, the name implies that one must be connected through *Chabad*—that is, simply put, to study the *maamarim* of the Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation. Since the intent of the one who says the *maamarim* is the drawing down of *Chochma, Binah,* and *Da'as* into the *midos* and the transformation of the *midos* through them, this necessitates *hiskashrus* by way of walking in his paths and following his instructions in the *midos* and the service of the heart.

But all this pertains to the *koach* or specific *kochot*, and at the very least to the revealed *kochot*. If so, since there still remains a doubt as to which path one is leading him, this casts doubt on which place he is connected to in his inwardness and essence.

The advice for this is only through the matter of *ha'maamad*, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 32, 37, *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 4, and elsewhere.

The above applies even in normal times. How much more so, *kal v'chomer*, in these times, when *hiskashrus* through *Chabad, Chagas, Nehiyim* has suffered due to the hardships of the times, the distance of location, and the cessation of connection—even by letter—for many long years. Therefore, the *hiskashrus* through *ha'maamad* must be with greater intensity and strength.

I have been brief in the above, confident that this brevity will suffice, and primarily in the hope that you are not in need of a reminder in this matter, nor even regarding preference and alacrity; for "his alacrity is what stands forever," etc.

I will conclude with regards to all those who seek your welfare, and with wishes for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**

It is likely that the bearer of this letter will telephone here in these coming days, and perhaps it will be possible to convey through him the information regarding the above, in an appropriate manner.

And great is peace, for the entire Torah was given to create peace in the world (Sifrei, cited in Rambam, end of Hilchos Chanukah; see also Likutei Torah by the Mitteler Rebbe, end of Parshas Noach).

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7414

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5707

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav M. Lipsker, shlita

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of the 5th of Menachem Av has been received.

a) Enclosed are two letters for Arani and Boasi. Together with them, you will receive from the packages five copies of *Tehillas Hashem*, three copies of our *Sefer* (Volume 1 and Volume 2), and *Unzer Buch* (Volume 1 and Volume 2). Please be so kind as to give each of the children I examined one book as a gift, as I wrote in my letter (regarding the other books, I have already written to Harav Shneur Zalman, shlita, Butman). Surely the administration of Arani and Boasi will confirm their receipt.

b) My relative, Harav Shneur Zalman, shlita, told me that he already sent them a telegram last week.

c) It is a pity that there is no urgency regarding the matter of the *maamad*. The trouble is that, intellectually, everyone has a reason for this as well.

One could say regarding the *parsha* of the week, which begins, "And it will be, because (*eikev*) you will listen to these ordinances" (*Devarim* 7:12)—noting specifically "ordinances" (*mishpatim*) (see Ramban on the Torah)—that this is based on what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, said regarding the virtue of the *eikev* (heel), that this is the concept of *kabbalas ol* (as explained in the *maamar* "Ein Hakadosh Baruch Hu Ba B'trunya" in *Sefer HaMaamarim* and elsewhere). It teaches us that even regarding *mishpatim*—rational *mitzvos*—were it not for the matter of *kabbalas ol*, who knows if, in the final analysis, one would listen to them.

With the blessing of "Immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 7815

28 Menachem Av, 5707

To the Committee of the Beis Rivkah Schools and for Printing Needs
in Europe, by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter:

1) I informed the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, regarding the content of your letter. It is a great wonder that not all those appointed have signed, considering that you have undertaken the holy task entrusted to you by the Rebbe, shlita.

2) Naturally, the main thing here is the "zerizin" (the swift) of actual action, and we await good news.

3) Since at this moment there is no prospect of continuing our support from here—in addition to what I have already promised Rabbi B.G. regarding the past—you must make every effort to collect the entire budget locally: from tuition, private donations, and special collections (including in the shuls) during Elul-Tishrei, through proper preparation.

4) Regarding your proposal concerning the Joint, I will clarify the opinion of the Rebbe, shlita.

5) The most appropriate way to gather the expenses for publishing and printing is to obtain them from individual donors who will give a respectable sum for the printing of a specific sefer in memory of a soul, etc., or also for the merit of the living. This is as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, did with the Toras Shmuel seforim that are in your possession (and as written in the Responsa of the Rashba, that the Torah publicizes those who perform a mitzvah, etc., cited in Magen Avraham, siman 194, at the end).

I await good news from you and wish you the best.

## 7718

B"H, Chag HaGeulah, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and Torah-observant individual, involved in communal needs, etc., the distinguished Chossid, R' Sh. M. (may he live and be well),

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter (which I have enclosed).

1) Please be so kind as to urge R' D. (may he live and be well) Browman to expedite the printing, and to make an effort that, finally, some of the printed copies should **also arrive here.**

2) Regarding the title page for *Shaarei Orah*—if it has not yet been found, he should use the one from *Ateres Rosh* or from *Shaar HaEmunah*.

3) Surely the aforementioned has already received all the instructions regarding the printing of the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe that I transmitted through R' B. (may he live and be well) Gorodetsky.

4) He should proceed with the printing of *Torah Or* and *Likutei Torah* (and he should use the proofread edition of *Likutei Torah*).

I will send instructions regarding the title page and introductions in some time.

5) Regarding the girls' school: I see no valid reason for changing the name "Beis Sarah" or changing the administration. Rather, anyone who recognizes the necessity of such a school and has the ability to assist—it is a **mitzvah obligation** upon him to come and assist. All the more so, no one has the right, due to petty factionalism, to actively destroy a good institution that others have built, or to invest energy and money into a parallel institution where there is no need for one.

6) Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was just brought from the *Beis Din*; please confirm its receipt. Surely you will merit the public through it.

Please be so kind as to forward the enclosed letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (may his merit shield us), to Pocking **as soon as possible.**

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah and with regards to all those who seek your welfare,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

***

## 7,819

7,819

B"H, Chag HaGeulah, 5708

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, etc., R' M. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

I heard some time ago about your successful arrival, and likewise regarding the arrival of your brother-in-law at the time.

And now I am writing regarding the following:

1) Please be kind enough to inform me in a letter, on a separate sheet, and with reference to the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch (MLC), what sums and how much of the funds belonging to the Kehot Publication Society and the camp were included in the total sum that was given to R' Ch. L. while he was here. This is certainly a great burden, but I see no other way to clarify this entire matter.

2) At the end of the copy of the writings of the Mitteler Rebbe that you sent to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, there is one responsum, and it appears that other responsa follow it. Perhaps it is possible to clarify their nature, their content, and who authored them.

3) If you have already decided regarding your participation in the printing costs of the *Kitzurei Shaarei Orah* belonging to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, please be kind enough to inform me as soon as possible, and also inform me of the dedication text that should be printed in the aforementioned book (in accordance with the words of our Sages, "It is a mitzvah to publicize those who perform a mitzvah").

Your brother-in-law told me before he left here that you would participate.

4) I am writing to remind you regarding your promise to exert yourself immediately upon your arrival regarding the settlement of the funds belonging to *Atah Hareisa* from Anash in Tel Aviv. Thank you in advance for your efforts in all of this.

Enclosed is a *Kuntres* for Yom Kippur that was just published. You will surely confirm its receipt and merit the many through it.

Signing with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah for all that is good, and with regards to your household, and awaiting your response.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Enclosed is a letter to R' M. Axelrad shlita; please urge him to fulfill my request.

## 7821

B"H, 7 Adar Rishon, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [scholar], Moreinu HaRav Sh.Z. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letters in due time. Regarding the books that are still in your possession, please be so kind as to hand them over to the committee for Beis Rivkah and printing, and forward the funds you received from their sale to HaRav B.G. shlita, as well as the repayment for my Gemach.

I have instructed that the *Sefer HaZichronos* be sent to you as you requested, and I trust you will confirm its receipt.

Regarding what you wrote about having been ill in your legs on several occasions (and I hope that by now you have fully recovered), perhaps it was necessary to fulfill the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, **simply**, without entering into calculations, lengthy contemplation, or asking for advice on the matter. This is based on what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 11, and in *Likkutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning "Yechayeinu Miyomayim," at the end of the *maamar*, that *emunah* is the aspect of the feet.

I am currently burdened with much work and many preoccupations, and I ask your forgiveness for the brevity of my letters; I am certain you will judge me favorably.

Enclosed is a *Moreh Shiur* that has just been published.

I will conclude with regards to your household and all those who inquire after my welfare, and in particular the congregants of the beis medrash and the gabbaim shlita.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

The regards via our shluchim surely reached them in due time.

## 7824

B"H, 22 Adar II, 5708

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Z. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

My letters of 23 Adar and 11 Adar II, along with the Kuntres for Purim, were surely received in due time. Enclosed is the Kuntres for 2 Nissan. Please be kind enough to confirm receipt of the above and inform me in what manner you have shared these with the public. As is well known, the Zohar (Vol. I, 106a) speaks of the great superiority of Avraham over Noach, in that Avraham prayed for the people of his generation. Consider this: Avraham Avinu was a neshamah of Atzilus, yet upon whom did he choose to focus his prayers? Upon the people of Sedom and Amorah—those who were, furthermore, specifically opposed to his own quality of Chesed and Hachnasas Orchim. How much more so, then, for us—neshamos of the ikvei meshicha—when the members of our generation are the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***7824***

From the secretariat archives.

**Moreinu Harav Z.:** Taubal. An additional letter to him—see above, Vol. 5, 1548.

## 7826

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5708
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Moshe Zev, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter:

a) You surely received the *Kuntres* for *Lag B'Omer* in due time, and likewise, Mr. Feiglin delivered to you, upon his arrival, the *shmurah* [matzah] which contained one of each of the three *mitzvos* from the *ke'arah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live.

b) Thank you for the book *Tohu Chaim*. I showed my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live, the story recounted there regarding the *tefillin* of the Alter Rebbe. He told me that he had not heard this story, but he had heard that for a certain reason, R' Nachum, son of the Mitteler Rebbe, gave the *Tefillin d'Shimusha Rabba* of the Alter Rebbe to the Tzemach Tzedek.

c) ...Surely, when there is news regarding R' Kliogant, you will inform me.

d) Regarding your question as to the meaning of what is written concerning "he who breaks a fence, a snake shall bite him" (*Koheles 10:8*)—that this refers to the *Nachash HaKadmoni* (the primordial serpent) and also a snake in *peshuto shel mikra* (the literal sense)—the *maamar* "Zachor" 5634 is not currently in my hands to consult. However, on the face of it, it is simple that "a snake in *peshuto shel mikra*" means a literal snake bite, or at the very least, a physical punishment, similar to the words of our Sages (Shabbos 110a). It is possible to say that what is written regarding Yehoshua (Yehoshua 6:26), "with his firstborn he shall lay its foundation," is an **additional** punishment beyond the known [principle that] "he who breaks a fence, a snake shall bite him." Therefore, Chiel died specifically from a snake bite, as our Sages stated, cited in *Yalkut Shimoni* (Melachim I, 18).

e) Thank you for the stories you transcribed in your letter.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, would say at certain times that *Shir HaShirim* [should be recited] on Erev Shabbos, but apparently, it is not permitted to reveal which times these are.

Regarding "Forgive us," etc., one does not strike the chest during any *tefillah* after which we do not say *Tachanun*. This means also not during *Ma'ariv* **all** year round.

The three stories regarding the Alter Rebbe are unknown (and to many, they are **highly** puzzling).

f) Thank you if you will send me (on condition that I return it, if you so stipulate) the *Iggeres HaKodesh* by R' Y. Diskin that you mention.

g) Enclosed is the *Kuntres* for *Lag B'Omer* which was just published, and may you merit to share it with the public.

With regards to all those who seek his welfare.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7828

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5708
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, etc., the Temimim, Rabbi Y. Chitrik, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of 23 Iyar was received. You do not explain why your influence on your students would diminish now if you were to also take part in the education of the youth under the auspices of the Agudah; in my opinion, the opposite is true.

As for me—it is obvious that you should not neglect your study with those who come from distant backgrounds [...] those who are distant from Torah and mitzvos. The greatness of "extracting the precious from the vile" cannot be sufficiently described. However, at the same time, improving education from mediocre to good, and from good to better—and ultimately establishing among them the study of Tanya, sichos, and maamarim—is also a matter of the greatest importance. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Lag B'Omer; may you merit to share it with the many.

With wishes for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**
