## 7831

7831

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., Moreinu Harav Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my letter of 9 Tammuz:

In the meantime, I have received your letter stating that you do not know the holy stories and sichos, etc., and therefore you are not reporting them! If this is indeed the case, the wonder is even greater than if you knew them and were simply not writing them down. But what can I do? A Yid, being rooted in the *Atzmus* of Hashem, possesses true *bechirah* (free choice), as is explained in *Likutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning *V'heineif*, chapter 3.

Enclosed is a copy of the letter sent yesterday.

With best wishes for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7833

B”H, 18 Menachem Av, 5708

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc.,
Rabbi A. A. [Axelrod]—may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your letter concerning the printing of a *kuntres* in memory of the late Rabbi G. Raud, I have not replied until now because, for the time being, I have no *kuntres* available to be printed.

However, we currently have in print the *Kitzurim v’He’aros* (Abridgments and Notes) of the Tzemach Tzedek on Tanya, and as an addition to them, the notes of the Rebbe Rayatz on several chapters of Tanya (five pages), as well as a letter from the Rebbe Rayatz regarding Tanya, and so on. It will be a book in the format of the small Tanya, approximately 170 pages long. I do not know the exact printing costs, but they are incomparable to the sum left from the estate of the aforementioned for this purpose.

Consequently, there are two options: either to wait until a *kuntres* is available (in my opinion, no later than the month of Tishrei-Cheshvan), and all the copies printed will be in the name of the aforementioned; or to print a number of copies of the aforementioned book of *Kitzurim* in the name of the aforementioned, corresponding to the sum he left for this purpose (estimated at 300–400 copies), and the remainder will be in the name of another donor.

Please inform me of your decision regarding this within the coming week, as that is before the completion of the printing of the *Kitzurim*.

In the text you propose to print, you also include the address of the donors. Certainly, as is the custom in America, this will increase the number of those seeking assistance who will turn to the aforementioned. I only mention this to offer a suggestion.

The Chassid, etc., Rabbi M. Dubinsky—may he live and be well—has already submitted his papers to the consulate.

To conclude with a matter of Torah: In connection with a letter I received, I happened to see in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, the *maamar* beginning "David Zemirot," where it writes there (160, bottom of the page): "The inwardness of Torah is completely unified with the *Ohr Ein Sof Baruch Hu*, etc., and in relation to *Ein Sof Baruch Hu*, all the worlds are literally **nothing** [k’lo], etc. Even the inwardness of Torah is not to be forgotten, etc., since they are not considered anything at all," end quote.

On the face of it, the opposite seems more logical; it should have said that in *Ohr Ein Sof Baruch Hu* it is **not** [anything], and in Torah it is **nothing** [k’lo]. This requires further study.

With best wishes,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Just now, the *sicha* of *Chai Elul* of this year has been released for publication. However, it will be printed in a small format—that is, like the *sicha* of Purim 5701, 10 Kislev 5707, and the like—and will contain approximately 25–30 pages. I am doubtful whether the family of the aforementioned Rabbi G. would be satisfied with such a booklet.

7834

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5708

I will conclude with the wish that you be healthy, both physically and spiritually, you and your family, may they live, and that you share good news in all details.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7836

7836

B"H, 18 Elul, 5708

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Shneur Zalman, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 6 Elul:

1) I was happy to hear that you have already begun your holy work as a shadar. It is a known principle regarding this (and all matters of holiness, which are an *is'arusa d'lesata*—an awakening from below—that correspond to the conduct from Above, measure for measure) that each and every day must be on a higher and more elevated level than the day (which is also a term for *giluy*—revelation) that preceded it (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 10). If this is true in all generations, then how much more so in this *ikvesa d'meshicha*—the heels of Moshiach—where we must transform the reality that "there is no day whose curse is not **greater** than the one before it" (*Sotah* 49b) into revealed and manifest good.

2) Regarding the method of drawing people close to the shul—the nature and quality of the Jewish community in Paris has changed since the time I lived there. This is a matter dependent on the changing times, and it is impossible for me to offer an opinion on this from here. However, in general, the name of Lubavitch and its Nasi, shlita, is already sufficiently known there. Anash, may they live, also know the nature of the leaders of the shul, each one individually. On the spot, they will find the appropriate path for each person. Provided that they set aside **melancholy** and hold fast to action and accomplishment—quite simply.

3) Regarding the matter of donating funds for the needs of the *melachah* (the institution/organization) there—there are no suitable conditions for the *melachah* at this time.

4) I am enclosing the *kuntres* for 18 Elul that was just published, and may you merit to share it with the many.

I will conclude with a blessing of *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* for you, your household, and all those influenced by you, and wishes for success in your holy work.

Awaiting good news from you,

**M. Schneerson**

7737

[Elul 5708]

I am always pleased to respond to matters of Torah, as they appear to me. I will continue to do so in the future, and naturally, if it is within my ability, I will answer.

Rashi at the beginning of Parshas Eikev is based on the Midrash Tanchuma there. See Yalkut Shimoni, beginning of Parshas Eikev; Tehillim 49 [Remez 858; Midrash Tehillim 49, 6], and elsewhere. There is no contradiction there—it is merely a clarification. The text states: "David said, 'Ribono shel Olam, I do not fear the severe mitzvos of the Torah because they are severe; rather, I fear the light ones, lest I have transgressed them because they are light. And You said, "Be as careful with a light mitzvah as with a severe one." Therefore it is said, "And it shall be if you hearken (Eikev tishme'un)..." [etc.]. "How great is Your goodness" (Tehillim 31)—this refers to the reward for the light mitzvos.'" End quote.

**The second question:** a) You seem to think that Chazal did not properly appreciate the greatness of Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai. This is not the case. It suffices to cite two or three examples:

1) Regarding his knowledge of Torah and the sciences: (Maseches Sofrim, ch. 16) "If all the heavens were parchment, all the trees were quills, and all the seas were ink, they would not suffice to write the wisdom he learned from his teachers." 

2) Regarding worldly matters and the conduct of the state: (End of Sotah) "When Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai died, the luster of wisdom ceased" (in worldly wisdom, see Maharsha). 

3) As a leader of Israel: (Sifrei, end of Parshas Bracha) "Moshe was in Egypt for forty years, in Midian for forty years, and sustained Israel for forty years. Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai engaged in commerce for forty years, served the Sages for forty years, and sustained Israel (he was Nasi) for forty years."

b) Regarding the assessment of the events during the time of the Churban—the political situation at the time, the mood of the Romans, whether there was hope for peace, etc.—how can we, who are removed from that time by more than 1,800 years and possess almost no **authoritative** documentation other than the Talmud from that era, offer an opinion that disagrees even in a minor detail with the opinion of people who lived in that generation or in the century that followed?

- This is true even if what was written in the book of Divrei Hayamim were **simple.** Now that this assessment has been incorporated into the Talmud—meaning that through Divine Providence it has become part of the Oral Torah, whose holiness is the same as the holiness of the Oral Torah—there is no room for debate as to whether the matter is true. There is only room for an effort to understand the matter and explain it, so that we, too, may understand it.

c) A decisive proof that Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai did **not** view the decree of the Churban as something that could not be averted, but rather that he strove even then to save the Beis Hamikdash from destruction, is that **before** he went to Vespasian, he tried [to persuade] the leaders of Jerusalem at the time to make peace with the Romans. Only when he did not succeed in this did he go to Vespasian, to endeavor, in the words of Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai, "perhaps there will be a small salvation."

[d]) One more thing that you write, and I wish, after asking your forgiveness, to protest against it: You write that if, in my opinion, your writing is inappropriate, I should write to you openly that you should busy yourself with your business and not with the aforementioned Torah matters.

How can I agree to this! Consider for yourself: for **thousands upon thousands of years** his soul—which is the essence of every Jew—has been engaged in Torah, and after our life in this physical world, the soul will return to engage in Torah and delve into its wisdom, which is endless, **for all eternity.** It is only that in the meantime, for a period of a few **decades,** the Holy One, blessed be He, has provided him with a business occupation. How can one view this as his primary occupation, and the matter of Torah as an additional matter?

Rather, each one of us must be careful to study Torah in accordance with the truth, as Chazal have taught us.

With wishes for all the best, and I am prepared in the future as well to clarify together with you that which is not so well understood by people like us.

## 7840

B"H, 11 Teves, 5709

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished [Rabbi] D. [Bravman], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of 12 Kislev was received. In response to your questions:

1) I reiterate my request that you please answer all my questions point by point, so that I will not have to repeat them.

2) Regarding the *piskei dinim*: I asked my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and he said that they should be printed in their place in two volumes, on the best possible paper, and as soon as possible. You will find other instructions regarding this in my letter of 9 Sivan, 5708. It is understood that this printing is in addition to the other printings of the *sefer* that you have in your possession.

3) I have pointed out to you several times that it is possible to send *seforim* via travelers without any difficulty, especially now that refugees are arriving in New York from the camps on a regular basis. Furthermore, it is also possible to send them via travelers to France, and from there we can arrange the shipment here through *anash*. For example, our friends R. Shlomo Palmer and R. Shneur Zalman Gurary will soon be returning here from Paris.

However, so that the *seforim* are not lost in Paris, please send them to the attention of our friend, the learned and distinguished Rabbi N. Nemonov, and inform him to arrange the shipment according to the instructions sent to him.

4) Regarding your suggestion to inquire with Rabbi Kalmanovitz about another shipping method, we have determined that the expenses involved would negate the entire matter.

5) As for the means, they are ready and waiting; the main difficulty is the transport. I have already urged R. N. Nemonov and R. B. G. [Gorodetsky] several times, and we hope they will arrange it properly.

6) The packages you send via the post office should be addressed to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, Machne Israel, and Kehot, and in such a way that the customs office here will not value any single shipment at more than one hundred dollars, because then one must provide paperwork, etc.

7) I have not yet received the *Likutei Torah* to this day. I do not understand why the post office is not receiving the shipment of *Likutei Torah* and *Torah Or*, and surely it is possible to send individual copies from time to time.

8) According to the law, *seforim* sent in other languages (not in English), such as *Lashon HaKodesh* and Yiddish, are exempt from customs duty here. Therefore, the difficulty with customs that you mention in your letter is not understood.

9) Regarding the sale of a portion of the *Shulchan Aruch*: there is no room to sell only a part at a low price, because then the rest would also have to be sold at that price. However, if it is possible to sell **everything**—except for fifty or a hundred copies for us—and for no less than one and a half times the cost, then it is worthwhile.

10) I urge you once again to answer my letter and inform me what has already been sent and what you still have to send, and especially to utilize travelers as mentioned above (section 3).

11) In the coming days, we will send you the *sicha* of 19 Kislev, and there will surely be a *sicha* for 24 Teves as well.

I sign with a request, an appeal, and the hope of receiving your detailed reply soon.

**M. Schneerson**

We have received word from the post office that 191 packages have been received. Even though there is no customs duty on them, the law requires that if a shipment exceeds one hundred dollars, there must be an invoice from the sender, as well as a consular invoice (certified by the American consul). Regarding the sender's invoice, we have arranged it here according to the enclosed copy, and we have deposited a sum of money for the second one.

If it will not cause confusion and difficulties, please obtain a consular invoice for the shipment of the 191 packages. If it will cause confusion, it is better to lose the deposit here.

For the future, if each shipment to Merkos, Machne, and Kehot is not too large at one time, so that they do not value it here at more than one hundred dollars, we will not need to deal with paperwork, etc.

## 7848

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5710

...I received your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh. Your words are alarming. I have already replied to someone else that this is a matter of *dinei nefashos*, and it is well known how much *chakiras hadavar* is required in *dinei nefashos*. Regarding the fact that I mentioned everyone while at the *tziyun*, and *b'li neder*, I will do so again tomorrow—it is *alles gute freind* (all good friends), and I have conducted myself this way for several years now, upon entering the *heichal* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *hakadosh*. See *Sefer HaSichos*, section 869: "And he exempts the masses with the *kiddush* while wearing the fine garments he would wear."

## 7849

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5710

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter:

I was pleased to hear that you are maintaining what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, instructed regarding the repeating of maamarim. It is very good to share with the listeners, either after or before the repetition—depending on the circumstances of the place—a segment from a sicha of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, that is appropriate for the time, the parsha of the week, and the like.

Certainly, even when there is no minyan for davening, one should at least hear Kaddish, Barechu, and Kedushah.

Regarding what you write, that on Erev Shabbos there is no learning at all—I do not understand this at all. Perhaps you mean that there is no classroom instruction.

As for your question regarding a tikkun—in my opinion, you should increase your efforts in the chinuch of the youth, and for the time being, divert your attention from the entire matter you wish to rectify, and strive not to think about it at all.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the holiday, and a copy of a letter I wrote to someone else.

Wishing you a kosher and happy Yom Tov, and success that you should be a yerei shamayim, a Chassid, and a lamdan,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7849***

From a photocopy of the letter.

## 7851

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5710

To the sons and daughters of Israel in the great city of New York and its surroundings,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

This is the ninth year since the "Beis Rivkah" educational institutions for girls were founded by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, in accordance with the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

And praise to Hashem, these institutions have grown in both quantity and quality, and the students who study there are educated in a kosher manner, based on the foundations of Torah and yiras shamayim.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, placed great importance on these institutions, viewing them as essential for the preservation of the House of Israel. From time to time, and especially on the occasion of the annual celebrations, he would issue a call of affection, request, and demand to draw the attention of the general public to the great obligation and privilege of every man and woman in Israel to support the "Beis Rivkah" institutions that have already been established, and to enable their development, expansion, and the founding of new branches.

The words of the tzaddikim and leaders of Israel endure forever. Even after the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, we must always remember his instructions in general, and now in particular regarding a matter that is timely: to awaken and exert ourselves with greater intensity in supporting these institutions, which were so dear to him.

Those involved in the "Beis Rivkah" educational organization, led by the diligent activist in the dissemination of Torah and kosher education, our friend, the distinguished Rabbi Yisroel Jacobson, may he live and be well, are arranging an annual celebration which will take place, G-d willing, on the upcoming 20th of Iyar.

I hereby turn with a call of awakening to every man and woman in Israel whose heart is touched by the fate of the daughters of Israel, to participate in this annual celebration with their presence and their resources, and to be active and proactive for the benefit of these institutions in general, and for the benefit of the annual celebration in particular.

And I am confident that the blessings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, with which he blessed all those who participate in supporting the "Beis Rivkah" institutions, will be fulfilled in them and in their households, may they live to be blessed with all good, both materially and spiritually.

I sign with respect and blessing for all good,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7851***

From a photocopy of the letter printed in *Yimei Bereishis*, p. 144.

## 7853

7853

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5710

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Sh. (may he live and be well),

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Thursday of last week, and your son, the Hatamim R' (may he live and be well), also conveyed to me what you discussed with him on Erev Shabbos.

Although you write that I cannot imagine what you are suffering from the partner in our camp, it is obvious that I am not saying that my distress is the same as yours. However, I do have an estimation of what you are going through. Even so, what benefit is there in you and your wife (may she live and be well) becoming agitated and increasingly upset? What will be rectified by this?

If he were able to pay but unwilling, there would be room to say that through agitation, threats, and the like, he might settle at least a portion of his debt. But since he is unable, what is the point of all the above, other than distress and suffering? Furthermore, he currently has no livelihood, not even for daily expenses, and as for what will be in the future—who knows?

These things should have been explained in appropriate terms, with the right tone and at the right time, to the partner in our camp as well.

Seemingly, for the time being, there is nothing more to be done regarding this.

Enclosed is a receipt for Mr. Gold (may he live and be well).

In the event that you find it necessary that, in addition to the receipt, there should also be some letter from the Vaad HaMaamad, you will surely let me know.

With blessings and in the hope of hearing good news from you as well,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***7853***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L'Melech* 5, p. 89, from a secretariat copy.

Regarding its content, see letter 4850 above.

**R' Sh.:** Pozner. Additional letters to him appear above in 7767, and in the notes referenced there.

## 7855

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5720

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright individual, who conducts his business with integrity, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. Hakohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, along with the enclosed check made out to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. In accordance with your authorization for me to distribute it as I see fit, I have allocated it as follows: a maaser portion for the *maamad*.

Half of the remaining amount—for **printing** and **distributing** the *kuntres* for the upcoming 12th-13th of Tammuz, when the Rebbe reaches seventy years of age. I have inscribed on the *kuntres* that this should be effective in strengthening the *hiskashrus* of the one who wishes to remain anonymous to the Rebbe (by printing and disseminating his Torah **throughout the entire world**).

I did this specifically because **I** do not know what is happening with [my own] *hiskashrus* (please do not take offense at my saying this).

I am seeing many, many *mofsim* from the Rebbe at this time; so if you say that for you there is "no news," there must be a reason for that.

It is very possible that the Rebbe holds that the building should not be sold at this time, and therefore there are no buyers, and the like.

And perhaps this is due to a weakness, *chas v'shalom*, in *hiskashrus*. (However, I believe that you, too, have experienced *mofsim*—with your partner and the like—only you do not notice them all.) That is why I used a portion of your money for the *hafatzah* of the Rebbe’s Torah—one of the best pieces of advice for *hiskashrus* to the Nasi Yisrael, the master of Torah.

The second half I have deposited into the secret charity fund from which the Rebbe used to provide assistance privately to distinguished individuals, and which continues to be used for that purpose.

The *kuntres* will be ready in a few days. The *Kesser Shem Tov* is enclosed.

Please notify me when you receive it.

Blessing you with all good and awaiting good tidings,

**Rabbi M.S.**

## 7857

7857

B”H, 26 Tammuz, 5717

The illustrious Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, distinguished in Torah and mitzvos, possessor of fine character traits, occupied with communal needs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi L. Rabinowitz, Chief Rabbi
of the countries of South Africa

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to have your visit while you were in New York, and I was happy to have the opportunity to speak with you. I hope that you have arrived home in peace.

The subject of our conversation is surely still in your memory. I am certain that it will not be long before you begin to implement what we discussed—the founding of a yeshiva in your country for those who are unable or unwilling to travel to a place of Torah. You should also immediately begin vigorous advocacy and action to strengthen and expand kosher education in general throughout your country.

Every man and woman in Israel shares in the responsibility for kosher education, and you, in your capacity as Chief Rabbi of your country, surely recognize the magnitude of the potential that rests upon you in this regard. Were it not for the principle that one only encourages those who are already diligent, I would say that it is unnecessary to urge someone like you; however, diligence is commendable for such an undertaking. I am certain that you will value the time so that it is not lost, and that you will proceed to implement the plan of action we discussed as soon as possible. I wish you *siyatta d’shmaya* with abundant success in both material and spiritual matters.

Enclosed is a new *kuntres* that has been published in the field of Chassidus—*Kuntres* 12-13 Tammuz 5717—and I am sure you will find it of great interest.

May the Ribono shel Olam transform these days of distress into days of consolation in our immediate future, in the merit of the Torah and the light within it.

With wishes for all the best,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 7858

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5721

Rabbi, Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, R' Y. HaLevi,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from last week:

Regarding what is brought in Chassidic discourse several times as *Sefer Emeich HaMelech* or *Am HaMelech*, the reference is to *Emek HaMelech* by R' Naftali Hertz, printed in Amsterdam in the year 5408 [1648]. See *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, the *maamar* *Tze'enah U're'enah*, where it is noted that one may rely upon it, as even in *Etz Chaim* "it is not mentioned at all."

Regarding your observation from *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Pinchas*, *d'h Kadesh Yisrael*, page 284, where it is written there several times "Kadesh HaAdam," and you wondered why it does not say "Yisrael":

You surely have an old printing; it has already been corrected in subsequent printings. It seems that due to fear of the censor, it was printed as "HaAdam" initially.

See *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Shemos*, page 86, and the notes there.

May Hashem turn these days into joy and gladness, and may it be revealed to the eyes of all flesh that "Yisrael is holy to Hashem, all who devour him shall be held guilty," speedily in our days.

With best wishes for all that is good,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 7864

[Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5711]

... Many thanks for the maamarim and sichos you sent me, several of which I did not yet have.

Surely, if you find more, you will send them as well, and I thank you in advance.

Regarding your difficulty with the Simchas Torah 5686 sicha concerning the decree of the hats and the holy Rebbe, the "Gaon and Chassid" (as he is referred to in Likutei Torah, Shir HaShirim 18:3) of Berditchev, noting that the years do not align—I have heard something similar, but it refers to **R. Hillel of Paritch** (and it seems the transcriber made an error). This also clarifies what is written in the *Hemshech* regarding what he said to his students, as we have not heard that there was a yeshiva by R. Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning *bikkurim*—see Zohar Vol. III, 253a, and the *Mikdash Melech* there; *D'H V'Yom HaBikkurim*, 254.

* * *

* * *

Regarding your son, Sh. D. *sheyichyeh*, who asks if he should travel here to study in Tomchei Temimim—see the *Kuntres* for Shemini Atzeres, page 90. *Anash* of London must continue the light of Lubavitch in London, *un es halt derbei* (and it is currently at that stage).

It would be proper to organize a group of *bochurei chemed* for the study of *Chassidus*, and your son *sheyichyeh* should also be energized by their spirit.

And then, "Hashem will enlighten the eyes of all." Once the group is established, we can then discuss the question of whether your son *sheyichyeh* should travel from there—and thank you for the good news regarding this.

## 7865

7865

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, and to all lovers of Torah
Wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and blessings!

The day of good tidings is drawing near—Tuesday, the 19th of Kislev—the day upon which the righteousness of the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) was revealed, and with it, the righteousness of the teachings of Chassidus—the teachings of Chabad Chassidus and the teachings of Chassidus in general.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, writes in his letter of 10 Kislev 5710, two months before his passing, that "the study of the teachings of Chassidus is not a matter that pertains only to any particular faction; rather, the obligation to study it is incumbent upon all of Klal Yisrael, and upon those who are learned in Torah in particular."

It is the duty of Anash to be **engaged** in the dissemination of the study of Chassidus. And "engagement" means a ceaseless effort, in such a way that in all of one's affairs—even the peripheral ones—one intends to achieve this goal, "just as in business, where one is occupied with it all day long, not necessarily only at the moment one is engaged in the core of the business, because the matter is of the utmost importance to him. He is 'clothed' in it at every hour and at every time."

In another place, it is explained at length how the condition that **"your springs shall spread outward"**—the springs of the Baal Shem Tov—is a prerequisite, a preparation, and a vessel for the coming of Moshiach.

This condition, which each and every one of us must strive with all our might to fulfill, contains three details:

(a) **"Spread" (Yafutzu):** To teach the study of Chassidus in a manner of **dissemination**—spreading it over a wide area, so that the study reaches every part of the place where one is teaching this Torah.

(b) **"Your springs" (Ma'ayanosecha):** The teachings of Chassidus that one disseminates must retain the characteristics of a spring.

There are two primary characteristics of a spring: 1) Its waters are living and flow forth without cessation from the source of the spring. 2) One does not pay much attention to the quantity, for the spring flows from its source drop by drop. This is also the condition for the dissemination of this Torah. Quantity is not the main thing; what matters is that the study be "alive," with the vitality of the soul and internal enthusiasm, and that it flows from its source—from the inner soul of the one disseminating the Torah, who is connected in the depths of his heart to the Nesi'im of the teachings of Chassidus.

(c) **"Outward" (Chutzah):** We must not be satisfied with studying only in the beis medrash and the shul, but also while walking on the way, while sitting in the store, and the like. Similarly, regarding the nature of the students, one should not be limited to certain factions or specific types of people, for the obligation to study the teachings of Chassidus is incumbent even upon the simplest of the simple, just as even the greatest of the great cannot reach its ultimate depth.

And even for those who are found outside of all the "camps," even in a place that Scripture testifies is **"outward" (chutzah)**—even there, the springs must be disseminated.

The merit of the effort to disseminate the springs outward will continue to be a vessel to receive the blessings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who blessed each and every one of us for the 19th of Kislev before his passing, and surely blesses us now as well for the 19th of Kislev of this year, saying to us directly: "May you be blessed by Hashem with a good year in the study and dissemination of Chassidus; may you, your households, your sons, and your daughters live in the ways of Chassidus; and may you, your households, and all who join you be blessed with everything you need, both materially and spiritually."

With blessings for success in your avodah and all the best,

**M. Schneerson**

***

A letter from the week of Parshas Vayeitzei has just been received. As requested, the kuntresim are being sent to your new address.

It is a matter of wonder that, as of now, there has been no response to what was written in sections 21-22 of the Reshimot for Parshas Bereishis.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7868

7868

B"H, 9 Teves, 5711

...Regarding what you wrote, that there are those who say it is not so important to find a source or a place in Chazal or a halacha that is brought in Chassidus, because the Chassidus itself is the source—I do not hold this way. Furthermore, when one does see the source, many times additional understanding is added to the matter in Chassidus as well. Seemingly, it is also more *chassidish* to say that a source exists and I have not found it, rather than to say that I know for certain there is no source and the Rebbe innovated this based on a directive, etc. And we see tangibly in the *hagahos* of the Tzemach Tzedek on Chassidus how much he labored in this.

And this is not the place to elaborate.

#### ***7868***

Printed in the *Kovetz Yagdil Torah* (Jerusalem), issue 20, p. 9.

## 7872

7872

B"H, 15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah La'ilan, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

The year of the histalkus of our Nasi, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, has concluded.

The longing intensifies, for the summer has ended, the winter has passed, and we have not been saved.

But on the other hand, habit takes its toll. There is room for concern that the matter may grow stale, and that the light and warmth of the hiskashrus to our Nasi—to his Torah and his directives, which are all one—will gradually diminish, Heaven forbid.

These are the words that Moshe spoke regarding Torah: "These words that I command you **today,"** which is interpreted as a new royal decree (*diotagma*) that everyone rushes to receive. And regarding mitzvos: "My mitzvos that I command you **today,"** which is interpreted to mean that they should be as new to you as if you had heard them on that very day.

#### ***7872***

From a photocopy of the Rebbe's holy handwriting. It appears to be the beginning of a general letter that was not completed.

## 7773

7773

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter informing me of the state of your health, that you are feeling a depletion of strength and the doctor wishes to perform tests, etc., and you are asking for my opinion—

He may comply with the doctor and undergo the tests. Regarding the depletion of strength—be careful to eat breakfast, and from time to time study some subject, whether in Nigleh or in Chassidus, that you will derive **simple pleasure** from. And it shall be health to your navel and marrow to your bones.

When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, for proper health.

It is my hope that you will bring me good news regarding this.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your spiritual health.

Perhaps you have heard the story of one of the people in America who came to ask the advice of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his lumber business. After the Rebbe gave him an answer regarding that, and continued to instruct him in matters of Torah and Mitzvos, the man said that he had not asked about that. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, replied: "What a strange thing! Regarding business, where you are the expert and it has nothing to do with me—you ask for my advice. But regarding Torah and Mitzvos, which are among the fundamental matters and the occupation of my fathers and forefathers—about this you do not ask."

Of course, the cases are not at all similar—but, in any event, I have more of a connection to the study of Gemara, Poskim, and Chassidus than to the science of medicine. And if so, "What a strange thing!"

With blessings for a speedy recovery and proper health for you and your wife, may they live.

#### ***7773***

From the secretariat copy.

**The story:** See also above, Vol. 4, Letter 1036.

## 7778

## 7880

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and faithful communal worker, Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht, I received your inquiry regarding your desire to arrange that after one hundred and twenty years, you be assured of the recitation of Kaddish and the study of Mishnayos.

Regarding this, if it is your wish, it is possible to arrange that after one hundred and twenty years, Kaddish will be recited and Mishnayos will be studied in Eretz Yisroel (may it be rebuilt speedily). I do not know the exact cost, but it is approximately 300–400 Israeli pounds.

However, regarding the essence of the matter, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known: "It is better to do things with living matters while one is alive." Therefore, my suggestion is that you should live long, good, and full years—filled with Torah and mitzvos, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

Take upon yourself the printing of a book of the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and have your name and the name of your wife (may she live and be well) printed at the beginning of the book. Anyone who studies from this book will grant you and your wife a share in their learning, and the merit of the many will depend upon you to lengthen your days and years in pleasantness.

Enclosed is the booklet published for Lag B'Omer; I am certain you will study it and delve into the sayings contained within.

With blessings for long life and good years for you and your wife (may they live) in peace and prosperity.

#### ***7880***

## 7882

B.H., Sunday, Parshas Beha'aloscha, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in today’s farbrengen of
"Irgun Beis Rivkah"
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and blessings!

It was good news for me to learn that "Irgun Beis Rivkah" — under the supervision of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch — has acquired another building in a new part of the city, with the goal of opening an additional Beis Rivkah school there, thereby providing the opportunity for a greater number of Jewish daughters — may they increase — to receive an education in the spirit of Torah and Yiddishkeit.

The expansion and growth of an important institution is generally satisfying, if only because it demonstrates the vitality of the organization. Even more praiseworthy is the establishment of Torah chinuch institutions in more and more parts of the city, through which, with the help of Hashem Yisbarach, the spiritual and physical existence of Klal Yisrael will be secured.

Particularly worthy of praise is the opening of new branches of the Beis Rivkah schools, which demonstrates the awareness of their askanim that one must not be satisfied with what has already been achieved in this field, as long as there is still one Jewish girl who is not receiving her education due to a lack of a sufficient number of authentic Jewish schools.

I send my greetings to all participants in the celebration and to all the askanim of "Irgun Beis Rivkah," led by the esteemed Chossid, man of action, and accomplished activist, etc., Rabbi Y. Jacobson, and I call upon them to work tirelessly, even more and more, for chinuch habanos al taharas hakodesh, in accordance with the will and command of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I hope that every conscious Jew, man and woman, will fulfill their duty to assist in the existence and expansion of the already existing Beis Rivkah schools and for the opening of new Beis Rivkah schools.

During a visit from chinuch askanim to him, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said:

**"The Almighty does not remain a debtor, and all those who act and help in the field of kosher chinuch — the Almighty pays them back with what they need, and especially with Yiddishe nachas from their children."**

The words of the tzaddikim are alive and endure forever.

And surely Hashem will bless all the supporters of the Beis Rivkah movement, and the participants of this gathering among them, with what they need in both gashmius and ruchnius.

With blessings for goodness in gashmius and ruchnius,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7885

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

Mr. Yosef Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write the main points of your life story and mention that you teach music, both in school and privately.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the explanation of the Mishnah, "I was created to serve my Maker," which is accomplished through fulfilling the will of one's Maker by studying Torah and performing mitzvos. From this, it is understood that in whatever profession a person is engaged, it is clear that there are possibilities within it to spread true Yiddishkeit and its matters among those with whom one comes into contact and connection. This is all the more so when the connection is that of a teacher and student, for every student naturally harbors a feeling of love and respect for their teacher. This also prepares the student to accept the teacher’s words even outside the realm of the specific subject matter. This is something that can be seen tangibly, especially since, according to your letter, your students in this field are mostly youth, for whom any improvement and correction of their situation is a correction and improvement of their future, and first and foremost, in the building of their Jewish homes.

From the above, it is understood that every effort and endeavor in this regard is worthwhile.

Regarding what you wrote about enrolling to study at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod, and detailing certain obstacles that are preventing you from doing so:

The question will practically be on the agenda in about a month or more, after the summer break, when the yeshiva’s schedule is organized. It is possible that during this time, some of the details you mention in your letter will be resolved.

As for your statement that you have debts, and therefore even after entering the yeshiva you would need to continue your professional work in order to settle them—you will surely discuss this with the yeshiva administration. There are many possibilities for arranging this in a way that will allow you to keep all the yeshiva’s schedules. It has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

May it be the will of the Creator of the world and its Guide, who watches over each and every person with Divine Providence, that you go from strength to strength on the path of Torah and mitzvos—the path that leads the Jewish man and woman to their true happiness, both materially and spiritually. It will be a pleasure for me to receive good news from you regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for good news.

7886

12 Tammuz, 5711

To be conveyed to all anash: L’chaim, l’chaim u’livracha, and for an awakening toward success in upholding Yiddishkeit and disseminating the revealed Torah and Chassidus.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7887

7887

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have just sent you a telegram: "I am very surprised by your despondency. Follow the instructions of two expert doctors and strengthen your bitachon in Hashem, who will surely restore you to your strength. I await good news. With blessings for a speedy recovery. My signature."

You learn, you learn — but when it comes to putting it into practice, where is the bitachon?

Study the *Shaar HaBitachon* in *Chovos HaLevavos* three or four times. Naturally, I do not mean that you should study it all at once, but rather over the course of several weeks.

With blessings for a speedy recovery, and awaiting good news regarding your health in both the physical and spiritual sense,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7888

7888

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711
Brooklyn.

To my friend, the illustrious Rabbi, the pious and G-d-fearing man, a descendant of holy lineage, scion of noble stock, etc., etc., Rabbi Yochanan, may he live:

Shalom and blessings!

I received your letter of the 18th of Menachem Av with pleasure, in which you inform me that the wedding of your eldest son, may he live, will take place on the coming 4th of Elul.

I hereby express my heartfelt blessings, a Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May the wedding be at a propitious and successful time, may the union be a beautiful one, and may they build an everlasting edifice upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are explained in the teachings of Chassidus—the teachings of Toras HaChassidus. May you see from them, and from your other children, may they live, abundant nachas and delight, both materially and spiritually.

It is known that the matter of marriage transcends the Seder Hishtalshelus. As our Sages of blessed memory said, it is comparable to the splitting of the Red Sea, for the matter depends on Atik—meaning, it is an extension of Ohr Makif.

It can be said that this is why we find in the matter of marriage the concept of Makifim: 
1) A Makif upon the bride alone, which is the matter of giving the ring.

As is known, although the Mishnah states that a woman is acquired through money, it has already been stated in Tikkunei Zohar (Tikkun 5, Tikkun 10, and Tikkun 21, 90b): "And because of this it was said regarding the bride, 'Be sanctified to me **with this ring**.'" This is also found in several places that the people of Eretz Yisrael sanctify with a ring (the exchange of customs between the people of Bavel and Eretz Yisrael, in Yam Shel Shlomo, and elsewhere).

The giving of the ring is a Makif upon the bride’s finger, and it comes from the groom.

2) The bride circles the groom seven times, which is a Makif upon the groom that comes from the bride. This is in the manner of "a woman shall encompass a man" (Yirmiyahu 31:22) in the future to come.

These two Makifim take place under the chuppah, which is a general Makif upon both the groom and the bride together—meaning, a Makif of Binah to Ze'er Anpin and Nukvah. The matter is explained in Likutei Torah, Shir HaShirim, in the maamar beginning "Al Kol Kavod Chuppah," and there is no room here to elaborate.

I conclude as I began, with the blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, your friend who respects and esteems you.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. As a *drasha geshenk* (wedding gift), I am enclosing a certificate for a package. Regarding the connection of a *drasha geshenk* to the concept of a Makif, see Likutei Torah, Parshas Naso, 29b.

## 7889

B"H, 8 Elul, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Parshas Shoftim, in which you describe the state of health of [name]—may she live and be well—and ask for my opinion regarding what the doctor told her.

In my opinion, regarding the surgery for the meridians, if this is the view of two specialists in this field, you should proceed with it, and may Hashem grant that it be successful.

Regarding the second matter, where he suggests she undergo surgery on the uterus, you must clarify with the doctor what his intention is: whether he wants to perform a complete "clean up," or merely remove the tumor. If it is the former—which doctors in the United States are generally eager to do—then you should also seek the opinion of two additional doctors. Only if all three agree to perform a "clean up" should it be done. May Hashem place in the hearts of the doctors the correct judgment to aim for the truth and the good, and may Hashem send His word and heal her through such-and-such a doctor and such-and-such a remedy.

Regarding what you wrote about [name]—may he live and be well—he should follow the doctors' instructions, especially regarding eating, drinking, and rest. And he should be a soldier for Hashem as he ought to be, as the Rambam writes in Hilchos Deios, Chapter 4: that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem.

My general letter to the students for the beginning of the school year surely reached you on time. I hope to hear good news from you regarding the start of studies as they ought to be, and especially regarding an increase in the number of male and female students, in accordance with the Torah ruling that we increase in matters of holiness.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I am surprised that the matter regarding Mr. [name]—may he live and be well—has dragged on for so long. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to suggest to him not to wait until the matter is finalized and the machines are arranged, but rather to set aside what he intended to give for printing in advance. When one demonstrates a conduct of generosity toward Hashem, one is shown a generous hand from Above, etc.

7890

**M. Schneerson**

From our Sages, of blessed memory: "The strength of the body is the strength of the soul [the *nefesh*]" — see *Zohar* Vol. I, 180b, 140b. The version "*d'nafsha*" is more specific, indicating that the state of the body affects the level of the soul closest to it specifically, which is called *nefesh*, as is known.

May this be the case in practice regarding your situation as well; the stronger one’s *bitachon* is in this, the swifter the improvement in health and the recovery.

I hope that from time to time our friends visit you, especially R' Schneur Zalman Butman, may he live.

## 7894

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Avreichim, R’ Avraham Yitzchak Shemtov, R’ Shalom DovBer Putterfas, and R’ Shmuel Dovid Gurkow,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

From time to time, I receive reports regarding your studies at the Manchester Yeshiva. While I am satisfied with your conduct in certain respects, even if everything were as it should be, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—which he repeated several times, quoting the Rebbe Maharash—is well known: "If 'good' is 'good,' then 'better' is not 'better.'" This is especially true since, in certain details, it appears your conduct and diligence in study require encouragement and strengthening.

I am writing to awaken you regarding the title that the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, gave to the Temimim: that they must be "candles to illuminate." Simply put, this must be manifest in the students of the Tomim. Each and every one of you must keep engraved in your memory the great responsibility placed upon you—that you must serve as an example to all the other students in the Yeshiva, so that they may see you and act accordingly. This applies not only to the study of Chassidus and the avodah of tefillah, but also to the study of Nigleh in general, and to matters of derech eretz between one person and another.

I hope that these few words will suffice to awaken you and bring you to the realization that the ultimate purpose of your coming to the Manchester Yeshiva is not only for your own benefit, but also to influence your environment—to serve as an example of how a yeshiva student should be, both internally and externally.

I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding your receipt of this letter, and that you have begun to put this matter into actual practice in all the aforementioned details.

With blessings for success in the study of the Torah of Nigleh and the Torah of Chassidus, with yiras shamayim,

**M. Schneerson**

With blessings,

## 7897

7897

B"H, 19 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Saadya
Shadar

Greetings and blessings!

I am sure you have received the general letter, as well as the Kuntres for 19 Kislev that was sent by the office.

Regarding your question: since your teaching schedule with the students makes it impossible for you to daven with *m'tinus* (deliberation), you ask for my opinion as to whether it is appropriate to leave the teaching position.

In my opinion, if it is possible for you to change your teaching assignment to a class that would allow you to daven with *m'tinus*, it is worthwhile to do so. However, in any case, you must continue teaching the students, as this is your connection to the *ilana d'chaya* (tree of life) in the most literal sense. Since you have merited this, you should not think about seeking any other endeavor.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

I am sure you will once again make efforts regarding obtaining a visa for Morocco.

## 7898

B"H, 1 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, R' Avraham Yitzchak, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

I received your letter for the "Chag HaChagim," 19 Kislev, in which you request a blessing.

It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the word *bracha* (blessing) is related to the word *geshem* (rain). Just as rain is only beneficial if it falls upon a field that has been plowed and sown, so too is it with a blessing: there must be plowing and sowing on the part of the recipient of the blessing. However, once that is done, even from a small amount of sowing, the blessing draws down great and extraordinary success.

Regarding *bnei Torah* and yeshiva students, the "plowing" is the observance of the yeshiva’s study schedule with precision, even if this sometimes results in less sleep or food and drink, and primarily, it is the opposition to the desire for laziness and a lack of diligence and persistence. The "sowing" is studying with appropriate diligence and persistence. When this preparation is present, the blessing draws down success in *haskalah* (intellectual grasp), understanding, and comprehension.

When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for success in Torah study and *yiras shamayim*. Surely, you, for your part, will do as mentioned above.

I trust that you recite Tehillim every day as divided for the days of the month, and that you also study the daily portion of the weekly parsha with Rashi.

With blessings for success and persistence in Torah study and *yiras shamayim*.

* * *

Regarding the fact that you prolong your *davening* and thereby miss out on the yeshiva’s study schedule—you should make up for this, and even add to it, during the hours after the *seder*.

Regarding your health—follow the doctor’s instructions, and divert your mind from thoughts about your health condition.

May Hashem grant you success.

## 7801

7801

B"H, 9 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, etc., R' Refael Nachman, may he live, HaKohen.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letters from the second night of Chanukah and the seventh night of Chanukah, in which you inform me that you have rented an apartment near where your daughters, may they live, reside and opposite the yeshivah. May it be the will of Hashem that this be successful, and may you dwell in your home with tranquility—both tranquility of the soul and tranquility of the body—and may you occupy yourself with your avodah, the holy work, as is fitting, without distractions from peripheral matters, and with proper health for yourself, your wife, and all your household members, may they live.

Many thanks for your precious gift, which is the *petek* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as well as for your account of the *seder hishtalshelus* of that *petek*, and for also including excerpts from the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

2) Regarding [the matter of]... one must not grow weary or tired of speaking with them again and yet again. The main thing is that the words be spoken with *nachas*, and the verse will be fulfilled: "The words of the wise are heard [when they are] in tranquility." May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding all of the above, just as you bring good tidings in your letter regarding the manner in which the *farbrengen* of the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev, was conducted. In accordance with this, I am enclosing a copy of my general letter on this subject.

Regarding your minimizing the matter of putting on tefillin, noting that it was only done three times—see Tanya, Chapter 26, that in truth it is **eternal, forever and ever.**

I conclude with a blessing of *mazal tov* on the entry of your grandson, Shneur Zalman, may he live, into the covenant of our father Avraham, peace be upon him. May his father and mother, as well as his grandparents, may they live, merit to see from him and from the rest of their offspring, may they live, *Yiddishe nachas* and *Chassidishe nachas*, in abundance.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7812

15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, Rabbi Yaakov Yehuda Hecht, in which he also writes to me what you told him regarding your past... and also about writing a *Sefer Torah* in your name and sending it to Eretz Yisrael, and you ask for my opinion on this.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize the holiness and greatness of a *Sefer Torah*. However, there is that which is even holier than a *Sefer Torah*, and that is the Jewish people who study the Torah. Especially in Eretz Yisrael at this present moment, where thousands of Jewish children have arrived who are in need of an education in Torah and *mitzvos*, so that they may know what Yiddishkeit is—*shmiras Shabbos*, kashrus, and so on. Unfortunately, the number of existing *yeshivos* and *chadorim* is too small to accommodate all these arriving Jewish children. Day after day, heart-rending letters arrive from there regarding this. With a relatively small sum, one could save thousands of Jewish children from being torn away, *chas v'shalom*, from the Jewish people, and ensure they remain Torah-true Jews forever.

The same is true in North Africa, where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zi"a*, commanded a short time before his *histalkus* to organize *chadorim* and *yeshivos* there to teach the local Jewish children Torah and *yiras shamayim*, and financial resources are needed for this.

Therefore, my advice is as follows: Since there is currently no shortage of *Sifrei Torah* in Eretz Yisrael (they have been brought from European countries), whereas money to support *melamdim* and to purchase *Siddurim*, *Chumashim*, and similar *seforim* is very necessary both in Eretz Yisrael and in North Africa—it is my opinion that since you have the good intention to write a *Sefer Torah*, but have **not yet** decided and are asking for my opinion, you should inquire as to how much it would cost to write such a *Sefer Torah*. You should then donate that sum, with an additional dollar, toward establishing another *cheder* or *Talmud Torah* in Eretz Yisrael and in North Africa, and also send them *Siddurim*. On these *Siddurim*, it will be printed that those who use them should pray and mention for the good the donors—you and your husband, *shichyu*.

The magnitude of the *zechus* that you will have through this is difficult to convey in words, especially in a letter, but I hope that you will grasp from my writing the importance of this. May Hashem help you to completely rectify your past, and from today onward, may you have a good Jewish life according to Torah and *mitzvos*.

With blessings.

## 7,903

7,903

B"H, 1 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 22 Shevat. Through *Hashgacha Pratis*, it arrived on Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, a few hours before I traveled to the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*. I read your letter at the *tziyun*, and surely my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will awaken compassion for you regarding the matters you mention. A *tzaddik* decrees and *Hashem* fulfills, especially a *tzaddik* who has departed, regarding whom the *Zohar* states that he is found in all worlds even more than during his lifetime—and especially since you were privileged to receive a blessing from my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It is understood and simple that in order to receive and sustain the blessings of *Hashem*—who gives His blessing with desire and from His full and expansive hand—a person must create broad vessels suitable for this. Therefore, you will surely do the same: namely, you will fulfill the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—if you have received such instructions—and you will also strive to fulfill the *shiurim* that are appropriate for every person, as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe: 1) A *shiur* of *Tehillim* (as divided for the days of the month) every day after *davening* *Shacharis*; 2) Studying the *parsha* of the *Chumash* with the commentary of *Rashi* for the weekly *sedra*; 3) A *shiur* in *Tanya* as divided for the days of the year.

Since you are involved in construction matters, and regarding the *inyana d'yoma* (the matters of the day), it is known from our Sages (end of *Taanis*) that "when Adar enters, we increase in joy." See the *sugya* there, which discusses buildings of joy. May it be the will of *Hashem* that your buildings also draw down joy into your home, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

From the Secretariat copy.

## 7804

7804

B.H., 6 Adar, 5712

Mr. Z. Altein, may he live and be well.

Your letter of January 27th has been received. I was very pleased to read that you have settled into the Chabad library, and I am confident that you will be satisfied and that this will bring you success, both in spiritual and material matters.

I am certain—especially as I recall your father, of blessed memory, whom I knew well—that your current situation, living in Kfar Chabad, aligns with your father’s intentions and wishes, as well as with the character traits you inherited from him.

You may always write to me in whichever language is more comfortable for you, for the importance lies not in the language in which one writes, but in the content of the letter—as language is merely the external wrapping.

I hope that in your next letter you will write to me in greater detail regarding your daily schedule, both concerning your work and regarding your Torah classes and studies.

Wishing you a good settlement in material and spiritual matters, and success in them.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7805

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

1) I received your Pidyon Nefesh. When I was at the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on Erev Rosh Chodesh Nissan, I read it, and surely it will arouse Divine mercy for all those mentioned in your letter regarding what they need.

2) You have surely already received the Kuntres for 2 Nissan via the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc. [name], together with the regards, etc. I await good news from you regarding all matters.

3) Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the upcoming Yom Tov, which I am sure you will publicize in an appropriate manner.

4) Last but not least, my request is doubled and tripled: that you, may you live, arrange your general and specific affairs in such a way that you can travel to Yeshivas Toras Emes in Yerushalayim, may it be rebuilt and established, once a week or every two weeks, in order to speak and study Chassidus in an appropriate manner with the avreichim and bochurim, to test them from time to time, and also to farbreng with them—naturally, not every time you go there, but approximately once a month.

I have also written regarding this to Yeshivas Toras Emes, and my hope is strong that they will agree to this.

I rely on your understanding that you will arrange this matter in such a way that it does not cause a decline in the spirit of the mashpia of Chassidus at Toras Emes, nor a lowering of his prestige in the eyes of the avreichim and bochurim, etc. You will surely be able to explain that since you are "new faces," sometimes the novelty—because it is cherished—is more effective, etc.

I spoke about this with the esteemed Chossid [name] while he was here, and I rely on you and on the esteemed Chossid [name] to arrange these matters in such a way that there will be no obstacle in this regard from the administration of the Lod Yeshiva either.

All of the above is also consistent with my proposal from some time ago: that after the students have "finished" (if it is possible to speak of a finish in the study of Torah), their aspiration should be regarding the study of Chassidus, to flourish in this study by entering the Lod Yeshiva. Therefore, as a preparation for this, your visits from time to time to Yeshivas Toras Emes will also serve a purpose.

I await good news regarding the arrangement of this matter, and the main thing is that it should be in a spirit of peace and in a manner of "brothers dwelling together."

With blessings for success in influencing a spirit of fear of Heaven during this time of "food of faith" and "food of healing" for all those you influence.

## 7806

B"H, 4th day of Chol Hamoed Pesach, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily:

Shalom and Bracha!

You are surely aware of and acquainted with our most esteemed friend, the G-d-fearing, Torah-observant, and honest businessman who has supported our holy institutions for many years, R' Yaakov Cohen Katz of Chicago. Since his father is currently in Eretz Yisrael and is in need of an apartment to live in, I request that you make an effort to find him a suitable apartment as soon as possible. Please speak with him; perhaps he already has a location in mind where he would like to live—I believe it is in Bnei Brak. In time, his father will certainly pay the expenses involved, little by little. Until he pays the full amount of the expenses incurred in securing the apartment, I suggest that you register the apartment in the name of Agudas Chasidei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael.

I hope that you will continue your efforts to secure the apartment for him, as according to the information I have, he is currently in uncomfortable conditions. Thank you in advance for your efforts in this matter, and I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding what you have accomplished for the best, as soon as possible.

With blessings for success in your holy work and a kosher and happy Pesach.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed this personally, and I sign on his behalf,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 7808

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, Rabbi Shmuel, Shochet and Bodek, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, for which the reply has been delayed until now for several reasons:

1) You describe your situation regarding *shechitah*, which has been decreasing lately, and that you are now working on a trial basis as a secretary at Agudas Chassidei Chabad in Tel Aviv. You ask for my opinion on whether to accept the job or wait until something easier comes along.

In my opinion, it is not worth waiting, for it is a pity to waste time while lacking work and activity. If *anash* have found that you are suitable for this work, then on the contrary, you should engage in it, as our Sages of blessed memory instructed us in such matters: "Seize and eat, seize and drink." That is to say, you should work at this with alacrity and fulfill your part in the organization of *anash*, for ultimately, the *maayanos* are spread outward through this, which will surely also serve as a vessel for increasing and drawing down success in your personal affairs.

2) You write regarding your son, Yechiel Yehuda, may he live, who has been placed in the Military Rabbinate, and you ask for my opinion on whether he should pursue a position of greater responsibility.

This is a very proper thing. May it be His will that it be with success. Surely you are using your influence on your son, may he live, to increase the light of "the candle of Hashem is the soul of man" that is within him. Especially since through this, he will also be able to see fruits among those he influences within the army, where the influence of *yiras shamayim* is needed more and more, with great energy and with words that come from the heart. As it is written, he should be a holy educator, as is brought regarding the matter of the "beautiful captive," etc.

Please convey my regards to your son, Yechiel Yehuda, may he live, and give him my blessing: that the *Ribono shel Olam* should grant him the merit to utilize the powers hidden within him—the heritage of his fathers from the lineage of *anash*—to bring them into action and to influence his entire environment with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of Torah"—this is the *Toras HaChassidus*.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7809

[2 Iyar 5712]

B"H,

Our Sages of blessed memory stated: "It was in the merit of the righteous women of that generation (of the Exodus from Egypt) that the Jewish people were redeemed from Egypt." They explain and recount at length how, despite the yoke of exile, the harshness of the servitude, and the decrees, they raised flock after flock of Jewish sons and daughters; they raised a generation that proclaimed with joy, song, and melody: "This is my G-d and I will glorify Him, the G-d of my father and I will exalt Him."

Hashem has promised us: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," in the future redemption that will come speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. "All the signs, miracles, and mighty deeds that the Holy One, blessed be He, performed in Egypt, He will perform for Israel," and "through the merit of the children of the house of the Rebbe, the strength will be fortified to prevail," for King Moshiach.

And just as it was then, so too now, it depends on the women of Israel. As is explained in the sicha, the fate of the sons and daughters lies in their hands.

The role, the obligation, and the privilege of the women of Israel is that, without fear of the darkness of the exile, the harshness of the servitude, and the decrees that seek to submerge—Heaven forbid—the souls of our sons and daughters in structures foreign to the spirit of the elders of Israel, opposing the faith of Hashem Echad, who gives—in the present tense—one Torah to one nation in the land,

They must make their homes a **house of holiness** for His Name, may He be blessed, and establish the education of their sons and daughters upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

And then, "Imma Ila'ah will be aroused... and King Moshiach will **begin** and gather the exiles from one end of the world to the other."

**Menachem Schneerson**

Tiferes sheb'Tiferes, 5712. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 7811

7811

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Vaad of Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Nissan, I was pleased to read that your efforts to ensure they remain in their place have succeeded, and consequently, you will all be together. Surely, even if it is not explicitly written as such, you will retain all the rights that were promised to you at the time you settled in Kfar Chabad.

2) The time has already come to make an effort to increase the number of settlers in the village from among the rest of anash and those close to anash in spirit who are located in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. This applies especially to young married couples, and also to the youth who, for various reasons, are not able to study all day in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, but whom it is possible to obligate and grant the merit of studying for several hours and living in a Chassidic Chabad environment throughout the entire day and night. In connection with the housing shortage currently prevailing in Eretz Yisrael, it is to be hoped that you will have the choice to select the best among those who wish to settle in the village...

5) ...Whether we wish it or not, we are filling the place of the Chassidim of Chabad of the generations before us, and before them, all the way back to the "generation of knowledge" of the Chassidim of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad teachings. Generation after generation paved the way for us, and nothing remains for us but to complete the "small vessels."

On the other hand, the duty is incumbent upon us and our generation to complete the *birurim* of *ikvesa d'meshicha* and to draw down the revelation of Mashiach to below ten *tefachim* in this physical world.

Even with a brief contemplation of these matters, one must be seized with trembling and fear, for all the awesome matters stated in the words of our Sages regarding Mashiach and the revelations of that time—and especially as explained in *Chassidus*—all of this depends upon our own *avodah*.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, may Hashem grant you the merit that you should fulfill [this] not only in the *nefesh ha'elokis*, but also with the human intellect with which Hashem has granted you the merit to be among those assisting in the work of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in building the *heichal* of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

Awaiting good tidings and celebrations.

## 7811

7811

B”H, 11 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Yeshiva in Lod,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have just received word that the distribution of the 100,000 (francs or dollars) is being handled in the following manner: ...

I was alarmed by this news, for it is not enough that they initially allocated a paltry sum of 5,000, but they have now reduced it even further, to 4,000!

Some say the argument is that the number of Yemenite children in Lod is small. There are three points to be made regarding this:

1. I am alarmed and astonished that although I have appealed to their hearts several times to absorb more and more Yemenite children, it seems to have been a voice in the wilderness.

2. I do not know the extent of the absorption of Yemenite children in the other institutions that were allocated disproportionately larger sums.

3. And this is the main point: the aforementioned sums were allocated not only for the children already in the institutions, but primarily to enable their absorption in the future. Consequently, the initial argument is entirely misplaced.

In practice, you will surely take all necessary measures immediately to rectify this matter, and you will do so with the appropriate vigor and without any procrastination or negligence...

Awaiting good news,

#### ***7811***

From a copy.

**To 4,000:** See below, letter 7815.

## 7813

## 7814

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Simcha Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write that through the esteemed and distinguished R' Meir Blizinsky, may he live, you have become acquainted with Chassidus Chabad and have begun to study the teachings of Chassidus, and you ask to be counted among the community of Chassidim of Chabad.

All of the above has given me great pleasure. It is written in the holy seforim that when a Jew wishes to conduct himself in a good path in truth, Hashem helps him. This is especially true regarding a matter connected to Torah, of which it is said, "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him." This applies all the more so to the teachings of Chassidus, which in our current times of double and redoubled galus are very necessary—matters that lead to ahavas Hashem, yiras Hashem, and to "serve Hashem with joy," all of which are the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus.

I hope that in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, who said that "we elevate in matters of holiness... and whoever adds, they add to him," you will also increase your shiurim in Torah in general and in the teachings of Chassidus in particular. You should also see to it that you participate in Chassidic gatherings—both gatherings for study and a farbrengen of Chassidim—which should strengthen ahavas Yisroel, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Hashem. All of this will give you an added vitality in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim.

You surely know about the three daily shiurim that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, instituted for all Jews—the daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should keep them.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

#### ***7814***

From a photocopy of the letter.

R' Simcha Meir: Weinman, Ramat Gan.

## 7915

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of 21 Iyar has been received. Although in my opinion it would have been possible to enter into a discussion with Mr. Kohl regarding the meager support provided to them—and even that only as a loan, in the sum of 4,000 Israeli Lira—it seems that now it makes no difference, as the sum has already been distributed. In any event, regarding the future, you will surely stand on guard to be informed in good time regarding them and their support, so that it will be possible to anticipate matters and receive appropriate support from them.

2) In accordance with this, I have once again come with the note to hasten the matter of the vocational school as much as possible. It is a pity that I do not have further information on this, because Dr. Shapiro, whose opinion will apparently be decisive in this matter, is currently in the United States and will return to France in about a week or two. While he is here, it would have been possible to influence him, had I possessed further information on the subject.

3) I was very pleased with what you reported, at least in part, regarding the trip to Meron on Lag B'Omer, and the travelers will surely follow up with detailed letters.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for success in your holy work, to increase Torah and glorify it, as requested by our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory, to connect the Torah from above with the Holy One, Blessed be He,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7816

7816

B"H, 16 [Sivan], 5712

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [Chossid], R' Meir, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

... Surely you are striving to influence your surroundings as well, to bring them closer to the ways of Chassidus and its customs. It is well known what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, related regarding the statement of our Alter Rebbe concerning the immense *nachas ruach* Above when one strives for the benefit of his fellow. If this is true when striving for the material benefit of one's fellow, then how much more so when striving for the spiritual benefit of one's fellow, through which one brings him to the life of this world and the World to Come. For in the Jewish person, these are interconnected and united with one another, to the point that they have become as one.

With blessings.
