## 7817

7817

B"H, 16 Sivan 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Avraham, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It gives me pleasure to hear from time to time reports of you, and of your work for the matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and for the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Montreal in particular. It is well known the statement of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his father, that "the Holy One, blessed be He, does not remain a debtor." Those who exert themselves and provide Jewish children—and all Jews are the only children of Hashem—with vitality, both physically and spiritually, by giving them the opportunity to study the Torah of Hashem, Hashem gives them additional vitality, quite simply in good health and success in their affairs, both communal and personal. And that which Rabbeinu HaZaken said—as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—is fulfilled in them: that Hashem gives Jews gashmius, and they transform that gashmius into ruchnius.

May Hashem assist you with long days and good years, good in every respect, and may you be able to continue your work, and to an even greater extent, for the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Montreal in particular, and for the raising of the horn of Yisroel in general.

With blessing,

#### ***7817***

## 7818

7818

May they live,

...Since the histalkus, it is evident in general how all matters conducted in his spirit succeed in a manner that is above nature...

I will reiterate my words, that it is not my intention at all to cause a falling or lowering of spirits, but only that from here on in, the mind should rule over the heart, even regarding excitement and hispaalus of holiness. I look forward to your letter bringing good news that the avodah is being conducted in an orderly fashion, and specifically regarding the development of the mosdos.

## 7819

7819

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

Soon, the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, Rabbi Shalom Haskind, may he live, will arrive in Eretz Yisrael. It is my wish that he visit all the institutions, camps, ma'abarot, and so on. I have two intentions in this: a) That his visit be utilized for the purpose of raising morale, as he comes from the U.S. and speaks English, etc., and also for the purpose of "instilling fear" [i.e., exerting necessary pressure] where such pressure is required. It is therefore appropriate to arrange for him to visit all relevant institutions (and not only our own), as well as the Chief Rabbis, etc. Surely you will also provide the appropriate publicity in the newspapers, and all the more so regarding the enclosed excerpt.

2. I have received information that there is a mikveh in Haifa founded by the late Rabbi M.M. Kuperstock, which is now in the possession of his descendants, may they live. However, due to several reasons, there are difficulties in its usage, and this depends on exerting influence upon the sons of the aforementioned Rabbi. If this is not done, there is room for concern regarding a chillul Hashem for Lubavitch.

I do not know the details of the matter, and surely it makes little difference, as you are on the spot and certainly know the situation. If there is any possibility, it is proper that you speak with the sons of the Rabbi regarding the above and endeavor to rectify the matter in every possible way.

3. I have received a request stating that a mikveh is being built in Ramat Hadar, Netzach Yisrael, Ramatayim, and these are the names of those involved [...]. The sum of approximately two hundred Lira is lacking for its completion. The location is a place where Charedi Jews reside, who will surely use the mikveh once it is completed. If all the above is true, it is very proper that you provide them with the aforementioned sum, provided that it is used in the most appropriate manner. Surely Menachem, son of the Rabbi of Yekaterinoslav, will take this upon himself, but it is not advisable to wait; they should simply inform him afterward that they have acted as stated.

4. I have received a request from my relative, R' Avraham Dovid Yanovsky, may he live, whose wife's state of health—according to the doctors' instructions—requires more comfortable housing, and they lack the means for this. It seems to me that the aforementioned Menachem should take this upon himself as well, up to a sum of one thousand Lira, if R' A.D. finds suitable housing.

5. I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from 17 Iyar and the minutes of the meetings from the 9th, 25th, and 27th of Iyar, and the 9th of Sivan.

6. Surely you are receiving the twelve thousand Lira for construction from the Jewish Agency. I am interested to know what is being done with them.

7. What is the final outcome of the Shmittah project?

8. Rabbi Goldman proposed founding a school in the Jerusalem corridor. What has been done regarding this?

With the blessing of success in the Holy Land.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7820

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Michael
Shy'

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 4th of Tammuz, along with the enclosed list of students, as well as your previous letters. G-d willing, I will mention them at an auspicious time at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the matter of the mikvaos that were constructed there using tap water—and as it appears from your letter, your intention is straightforward, that they are using water that comes from the "vodaprovod" (water mains)—you should, without causing a stir, gradually change them. Either to a mikvah of rainwater, or if there is no rainwater in your location, perhaps it is possible to obtain artificial ice, or by drawing water from a spring.

The Kuntres for the Chag HaGeulah of 12-13 Tammuz, which is approaching, has surely reached you by now. You should organize the celebration with appropriate publicity, including the participation of the local residents, and utilize this for practical matters, for "action is the essential thing."

With blessings for success in communal and personal matters, and with blessings for the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7823

7823

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, etc., R' Naftali, Shochet and Bodek, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from 1 Re'eh and the one preceding it, and I ask your forgiveness that due to the great pressure of work, I have not acknowledged their receipt until now.

I was pleased by your interest in the state of the matters of Shechita in our camp, although I was very distressed by the events and matters that are not as they should be, which you mention in your letter. It seems that your intention in this is regarding the Shulchan Aruch.

Surely these days will be an opportunity to speak with a few more of Anash who are able to intervene in this, and my hope is that it will eventually succeed in rectifying the situation little by little. It is understood, of course, that I will not mention that the initial report came from you. May Hashem grant you success in your learning and in your holy work without any stumbling block, G-d forbid. It is also known what our Sages of blessed memory explained: "There is no 'slaughtering' (shechitah) except 'drawing' (meshech)," which means that just as, according to the simple meaning, the purpose of Shechita is to render the meat of the animal or bird fit for consumption, raising them from the level of "living" (chai) to the level of "speaking" (medaber)—since it becomes the blood and flesh of the human—so too, one should perform this matter in a spiritual sense: to draw down and elevate the animal soul to the level of "Adam" (man), which is related to "I will be like the Most High" (adameh l'elyon). This is as written in the Shelah, page 7b, and it is in the book Asarah Maamaros, Maamar Em Kol Chai, Part 2, Chapter 33.

With blessings for a good inscription and sealing for you and all your family, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7823***

From a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Naftali:** Unik. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 20, 7772, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 7927

7927

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Schneur Zalman HaLevi,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I have just received your two letters dated the 15th and 19th of Cheshvan, in which you write regarding your various thoughts concerning your relocation—whether to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) or to Canada—noting the various difficulties and advantages of each.

As is evident from your letters, the matter is not yet clear even to you, regarding the capacity you and your family (may they live) have for moving from your current location to Eretz Yisrael or to Canada. Therefore, my opinion is that you should assemble three of your friends from among the elders of Anash in your current location, and present the entire matter to them as it stands at that time. The Ribono shel Olam will grant them the correct insight to advise you in a way that is good for you and your family (may they live) both materially and spiritually. Follow their guidance, and it will be successful.

With blessings for an easy relocation—and one that is appropriate in both body and soul,

**M. Schneersohn**

## 7828

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Shmuel Zanvil, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter from the 2nd of Chayei Sarah, in which you ask for a blessing regarding the difficulty you have falling asleep and the fear you experience, and you ask for my opinion on the matter.

In my opinion, you should completely divert your attention from this. You should see to it, as soon as possible, to have your tefillin, tzitzis, and also the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Furthermore, you should take upon yourself—without a vow—to observe the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to recite a portion of Tehillim every day after davening in the morning—as the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month—and to give a coin to tzedakah every weekday before davening in the morning. Also, ensure that not a day goes by without you studying at least a few verses of Chumash from the weekly parsha and some study of Torah Shebe'al Peh that you find enjoyable. I hope that if you consult with Anash of Lubavitch, they will give you good advice on this.

One must know by heart some Torah, at the very least a few chapters of Tehillim or Mishnayos. Whenever you feel any fear or an unhappy thought, you should at that moment recite a chapter of Tehillim or some Mishnayos that you know by heart. You will certainly feel better then, and I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding this.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary

**Menachem Schneerson**

...Thank you, thank you for informing me regarding the health of the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, etc., Rabbi Shneur Zalman, may he live, Bezpalov. And may Hashem fulfill the pregnancy of your wife, may she live, properly and easily, and may she give birth to a healthy child properly and easily.

With blessings, awaiting good news,

M. Schneerson

P.S. I have not heard of any special customs for the day of the haircutting. Copied here is an excerpt from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this:

...Regarding the cutting of the hair—*upsherinish*—it is a significant matter in Jewish custom, and its essence lies in the education of leaving the *pe'os* of the head. From the day of the haircutting and the leaving of the *pe'os* of the head, it is customary to be diligent in accustoming the child to wearing *tzitzis katan*, reciting the morning blessings, Grace After Meals, and the *Shema* before retiring to bed.

May Hashem be their help that they raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with an expanded livelihood and peace of mind, both materially and spiritually.

## 7,934

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

I am deeply saddened and concerned by the lack of proper organization at the Yeshiva in Tel Aviv, despite the discussions and exchange of letters that have taken place from here to there and from there to here. I do not know what measures to take so that the institution of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may be in accordance with his will—namely, that all who participate in it, including the administration, the teachers, the Rosh Yeshiva, and the students, should understand that they are shluchim of the founder, to illuminate their portion of the world through this institution. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With blessings for true health and for an abundance of Chassidishe nachas from all your children, together with your wife, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

I have now received your letters from the 17th and 20th of Kislev, along with the pidyon nefesh, which I will read at the holy gravesite. Thank you for your brief report regarding the 19th of Kislev. It is worth looking calmly for a position that is easier for him.

## 7835

B"H, the fifth night of Chanukah, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the entire congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

The "Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim-Lubavitch," whose work and development in the United States began through my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and under his instruction immediately upon his arrival in America in the year 5700, has—thank G-d, and through the merit of our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory—borne fruit with extraordinary divine success. Today, many hundreds of students—may they increase—from these yeshivos serve with distinction as Rabbis, heads of yeshivos, shochtim, and in other holy positions in important communities in Israel. Even those students and alumni of Tomchei Tmimim who earn their livelihood in other ways remain at their post in the holy service, working, each according to his status and situation, in the field of spreading Torah and yiras shamayim, and taking a leading role in the efforts to strengthen Yiddishkeit in all their places of residence.

Together with the growth and flourishing of the institution, the expenses involved in its maintenance in all its branches have also grown, to the point that recently, debts have multiplied and risen to an alarming level, shaking the very existence of the institution and making its management and development extremely difficult.

Substantial assistance is needed as soon as possible.

I am therefore turning to all lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos with a double and redoubled request to come to the aid of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim-Lubavitch, to contribute a holy donation with a generous heart and an open hand, and to influence their friends and acquaintances in this direction as well, in order to lighten, at least to some degree, the burden of the debts and to provide the possibility to conduct the work of the institution in the future, with Hashem’s help.

We are assured by our Sages that the merit of supporting those who study the Torah of life, the words of the living G-d, the source of life, is great—to protect all those who act and contribute, and that they will be blessed with all the best, with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With wishes and blessings that in our near future we will all merit to see the raising of the horn of Torah and the horn of the Jewish people, and that the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem.

With regards and blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

From a photocopy of the letter.

## 7,336

B"H, 5 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To our masters and teachers, the Rabbis and Geonim who sit in judgment, each in his camp and community; the communal activists engaged in raising the banner of Torah and Yiddishkeit in the spirit of our ancestors; and to all our brethren, the children of Israel, who cherish Torah and mitzvos, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life.

He will convey to them my greetings and regards, and bring back their regards to me; to learn of the state of Yiddishkeit and the standing of the Torah and educational institutions in their respective camps; to encourage that which requires repair and strengthening in accordance with the spirit of our ancestors; and to explain the status of our institutions in this country, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, in Europe, and in Africa.

Relying on the verse, "I sleep, but my heart is awake," and based on the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that even in exile the heart of Israel is awake to every good thing—and there is no "good" other than Torah, mitzvos, and good deeds—I am certain that you will assist him in fulfilling the mission successfully, as well as in matters regarding the strengthening of our institutions in the aforementioned locations.

May the Ribono shel Olam enable each and every one of us to fulfill our role in this world by illuminating our surroundings and our portion of the world with the light and radiance of Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael.

With respect and with blessings for material and spiritual good,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7737

7737

B"H, 15 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Saadya, may he live, Shadar [emissary].

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter with the lists in due time. You have surely already received the receipts from the office. I have now received your notification that the visa for Morocco is in your possession.

Regarding your question about the method of travel and the details involved, you should speak with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi B.A. Gorodetzky, may he live. If it is possible to arrange, during your visit to Madrid, your travel route in a way that relates to the kashrus of the students there, then it may be worthwhile for you to travel via that route. However, if this matter is not practically relevant, you may travel either by plane—in accordance with the opinion of the doctor who will examine your health condition—or by ship.

Regarding the location where you will organize your work, as well as the terms of your work, it is well known how much our Nesi’im in general, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in particular, emphasized the importance of order in every single matter. Therefore, you should speak in Paris with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi B.A. Gorodetzky, may he live, who is in contact with both the representatives of the Joint and with Anash, may they live, who are already on-site, to arrange all matters in the most effective manner for the work, which is, in any case, also the best way for each of the workers. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to fulfill our role with true ease and expansion.

With blessings for success in your holy work, I await good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,338

B"H, 17 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established,

This certainly requires attention even after the month of Kislev and the connection made then, whether through letters or through face-to-face meetings from time to time, in every place and location according to its particular circumstances.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 7,939

B"H, 18 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn

1) Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in the health of Mr. Yisroel Henkin, may he live. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, his condition will have improved even further; please share good news regarding this. Likewise, if you are aware of the doctors' professional opinion and the methods of treatment, please inform me.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the rationale for striving to enhance the quality of the Achi Temimim Yeshiva in Pittsburgh so that it would also be suitable for the students Feigenson and Garber, may they live, who have now arrived from France: It seems to me that between the students currently there and the students who arrived from France, there are still several grade levels missing in between, and therefore it is difficult for them to be in one continuous track. Primarily, I do not see how you would be able to find mashpiim in Chassidus and Rosh Yeshivas suitable for the students from France, especially since there are only a few of them. If you have hope (an *oisskuk*) that it is possible to obtain such mashpiim and Rosh Yeshivas, at least over time, perhaps it would be worthwhile to inquire whether this is feasible both in terms of the expenses involved and the individuals themselves. If so, it is not far-fetched that for the coming year there would be room to consider this, as by that time the graduating class currently in the yeshiva will also have grown. However, to begin this in the middle of the term, on the face of it, is not advisable.

3) I would be interested to know in detail, as far as you are aware, the material situation of Mr...

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7840

7840

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5713

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all those gathered and participating in the thirteenth annual United States celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I warmly greet all those gathered and participating in today’s annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, and I address each one of you with the expression of blessing sanctified by the custom of Israel, which is Torah:

**Baruch HaBa B’Shem Hashem!**

American Jews must offer praise and thanksgiving to the Ribono shel Olam for the merit they have attained: that thirteen years ago, upon his arrival here, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, immediately planted the unique Divine vineyard, Kerem Hashem Tzevaos, the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, on American soil as well.

Today, as we take stock of thirteen years of tireless, mesiras nefesh-filled work by the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim here in this country, all those who see and evaluate matters according to their true, inner content and value are convinced of the great Divine blessing that the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch—with their many hundreds of students who are yirei shamayim and shleimim, devoted and dedicated to Hashem and His holy Torah—have brought into Jewish life in America. The model of mesiras nefesh of the students and those being educated, and their profound influence on Jewish communal and private life, is a universally recognized fact.

We all see clearly how, before our very eyes, the great, holy mission that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, set for himself upon his arrival in America—and which he announced on several occasions—is being realized more and more each day. This is:

**To make America a makom Torah b’yiras shamayim!**

And the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch have a great and significant share in the fulfillment of, and the drawing closer to, this goal.

Therefore, at this time, when the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch is experiencing a most serious financial crisis, which puts the existing institutions in danger and, naturally, hinders the absolutely necessary expansion and increase in the number of yeshivos,

American Jews, and especially all those gathered here, must be permeated with the awareness that it is their holy obligation to make the greatest efforts to provide maximum assistance to the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, in order to cover their large deficit and provide the possibility to continue the work of harbotzas Torah b’yiras shamayim, and to make America a makom Torah u’yiras shamayim.

I hope that all those gathered, and each one of them, will strive at today’s gathering to contribute the maximum amount themselves, and also help ensure that the necessary sum expected by the administration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch is raised immediately.

And the zechus of tzedakah in general, and in particular tzedakah that is connected with chinuch hakasher, the strengthening of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and yiras shamayim,

Will draw down and bring to the participants, they, their households, and their families, may they live, blessing and success in all that they need—in children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***7840***

From a photocopy of the letter.

## 7842

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Not long ago, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov, conveyed to me your question regarding the medical tests. It is a well-known saying that we have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: "As one asks, so is one answered."

Although it is truly astonishing that after having witnessed the wonders of Hashem—even with physical eyes—new doubts arise from time to time regarding the possibility of performing tests, or perhaps sending your daughter (may she live and be well) to another doctor so that he may learn his craft and wisdom, etc., nevertheless, since this very question indicates a weakness in *bitachon*, it is possible that the path regarding your daughter (may she live and be well) must be to proceed by consulting with doctors, for there is none among us who knows the wonders of the Perfect Knower, blessed and exalted be He.

May it be the will of Hashem that whatever you decide, it should be for success and for the strengthening of the health of your daughter (may she live and be well), and may you raise her to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, with peace of mind.

May Hashem help each and every one of us so that we are not "like dreamers," even according to what is explained in *Torah Ohr*—that at the time of *hiskashrus*, it is a true *hiskashrus*—and certainly according to what is explained in the *maamar* regarding the concept that "the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures," which refers to a lower level than that.

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 17 Teves and 4 Shevat, along with your opinion regarding the students. Thank you, thank you for this, although I am not satisfied that you did not send your opinion regarding the [matter of the]... for it seems that in this instance, the failure to send an opinion is, in itself, an opinion. And it should not have been in such a manner—it does not align with the instruction of our *Nasi* regarding the concept of *ahavas Yisroel*, and that the other person is like a mirror; consequently, if one sees a flaw in him, it is very likely that, as the saying goes, "one’s own flaw is being reflected."

Regarding the above, I am writing separately and more sharply, and therefore I hope that you will not take offense at this letter.

With blessings for the strengthening of *hiskashrus*, especially for the upcoming *Yom HaHillula*, and with blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal matters,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published recently. Also, the *Sefer Maamarim 5703* has been sent to you separately.

## 7843

7843

2, 5, 6 Shevat, 5713

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi... may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

With satisfaction and joy, I received your letter which you began writing on 19 Teves, in which you describe how the month of Tishrei and the time following it passed.

I am extremely pleased to see that you have convinced yourself of the achievements regarding the *Sifrei Chassidus*, and I am certain that this will serve as a *mussar haskel* for you: that every Jew is a *shaliach* of the *Ribono shel Olam*. Even when it seems to him that he is weak in his physical or spiritual powers, this is only because he momentarily forgets that he is a *shaliach* of the *Ribono shel Olam*, whose powers are *ein sof* and *bli gevul*. But when he remembers that he is a *shaliach* of the *Ribono shel Olam*, this brings him *hatzlacha* and also brings health, literally, in the physical sense.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you the merit of further good *shlichus* for long days and years, and may you carry them out with *simcha* and in a better state of health, and may you be able to report good tidings regarding the condition of your wife, *tichyeh*.

After Shabbos — Monday, 10 Shevat — is the *yahrzeit* of my father-in-law, the *Admur* *ztzukullehah nbgm zie*. In accordance with your request, I will mention you and your wife, *tichyeh*, and enclosed is a short biography in Yiddish which was recently published, and which will also be useful to you in your *hashpaah* among your surroundings.

With blessings for a speedy recovery for him and his wife, *shichyu*, and for proper health.

Awaiting good tidings.

## 7944

7944

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5713

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letter from 27 Teves, and I was happy to read that the wedding arrangements for... are progressing.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the participation of anash, may they live, and as is well known, when one performs a mitzvah, the one who caused that mitzvah to be performed also shares in it. This is especially true in matters of giving and receiving—both in spiritual and material affairs—where the recipient does more for the giver than the giver does for the recipient.

Surely you have also read in the *Sefer HaZichronos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, how the youths would make a practice of giving *gemach* to one another, so that the giver would merit the mitzvah of *gemach* and the recipient would merit the mitzvah of repaying a debt. This is especially relevant regarding the matter of marriage, as it is known how highly Chazal spoke of all the details connected to this.

In continuation of this, I, too, will take the liberty of participating in the wedding expenses by way of the enclosed scrip...

With blessings for *mazal tov*.

## 7946

7946

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Yisroel Noach, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Va’eira, and today I also received the Pidyon Nefesh from the residents of Prima, which I will read, bli neder, when I am at the holy Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the trip to Eretz Yisroel, may it be rebuilt and established, and your request for an urgent reply—while beginning your letter by stating that in your opinion, it is a correct rationale for you to travel to Eretz Yisroel:

It seems to me that in my aforementioned letter, I also wrote that you must take into account that in your current location, you are taking an **active** part in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of Yisroel. This is not the case in Eretz Yisroel, etc., etc. Furthermore, according to the information received from there now, it is even more so than in the past—that naturally speaking, it does not appear that you would have such an opportunity there. It is surprising that in this letter, you do not mention anything regarding this fundamental and essential point.

Regarding your question of whether to travel in the month of Adar or afterwards—based on the above, it is understood that any delay is for the good. May Hashem grant you the correct thought to decide and act in the way that is best before Him, and consequently, also for your wife, may she live and be well, who is like your own self, with goodness—both physically and spiritually alike.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7747

7747

B"H, 16 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Chana, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

Regarding what you write in your letter—that you are disappointed and have therefore stopped working on the matter of Taharas HaMishpacha—this is certainly not a sufficient reason. Since Hashem is willing to deal with each one of us many times over and, G-d forbid, does not become "disappointed," this should serve as a lesson for us not to become weary of drawing Jews—men and women, young and old—closer to Torah and mitzvos through every possible means. We are assured that if one acts with seriousness and with a sincere will, then, in the end, whether a little sooner or a little later, one will succeed.

Regarding what you write about the mikveh in your city, I am surprised that none of the young people who have been to see me, including your husband, mentioned this to me. I will see to it at the first opportunity to find out the state of affairs regarding this.

With blessings for Chassidishe nachas from all her children, together with her husband, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7951

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Avraham, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from 17 Teves and 9 Shevat, as well as the list of students from Tomchei Temimim who received Chanukah gelt, and also the Pidyon Nefesh for 10 Shevat.

... 3) After all the letters received, I still do not see any clear direction regarding what is to be done about the efforts concerning the children whom the missionaries are enticing. It seems that, for the time being, this remains between one group of Anash and another, and consequently, no one is actually dealing with it. For, as I have written for various reasons, it is impossible for this to be officially connected to the Reshet, and certainly not to the Yeshiva in Lod. But, on the other hand, since they promised me almost officially that if it were done in the appropriate manner—regarding the building and the pedagogy—they would cover almost the entire expense, it is a pity not to utilize this opportunity. And the magnitude of this matter in terms of spirituality is beyond estimation or calculation.

... 5) Regarding the farming in the village, this is also distressing. According to reports, there are those there who have no connection to farming and are not even thinking about it, yet they have registered on the list of farmers in the hope that perhaps they might gain something from it, even though this will cause damage to the true farmers...

With blessings for Chassidishe nachas from all your offspring, and from yourself—certainly—for good health and the greatest merit to bring only good tidings, signed with respect...

Regarding the publication of the maamarim and what was discussed at the farbrengen, all of this depends on a lack of time.

#### ***7951***

Published in the booklet "Tzadik L'Melech," section 121.

## 7853

By the Grace of G-d
25 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in the work of the Rebbe, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. [Matusov], may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

For the sake of order, I hereby acknowledge once again the receipt of your letters from the 1st of Teves, the 10th, 22nd, and 29th of Teves, and the 7th, 10th, 16th, and 20th of Shevat, along with their enclosures. Thank you for the detailed writing. The packages of seforim sent by you on the 6th and 15th of Teves were also received.

2) Regarding the distribution of Chanukah gelt: I believe I have already written that it is not worthwhile to be stringent in this matter. That is, if there is even a doubt—give, and let it be for the sake of the future. Perhaps this itself will help them draw closer sooner.

3) Regarding what you wrote concerning the work in the villages and the large towns, etc.: My opinion has long been that while one must work in the villages—because one is simply saving them from assimilation—it is nonetheless more vital to train teachers and guides from among the Moroccans themselves. They should, on the other hand, be connected to and imbued with the spirit of Lubavitch, to the point where they are "moist enough to moisten others." At most, they will only need to "refresh themselves" from time to time (for which it is appropriate—during school vacation days—to organize for them special, intensive studies regarding the surrounding environment and matters of chinuch. In addition to the studies themselves, this will create a sense of rapport, and perhaps it is worthwhile to offer prizes to those who excel in this. I believe the vacation times are Nissan, Tishrei, and mid-summer. You will surely inform me about this).

4) Regarding what you wrote about the rumors of corporal punishment, G-d forbid, which some suggest as a method of discipline: It is obvious that within the walls of the yeshiva, this is entirely rejected. Aside from the fact that the act itself—reproof through physical punishment—is more negative than positive, it will surely become known among the parents, and even more so among the students, both the punishment and, primarily, the reason for it. Then there is cause for concern that even those who do not know about the matter in general will become interested. It is known from the matter of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge that things which are drawn into one's consciousness act in an internal way, etc. One must seek other methods of punishment, such as distancing them from the school for a period of time, or entirely.

Or, as brought in the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, one should not permit them to be present during the telling of stories of tzaddikim and similar matters that their hearts desire. And above all—increased supervision of the students, and it is to be hoped that in this way the matter will gradually diminish until it ceases entirely.

5) You will surely inform me of the progress of matters regarding Otzar HaTorah, etc., during the time that has passed since you wrote.

6) I have already noted in the past that you should look for ways to publish, from time to time, in the newspapers appearing in your country, about Chabad in general and its activities in your location in particular. Regarding the French language, there is no liability at all, since they understand it. And even regarding the Arabic language, you will surely be able to find someone trustworthy who can attest that the translation matches the intent.

7) Regarding the Siddurim: I believe I have already written that it is worthwhile to give them to the Alliance—in a manner that will not be interpreted as an agreement with their ideology.

8) In your letter of the 7th of Shevat, you do not write details regarding your health. Surely, by the time you receive this letter, you have already improved. It is unnecessary to note that you must follow the doctors' instructions. The ruling of the Rambam is well known, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem. The same applies to the avreich, Yonatan ben Miriam, may he live, Halevi—a pidyon nefesh for him is also enclosed. You will surely share good news regarding this as well.

9) I was very pleased with what you wrote, that one of the teachers at Oholei Yosef Yitzchak announced that tefillin and mezuzos should be checked, and he rectified the matter. It would be very good if other places would also take an interest in this. It is worth discussing with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi R. A. G., may he live, regarding a special budget for this purpose. The expenses and effort are worthwhile due to the importance of the matter. Furthermore, it will surely also have an impact on chinuch. And regarding the current season—it is worthwhile to take an interest in the local custom regarding Pesach, and specifically regarding shmurah matzah.

I believe that last year, too, you gave some out. If there is no difference between the Western and Eastern customs—that is, Ashkenaz and Sephard—perhaps it is worthwhile to give, as a gift to those at the head of Oholei Yosef Yitzchak who have begun to follow Chabad customs, shmurah matzah for the Afikoman at the very least. You will surely discuss this as well with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi R. A. G., may he live.

11) I was very pleased that the sending of students to the synagogues has been put into practice. May the Almighty grant success, both in the students' influence on the listeners and in the effect of the speech on the students themselves.

12) The arrival of Rabbi R. N., may he live, Pinson, brought me special joy (which will surely also cause a lifting of his own spirits)... May the Almighty merit him to bring good news, and frequently—regarding communal matters as well as his own personal affairs.

13) I received word from Chicago that the synagogue there sent, in your name, another ten packages of clothing, and there are about ten more ready.

With the blessing of success in your holy work and in all your affairs, and regards to all those who participate with you,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7954

2, 5, 26 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Avraham Eliezer, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter—with some delay—in which you write about your situation and ask for my opinion as to whether you should travel now to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

In my opinion, since you are in a country where, recently, several G-d-fearing people have arrived in addition to those who were already living there, and since no one among us knows with certainty the Divine intent behind why one is located in a particular place—for "the steps of man are established by Hashem"—you should fulfill within yourself the instruction "stay in your place." You should influence your surroundings in an appropriate manner to strengthen them in Torah and mitzvos and warm them with Yiddishe warmth. May Hashem grant you long life and good years to illuminate your surroundings, and with the addition of the "candle of mitzvah and Torah of light," and the "light of Torah"—which is the Torah of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs. Even for the sake of a single good deed, it is known from the Tanya, Chapter 25, that when one performs any mitzvah whatsoever, it is an eternal matter on High, forever and ever. It is also known from the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that a neshamah descends below and is enclothed for several decades in a Jewish body in order to do a favor for a fellow Jew, whether in material or spiritual matters.

With blessings for long life and good years, with all that this implies.

#### 7954

From the Secretariat copy.

**R' Avraham Eliezer:** Zerkowitz, Muizenberg, Cape Province, South Africa.

## 7955

B"H, 4 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Enclosed is my formal letter of response regarding your decision at the meeting. I find your decision somewhat surprising. Surely Rabbi A. Wolf told you how he traveled to conduct a fundraising campaign while he was here, as did Rabbi M. Gurary. Furthermore, you are undoubtedly aware of the difficulties encountered by Rabbi Kipnis, and now by Rabbi Havlin, and among those mentioned are individuals who are experts in the profession of fundraising, and yet, the situation is as described. Based on the information I have regarding the nature of Rabbi... [Zevin], it seems on the face of it that he is not at all suited to be a *shadar* (fundraiser) to collect money, especially in this country, where there are so many such people in every field and every matter—individuals who have already become experts in this profession over many years. When you throw them out the door, they crawl back in through the window with a smile and a pleasant demeanor, etc.

With respect and blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7859

B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the engagement of your daughter, *tichyeh*, may Hashem grant that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and that it be an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*, as they are illuminated by the "Light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

It is known that the path of holiness is one of "slowly, slowly." Consequently, one must find appropriate ways to bring the groom closer to the teachings of Chassidus, its paths, and its customs. This is especially true in light of the Sages' statement that a son-in-law is like a son. It is well known that the *mitzvah* of educating a son is incumbent upon the father, particularly the *mitzvah* of Torah study, which is a Torah-mandated obligation for the father, as ruled by our Rebbe [the Alter Rebbe] in the opening of his *Hilchos Talmud Torah* and in several other places. It is obvious that the study of the teachings of Chassidus is included in this.

With blessings of *mazal tov*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7958

7958

B"H, 25 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, occupied with communal needs,
Rabbi Moshe Pinchas, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your report regarding the Melaveh Malkah—the *Seudata D’David Malka Meshicha*—that you hosted in your home this past Motzaei Shabbos. It is surprising that you are distressed because, in your view, the results were meager. It is already a well-known adage of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "Though your beginning was small, yet your latter end shall greatly increase" (Iyov 8:7)—and through this, "your latter end shall greatly increase." Certainly, in this matter as well, it will be so—both materially and spiritually. May Hashem grant you and your wife, may they live, and all those who gathered at this farbrengen, the merit to gather many more times in Chassidic farbrengen and with true joy. May you thereby break through the matters that conceal and hide [the truth], until we all merit, together with the entire Jewish people, that the walls and partitions be removed, and that which is said of Him—"Behold, He stands behind our wall" (Shir HaShirim 2:9)—be revealed below ten tefachim: He, our beloved Malka Meshicha.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7859

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, wise and understanding, occupied with communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav R. Sh. Y. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to Mr. Sh. Z. R. shlita, the content of which requires no further explanation. I await your opinion on all of this. As I see it, this is the only way out of the current situation, where there is a danger, chas v'shalom, that the entire education system will be taken over by the government. Anyone who remains outside will receive only half the budget, and the other half will have to be raised by each party that refuses to relinquish its own educational system. In that case, there is reason to fear—and it is highly probable—that the parties will not be able to provide the budget, and consequently, many of the children of Israel will be deprived of their education, etc., etc.

...According to the information I have received in recent days, it seems that some of the G-d-fearing individuals have already come to terms with the idea—without any fight, and apparently even without any effort. Based on the words of our Sages, "Do not judge your fellow until you reach his place," and since I am currently abroad, I am not judging the matter itself as to whether they should be blamed for a lack of effort or not. However, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—"This is a matter for the Angel Michael, but the matter itself is not being resolved." Therefore, I wrote to Sh. Z. R. shlita as mentioned above. I am firmly of the opinion that this "mesiras nefesh" must be demanded forcefully from all the parties—starting with Agudah and ending with Poalei Agudat Yisrael—and to create an uproar if they do not agree to such mesiras nefesh. And woe, woe, that even this is called mesiras nefesh.

I would be grateful if you would inform me as soon as possible of your opinion on all of the above. Surely, you will do whatever is in your power to do in this direction. Thank you for the notification.

I received joyful news before Shabbos, although I do not yet know if it is entirely accurate, that in any case, they are talking about government education taking effect not in 5714, but in 5715.

I received your letter with the news that you are moving to a new residence. It was received before I traveled to the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and as you requested, I mentioned you at the tziyun, that the change of place should be a change of fortune for the good, in both material and spiritual matters alike. For true freedom is when both go together—peace in the assembly below, which thereby also brings about peace in the assembly above (see Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Matos), and blessing and success are drawn down, since the vessel is peace.

I am sure you will inform me of news regarding Mr. Tzioni and Z. shlita.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and with proper health of body and soul,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is a general letter, which will surely interest you.

## 7860

7860

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished and esteemed individual, a branch of the tree of the forefathers, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Recalling our conversation during your visit here, and your perspective regarding the respectful attitude toward the religious sentiments of the Charedi segment of the Jewish people and the traditions of our past—which should be demanded of all offices and institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—I am writing to you regarding the following:

1. You surely surmise, and indeed know, at least to some extent, the painful impression and the resentment in various circles—and not only among the Charedim—caused by the news of the government’s aspiration to change the current situation, to transfer all education in Eretz Yisrael to its own authority, and to abolish the [independent] *zeramim* (educational streams). This is occurring at a time when the government’s track record in religious matters has not been neutral until now, and from time to time, it is only deteriorating further.

I would like to note that I am not discussing the actual fact of children being educated by political parties, as this is neither the time nor the place for that discussion. However, changing the existing situation and shifting it "from right to left" in such a manner is painful.

2. Apparently, and logic also dictates this, the primary reason for the government’s aspiration to abolish the *zeramim* is not for the sake of attacking the religious aspect of the matter, but rather for political reasons. That is to say, without flowery language, they are simply devising a strategy on how to prevent the schools of the *zeramim* from educating and raising children in opposition to the political and economic views of the parties currently holding the reins of government. For the educational *zeramim* currently belong to parties, and consequently, they also serve as platforms for political views that are diametrically opposed to one another.

3. Even if there are those whose intention in abolishing the *zeramim* is to attack religion, they are surely few, and they are not the ones formulating the policy of the ruling parties. Furthermore, upon contemplation of the appropriate approach, one finds in the heart of **every** single Jew an affinity for religiosity—and not just any religiosity, but the religion of Israel—even though this feeling is expressed among many of our people in different ways, due to various reasons.

4. As a result of these three points, the correct solution in my opinion is—if it has already been decided to abolish the *zeramim*—to remove the education of the *zeramim* from the background of politics. That is, the schools should be removed from the authority and management of the political parties and placed under the authority of organizations whose nature is purely spiritual-educational. In other words, the management of the schools should be handed over to institutions and individuals (activists, parents, teachers, and the like) whose lifestyle and perspective on religion align with the school’s curriculum, rather than being in the hands of people whose spirit is not the spirit of the school, merely appointing a "supervisor for kashrus."

I hope that my aforementioned proposal will be accepted by you, and consequently, you will exert effort in this matter in the appropriate manner.

The prospects for realizing this matter certainly depend to a great extent on your efforts. And the man who merited to bring about the matter of compulsory education will also merit to succeed in the matter of the education of *mitzvah* and Torah. I would appreciate it if you would inform me of your opinion regarding the above.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

#### 7860

From the copy attached to the previous letter, as mentioned there.

**R' Shazar:** Shazar. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 20, 7575, and in the references in the notes there.

**And to abolish the *zeramim*:** Which the Rebbe also recoiled from, and he exerted effort to establish a "non-stream stream," as above, Vol. 6, letter 1531, and in the references in the notes there.

**And placed under the authority of organizations:** In continuation of this—above, Vol. 7, letter 2107.

**Supervisor for kashrus:** In "state-religious" education.

## 7861

7861

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5713

Regarding his publication in the controversy concerning what was printed in *Talpiyot*: he has gone even further than that. I only learned of this now, upon receiving the "Haggadah..." in which I was alarmed to read that he actually proposes drinking a fifth cup, and even writes down the procedure for this—specifically that one must give thanks for the miracle of the *atchalta d'geulah* (the beginning of the redemption), etc., etc. This is the opposite of the *psak din* of the *Shulchan Aruch* and the *Acharonim*, the teachers of Israel and the *poskim* accepted by all of Israel. The severity of this, compared to the aforementioned, is understandable, for the Haggadah is a book accessible to all, and the instruction pertains to actual practice. Especially when it is vowelized—it reaches even those who are *amei ha'aretz* (unlearned) who do not realize that they are *amei ha'aretz*. They will certainly draw *kal v'chomer* and *binyan av* arguments, etc.—that if it is permitted to act contrary to the *Shulchan Aruch* in this matter, even though they have never seen it done in their lives, neither by their fathers nor their grandfathers, then *a'ch v'ch* (all the more so) it is possible to act contrary to the *Shulchan Aruch* in other matters. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

#### ***7861***

Printed in *Kovetz Yagdil Torah* (Jerusalem), issue 28, p. 5.

## 7863

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Saadia, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 7 Nissan, as well as the letter that followed. Regarding your question as to where you should focus your avodah: as the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, Rabbi Avraham Abba Gurary, may he live, related, there was a joint meeting of everyone together when he was in Morocco. At that time, it was discussed that you should work in one of the larger towns following Meknes and Casablanca, and the most likely candidate is Midelt, since our institutions there have the largest number of students. In general, this seems appropriate.

Since our people in Morocco are only four or five individuals, and there is a vast field there for major work in chinuch—and consequently, in the dissemination of Chassidus, its ways, and its practices—it is worthwhile that you spread out as much as possible into different towns. Surely, within a short time, each of you will find local assistants for the secondary matters.

Since the intention is to influence not only the students and the young, but also the adults, the baalei batim, the rabbis, etc., in order to draw them closer—not only to assist the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok institutions, but also to the matters of Chassidus in general, which is accomplished more effectively through the study of accessible Chassidic concepts, stories regarding the ways of Chassidim, etc.—it is my hope and confidence that in whichever place you settle, you will organize a circle of avreichim and baalei batim. This should, of course, be done with the permission of the rabbis and sages, so that there will be no issue of diminishing their honor or standing (for various reasons). Consequently, in time, this circle will also produce assistants, mashpi'im, and educators.

Further elaboration is unnecessary. It is surely redundant to remind you about the upcoming day of Lag B'Omer. As is known, the yom hilula is very significant among the Sephardim, especially that of the Rashbi, author of the Zohar. Consequently, its celebration will surely bring satisfaction to all those mentioned above.

Awaiting good news and with blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7865***

7866

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. A. M. Habermann, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

The booklet *Shaarei Chabad*, edited by you, came into the hands of the Rebbe shlita (and it is surprising that you did not see fit to send it to the library of the Rebbe shlita). The Rebbe shlita examined it and noted several comments in the margins. We are copying them here, and they will surely be of use to you. They are listed according to the numbering of the books in your list:

4 – A project that has not yet been realized.

5 – **Shemos, Bo.** Only the parsha of **Shemos** is included here. Va'era and Bo are currently in print.

9 – A photocopy from the Kapust edition.

13 – Only the letter of request is included here. It was printed based on a comparison of two manuscripts—in the publisher’s introduction, it is noted that the author of the text is the Mitteler Rebbe, **not** his father, the Alter Rebbe.

41-42 – This is a list by the Rebbe (Rabbi Yosef Yitzchak) of Lubavitch, may the memory of the righteous and holy be for a blessing, except that he wished for it to be printed anonymously.

42 – It was also published in a Hebrew translation with additions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

47 – Page 307, line 11: **Gimmel Daled**, should be **Gimmel Chaf** (a long *chaf*)—see regarding this a letter from the Rebbe (Rabbi Yosef Yitzchak) of Lubavitch, printed at the end of the notes to Tanya, page 120.

52 – Page 310, line 16: **Cheis daphim** (eight pages) is a typographical error.

55* – **At the end: Iggeres HaKodesh.** It seems it should be Iggeres **HaTeshuvah**.

82 – **At the end: Mishnas 5660.** Several details were corrected therein; for example, the word **"perek"** which appears at the beginning of every *siman* in Iggeres HaKodesh was omitted.

85 – Printed in Germany, in the vicinity of Munich, and not in Brooklyn.

93 – **Shemos, a few parshios** are only Parshas Beshalach (one *drush*) and Parshas Pekudei (two *drushim*). The *drushim* on Sefer Shemos—aside from Parshas Pekudei—appear in Sefer Torah Or.

94 – The approbations are for the Likkutei Torah and not for the additions.

98 – Printed with special proofreading (according to the words of the scholar R' Anshil Aranowitz, may his blood be avenged, who worked on this—nearly **three thousand** errors were corrected!). A list of corrections appears at the end.

99 – The list of corrections was omitted.

100 – Like 98, and not 8.

102, 104, 105, 106, 107, 108, 108, 108 – **All** are photocopies from the manuscript of R' Shmuel Sofer, also known as R' Shmuel der Schreiber.

109 – Also printed therein are collected letters, etc., from our Master the Elder—the author of the Tanya—from his son the Mitteler Rebbe, from the sons of the Tzemach Tzedek, etc.

116 – Still in print.

121 – (4), 58, (6) pages.

132-133 – Error. They are 131'.

179-182 – There are *drushim* that were printed in one of these but not in the other. In general, there are several differences between these editions.

201 – On page 6a—this is a letter from the author of the Tanya, printed in his Iggeres HaKodesh, siman 27.

226 – With an introduction and a long list by the Rebbe (Rabbi Yosef Yitzchak) of Lubavitch, may the memory of the righteous and holy be for a blessing.

229 – The copy arranged according to *shemos* (names) is currently in the possession of Kehot Publication Society, and they are preparing it for print.

230 – Mimeograph, **not** a photocopy.

236 – Including two letters from his son, the Rebbe (Rabbi Yosef Yitzchak), may the memory of the righteous and holy be for a blessing.

With respect and blessings,

## 7867

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, a man of merit, an energetic activist who stands in the breach, a fruitful vine, etc., Mr. Yosef, may he live, Morsiano, Head of the City Committee of Bergen, may it be protected by the Almighty.

Peace and blessing!

I was very happy, and my heart rejoiced, to hear of the great rectification that was achieved in your camp to prevent the public desecration of Shabbos and Yom Tov by the sons and daughters of Israel. Through the efforts of your honor and his colleagues, the students of the French school have ceased attending school on the holy Shabbos and on the days of the festival. How great is his reward, and the reward of his colleagues, may they live, for they have merited to be among those who bring merit to the many, upon whom the merit of the many depends. Surely, in the future as well, you will remain at your post to strengthen the wall of Torah and Yiddishkeit, and kosher education in particular.

And surely you will not be satisfied with influencing the sons and daughters of Israel to "turn from evil," but will also strive in the area of "doing good"—namely, to fill the days of rest and joy with content of holiness and the light of Torah through Shabbos gatherings and the like.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant success to your holy work for the benefit of the community and the individual, and may you add strength and courage in your work, for as our Sages of blessed memory said, "We elevate in matters of holiness." May this communal activism continue and bring down upon you and your households, may they live, an abundance of blessings in your personal matters as well, in revealed goodness.

With blessing.

#### ***7867***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L'Melech* 1, p. 73.

## 7969

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and involved in communal affairs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi R. Sh. Y. (may he live)

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter. The response was delayed for several reasons, and I ask for your forgiveness regarding this.

... It is an explicit Mishnah that even though one might say, "What do we have to do with this trouble?" nevertheless, this argument is rejected.

The same applies in the present case: since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, entrusted you with a very important and necessary matter, this falls under the category of being "sworn and standing from Mount Sinai"...

This aligns with what we heard from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, that the Ribono shel Olam does not "remain a debtor." Based on the teaching of our Sages that the measure of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," it is certain that by dedicating your time to the affairs of Tomchei Temimim, success will be drawn down for you in the time that remains at your disposal for your other matters, both general and specific. In the final analysis, you will actually gain from this...

6) Following the above: It has been on my mind for some time that all the Chabad yeshivos should publish a joint Torah journal containing chiddushei Torah from the students. This would be on an informal basis—please let me know your opinion, and whether there are students among the talmidim of Lod and Tomchei Temimim who are suitable for this.

7) Regarding what you wrote about Mr. ... (may he live): Since they have already been to the professor once and were not satisfied with his treatment at that time, they wish to wait for my opinion once more—whether it is as I wrote previously, that they should visit him, or if I am retracting that.

It is surely unnecessary to inform Mr. ... and his wife (may they live) that I am not a professor of medicine, nor even a doctor or a medic. Furthermore, when people ask for my opinion and I write what seems right to me, the inquirer is not obligated to follow what I have said, for free choice is theirs, and they should do as they see fit. Consequently, there is no room for any resentment, etc., on my part. They should not refrain from taking any action out of a concern that it might somehow harm my "honor," for there is no basis for such a concern at all. Regarding the fact that the professor’s treatment did not satisfy them previously, several years have passed since then. I know of many who have turned to him for help and have succeeded, and I see no reason why it should be different in this case. In any event, whatever Mr. ... and his wife (may they live) decide to do, may the Ribono shel Olam grant them success so that it will be for their good, both materially and spiritually.

8) And last but not least: In response to your notification regarding the birth of a son to your son, the G-d-fearing, learned Rabbi Aharon (may he live), may it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that just as his parents (may they live) have brought him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu, so too may they bring him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to maasim tovim, in a state of true expansion, both materially and spiritually. May you (may you live) derive much Chassidishe nachas from all your descendants (may they live), and may you also be able to share good news regarding your family (may they live) who are in our former country.

With a blessing of Mazal Tov,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,970

7,970

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5713

Regarding your question about *Sefer HaYashar* — see what is written on this in *Sefer Shem HaGedolim* by the Chida under that entry. Regarding *Sefer Yosippon* — it is known that many changes (and even forgeries) have been introduced into it, and its contents require the critique of an expert in the field. In general, regarding questions of this nature, the instruction of Chazal is well-known: "Where vegetables can enter, let meat and fish enter" (*Shabbos* 140b). This is especially true when it is doubtful whether it is even "vegetables."

## 7972

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all lovers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

The Beis Rivkah schools for girls, which operate under the supervision of **Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch**, have, over the course of their eleven-year existence, raised and continue to raise hundreds upon hundreds of Jewish daughters in the spirit of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits—daughters who are a source of nachas to their parents and a pride to the entire Jewish people.

In the merit of their holy founder, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and thanks to the tireless and devoted work of their administrators, the **Beis Rivkah** institutions have earned a name of praise and glory in the field of kosher chinuch, raising a generation of responsible religious Jewish daughters and mothers, upon whom the future of Beis Yisrael in the spirit of Torah and mesorah depends to a great extent.

Regrettably, the **Beis Rivkah** institutions now find themselves in a critical financial situation. The heavy burden of debts that have accumulated over previous years, combined with current high expenses, threaten the very foundations of their existence.

Immediate help is urgently needed.

I therefore turn with a heartfelt appeal to all lovers of Torah and mitzvos, and especially to those for whom the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, are holy and dear, that they respond warmly to the emergency campaign of the Beis Rivkah institutions. With an open hand and a warm heart, may they contribute themselves and also collect from their friends and acquaintances, in order to save the Beis Rivkah institutions and to give these vital institutions the possibility to continue their work of kosher chinuch.

And in this merit, Hashem will help all those who support and assist in whatever they are in need of, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and with regards,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7972***

From a photocopy of the letter.

## 7972*

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, etc.,

You did very well to add the few lines regarding the fact that the time for *sicha* is all year round, although it is worth considering whether it might have been better to place that at the beginning of the booklet.

I am sure that on the next occasion, you will fulfill the distribution in some manner.

2) I do not know at which end one needs to expedite the matter of the permit for Rabbi Pinson, may he live—whether in Morocco or in France. You should certainly discuss this with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi R.A.G., may he live.

3) As it appears from the letter of the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi S. Liberow, may he live, the scope of his work has not been clearly defined.

It is a wonder and a surprise as to what the reason for this is. Although I am writing about this to the esteemed Rabbi, etc., and the Chossid Rabbi R.A.G., may he live, nevertheless, for the sake of order, I am mentioning this to you as well.

4) Enclosed is the list of the continuation of the imprisonment, which was apparently forgotten by mistake in the previous letter.

5) I have asked a few times: seemingly, it would be worthwhile that in the newspapers appearing in Morocco—which are surely read by the Jews—one should endeavor to have them print, from time to time, information regarding our activities, as well as matters of Chassidus, its guidance, customs, and history, adapted to the nature of the readers and the type of newspaper.

6) I was pleased that between the lines of your letter, it is evident that even with physical eyes you see the success of the matters. May it be the will of Hashem that both the success, and your vision regarding the matters you have not yet seen, will come to fruition in a visible and revealed way, speedily.

With a blessing for success in your holy work and in your personal affairs,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7973

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work,
Rabbi Shalom, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the rationale for organizing a continuation of the classes of the Yeshivas Achei Tmimim at the summer camp, in addition to those that currently exist. You suggest that this might prevent some students who are in the higher grades from discontinuing their studies at the Yeshiva in the future. You ask if it would be possible to send 6–7 students from here, along with a Rosh Yeshiva, to the summer camp in order to supervise these students.

Certainly, adding higher grades is very, very appropriate (see *Likutei Torah, Shelach* 38c).

Regarding the matter of sending students from here, this must be discussed with the administration of the Yeshiva here. However, on the face of it, there are several difficulties with this. The main point is that, seemingly, the parents of these students might not agree to this, as it is contrary to the usual path—people travel from a small city to a large city, and from a small yeshiva to a larger yeshiva, not the other way around. You surely also recall the attempt in Chicago regarding this, which did not succeed, even though not all the conditions are identical. It would be different if you were to bolster your efforts regarding the boys and bochurim in your own city; it stands to reason that this would be much easier. In any case, I am not ruling out the matter, and as mentioned, you should discuss it with the Yeshiva administration.

Regarding your request that Mr. Dan, may he live, build a mikveh in your courtyard—and surely it will be done without controversy—this is very appropriate from all perspectives.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

7974

B”H, 8 Menachem Av, 5713

The students from Spain—it is worthwhile to accept them (and this will also hold their brothers). The students from Morocco who are with you and wish to leave—it is necessary to prevent them from doing so (in ways of pleasantness)—except in a place where there is a fear of harm to the collective, G-d forbid.

With blessings for success in all matters, and especially for proper health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7995

7995

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5713

Brooklyn.
Mrs. Miriam Mareisha, may she live.

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter in due time, in which you ask for my opinion as to when your husband, the Rav, may he live, can come to Paris.

I received the same question from your husband, the Rav, and I answered him that it depends on the situation on the ground. He must ensure two things: a) That his departure will not harm the chadarim and yeshivos there. b) That he will be able to obtain a re-entry visa to Morocco without difficulty. And since Hashem has granted him the merit—and through him, the entire family—to participate in managing the mosdos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, it is certain that this is the path through which your husband, the Rav, and the entire family will have the hatzlacha and bracha that everyone needs. Therefore, one must hold onto this with all one's strength.

May Hashem help you all so that this comes to you easily.

It goes without saying that in connection with the above, the scheduling of the time for your daughter’s wedding, in a good and auspicious hour, also depends on this.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, may he live,

The Secretary: A. Quint

...Regarding your inquiry about the *heter* (permission) your wife received for a second marriage: this must be clarified with one of the local *rabbonim* who is familiar with those who granted the *heter*, as they are surely reliable authorities. The aforementioned individual must remain strong in his *bitachon* (trust) in Hashem, that He will fulfill his needs with whatever is necessary for him. ## 7996*

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

Regarding the conclusion of your letter: it was written in a moment of anger, or at the very least, at a time when the heart held sway over the mind. I hope that by now, you too see that the request you wrote has no place at all. Since Hashem has granted you, and your entire family—may they live—the merit of being attached to the *ilana d’chayei* (the Tree of Life), the institution of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h*, *nvg"m*, *zy"a*—which is the source of your success, both generally and specifically—it is understood and simple that you must hold fast to this. On the contrary, you should add strength and vigor. If, as is the case with all human endeavors, there are shortcomings or things that are not as they should be, one must seek the ways and means to prevent them. To elaborate on this is surely unnecessary. May you add courage to your *avodah* for your own sake, and in the natural course of events, many things will smooth themselves out.

2) Regarding the content of the letter... I am compelled to say, as I also wrote to the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid... *shichyeh*, that due to the order of our *avodah*, it is necessary that all actual influence flow through our center. This is notwithstanding the fact that regarding the manner and quantity of the influence, he will speak [about this] with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid... *shichyeh*. It is impossible to act otherwise, especially regarding the Joint and various other channels. It is self-understood that the influence must be provided in such a way that it does not diminish the stature of the recipient (as for several reasons, this must be handled according to *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and also in accordance with the benefit of the *avodah*). There are many ways to do this so that the recipient does not feel slighted, and surely, to elaborate on this is also unnecessary.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal matters,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. The package of books that you sent [...] Tammuz has been received, and I am sure you will continue to do so in the future. Regarding what you wrote—that some of them are well-known—in our generation, even well-known books have disappeared from the market. In all such doubts, one should rule leniently—that is, send them here.

#### ***7996\****

From a photocopy of the letter.

**The conclusion of your letter:** Regarding the difficulties in the work of *shlichus*.

**The package of books you sent:** For the library.
