## 7778

B"H, 9 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 4, 16, 21, 22, 23, 29, and 30 Menachem Av, along with their enclosures. Thank you, thank you for the good news that you are seeing success in your work and that you feel the blessing of our Nasi, after whom the institutions are named, resting upon you and influencing blessing and success. May Hashem continue to add to this in the days to come, and as our Sages have ruled, we increase in matters of holiness.

2) I await good news as soon as possible regarding the successful conclusion of the matter of the payments you are to receive from the institutions mentioned in your letter, as well as regarding the continuation of the proposal to establish a school in the vicinity of Haifa.

3) Some time ago, Siddurim and our sefarim were sent to the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and noble Rabbi Yehuda, may he live, Shmotkin. We are now writing to him to hand over to the needs of the Reshet a certain number of Siddurim and our sefarim, in accordance with your request in your letter.

... 5) I was alarmed to read in your letter regarding the resignation of the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and noble Rabbi [Name] from his position, and likewise his father from his assistance. My alarm is not because I fear a lack of support for the Reshet, for I am confident that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will provide for this. However, the adage and interpretation of the Rebbe Maharash on the verse, "Relief and deliverance will arise from another place, but you and your father’s house will be lost," is already well-known—meaning, **the merit for this** [will be lost].

6) I was pleased by what you wrote, that you have adopted the practice of requiring two signatures on checks, in accordance with our Sages' teaching regarding tzedakah, which should be handled by two people.

7) You should certainly maintain a connection with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi Yisrael Abuchatzeira, may he live, for beyond the letter you are requesting from him, he has influence within the Sephardic circles... The drawing together of minds from both sides will certainly be beneficial.

... 10) It is good and necessary that you organize all the teachers affiliated with us and begin studies not on the 25th of Tishrei, which is the official start of the term, but earlier than that, as the needs of the situation dictate. You must recruit the best teachers who have been with you until now, as well as the teachers from among Anash who are needed for work in the Reshet. Since the debts of the year 5713 have finally been paid, the teachers will certainly receive their salaries in the year 5714, and surely in better ways than until now. In accordance with your request, I have also sent this opinion of mine via telegram, which reads:

"Beginning studies in the Reshet institutions in Elul is very correct, and my confidence is strong that the teachers from Anash will mobilize themselves for this plan as needed, and their salaries will certainly be secure. I await good news. My signature."

... With a blessing for success in your holy work in a manner that is above nature. You will surely utilize for this the days of the year 5713, which was a year of success in the places where they at least began with actual deeds. With a blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* to each one of them and their families, may they live.

7979

B"H, 10 Elul, 5713

Greetings and Blessings!

Some time ago, the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, Rabbi B.A. Gorodetsky, may he live, wrote to me that among his other duties, he had taken upon himself a special role in the work of the Reshet.

## 7880

B”H, 10 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, R’ Menachem Zev, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letters of 17 and 22 Menachem Av in due time, and I am surely waiting to hear good news regarding your personal matters.

Regarding the visit of Mr. ... may he live, here: as I have written previously, it is not a matter of planting alone—that one "plants with a word"—but rather, one must subsequently make the effort to ensure it comes to fruition, for each person according to his situation.

The beginning of this effort is to ask him what he heard, etc., and in doing so, the aforementioned individual has the opportunity to share what is on his heart, and the one asking can then fill in the gaps and bring him closer in practice, etc.

Regarding what you wrote, that R’ A. Stern, may he live, a shochet, will soon be publishing a book of stories of Tzaddikim: he should be encouraged to note in the margins or at the end of the book from whom he heard the story, whether the source is reliable, and to what extent, etc.

Regarding Rabbi ... may he live: he should have been encouraged—both regarding his influence on his son who traveled to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and regarding the mikveh in his camp. In both matters, they spoke with coldness, and his explanation was, as the Baraisa says, "We have no one to rely upon except our Father in Heaven." It is well known that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Admur, noted that the Baraisa brings this statement in the context of all the matters of the birth pangs of Moshiach, such as the rising cost of living, etc.

Thank you for what you wrote regarding the Yeshiva students. You are surely aware of what is being done with them, especially during the days of Elul and Tishrei. It was surely heard that in their Yeshiva, which was here, I suggested that the Yeshiva students (and the administration, all the more so) should increase their study of *avodah*-oriented maamarim, especially during these days. It would be very good if they would do the same in Montreal, and it would be even better if they did so in other places as well.

... You are certainly permitted to justify yourself regarding what you wrote concerning the above matters, for it is a very correct thing, and if only it were done more frequently and with more detail.

May Hashem grant you the merit to bring good news regarding your personal matters.

## 7881

[13 Elul, 5713]

...I have now received your letter informing me about your sons, may they live. Surely you are utilizing your influence upon them so that they may be channels for spreading the wellsprings outward, especially your eldest son, Mr. David, may he live, who is serving in the army. There, it is most necessary to illuminate them with the light of Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus—and with Chassidic conduct and all that surrounds Chassidus. And who knows if it is for a time such as this that he reached his current position. The promise of the Alter Rebbe to all those who exert themselves in his affairs is well known—that he promised them they would succeed in this.

Regarding your note as to why the sum of the verses of the parsha was not marked at the end of Parshas Pekudei: one should search in the early printings, for in my opinion, this is merely an omission by the printer, and it continued as such with the other printers who followed him.

Alternatively, it is possible that it was written "without any sign" (*bli kol siman*), and the intention was that there are 92 verses in the parsha. The typesetter then took this literally, thinking there was no sign here, and omitted these words out of a lack of knowledge.

With blessings for Chassidic nachas from all your offspring, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7881***

A portion was printed in the sefer *Toras Menachem—Toras Menachem* on Shas at the end, and in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 6, p. 408; it was completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

The letter is to R' Alexander Sender Yudasin. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 18, 6557, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

B"H, 23 Elul, 5713

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos, along with the *pidyon nefesh*.

## 7884

B"H, 27 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal needs,
R' Moshe Pinchas, may he live, Hakohen

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 23 Elul. Although the time is not at all conducive to writing letters, the pleasure and joy I felt upon learning of your interest and efforts to settle what is owed to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal needs, our friend R' Y.D. Graner, may he live, compelled me to step out of my routine and the constraints of time to write these lines. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue in this path with added strength, and especially as a Kohen, through which the necessary funds will be influenced to reach the others who are involved and working in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in an appropriate manner. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

In connection with this:

2) It would be worthwhile for you to also exert effort regarding the following matter: It is surely known to you that the late R' Sh. Kantorow, a"h, stipulated in his will a certain sum for the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva. His children would not have minded if he had been buried in a plot he had purchased in a different cemetery, and consequently, there was no place to ask them to pay for the plot in the Agudas Chabad cemetery. As it stands, he is still buried in a plot that has not been paid for, and one should not leave such matters hanging. Therefore, it would be appropriate and good—and perhaps even necessary—that from the sum the aforementioned deceased allocated for the Yeshiva, the Yeshiva should pay the fair market price for such a plot. I have raised this matter now, rather than earlier, for several reasons. The main point is that since a portion of the aforementioned estate has already been received by the Yeshiva, this matter must be settled. It is understood that I will raise this from another side as well, but merit is brought about through the meritorious, and surely you will do what is incumbent upon you regarding this.

Approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live, a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7886

7886

B”H, 4 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 Elul, following a long silence and interruption. Time does not permit the writing of letters at this moment, and I am enclosing a general letter which will also serve as a personal letter to you. I am certain you will publicize it appropriately within the widest possible circles.

It is surprising that, after writing to me that you are in contact with Tzeirei Agudas Chabad of Tel Aviv, you did not participate in a noticeable way in the publication issued for 18 Elul. I am sure you will rectify this at the appropriate opportunity.

Regarding your question as to whether to send the letter found at the beginning of *Kuntres HaAvodah* and *Etz Chaim* to all the *Roshei Yeshiva* and yeshiva administrators: in my opinion, it is still too early for this. While the aforementioned should be publicized among your friends and acquaintances without discrimination regarding which yeshiva they attend, I do not know if "ascending the wall" with great noise will succeed in practice. After all, the purpose of all *avodah* is that it should come to actual fruition, and if it can be done with a "still, small voice," that is better, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Walk in His ways; just as He is... so too you... and it was not in the wind, nor in the earthquake, nor in the fire... but in a still, small voice."

With a blessing for a *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah* to each one of you individually and to all of you together, that the desire of Hashem may succeed in your hands to spread the *maayanos* outward, to turn the "outside" into "inside," and to make the springs of water like the sea that covers the earth, for the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem.

P.S. It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter a work plan for the month of Tishrei. I am certain there will be no lack of actual work, only that you did not write about it.

From the Secretariat’s copy.

## 7889

7889

B"H, 23 MarCheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of 9 Cheshvan, in which you apologize for writing news that is not particularly happy.

As a rule, when one **needs** to write and puts it off from day to day, a reason eventually arises that forces one to write. Conversely, when one writes in a timely manner—when there is good news to report—and does so then, rather than, Heaven forbid, in the opposite case, one is spared from having to be prompted from Above by other means that force one to write and connect with one another.

I hope that by the time this letter reaches you, the matter about which you write has already been arranged for the good, and hopefully the other matters will also [be resolved] as they should be, little by little. I look forward to hearing good news from you that all is well in terms of gashmius and all is well in terms of ruchnius.

With blessings.

P.S. When I am at the Tziyun HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nbg"m, zy"a, I will mention all the matters about which you write for the good, for health and parnassah tovah.

Just now received his letter of 19 MarCheshvan.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding this in your letter. Surely you are acting with the appropriate energy, and may Hashem grant you success. The saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." It would be worthwhile to publicize the yeshiva there through shluchim and in every possible way, making it known that you are accepting students into your yeshiva, etc. After all, there are several students from the yeshivos in England and Antwerp, etc. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote in one of his letters, when one sets up a lantern in the darkness of the street, people gather around it; how much more so when one sets up the "light of Torah"—this being the Torah of Chassidus—in the street, people will surely gather around it. It is just that those who are currently on a different "street" need to be informed of this in terms that will reach them...

I await good news.

## 7993

B"H, 29 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work,
Rabbi Menachem Zev, may he live, Halevi

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Vayechi, as well as those preceding it, along with their enclosures. I also received the *pidyon nefesh* via the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, Rabbi Ben-Zion, may he live, Shemtov, the *shadar*. Truly, it is not as satisfactory as I had hoped, for it seems that matters are not only failing to ascend, but in comparison to his previous visit, there is a sense of regression. Since there are several "cedars of Lebanon" in your location—both those who have been there for some time and the new *anash* refugees who arrived recently—I do not know who is holding things back, if not for negligence and a lack of action. It is a tragedy that one must wait for someone from the outside to come and stir up interest in matters as basic as the *daled amos* of Chassidim.

And if there were no discussions that break through the limitations, then even this is of no avail.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the form of the letters that Rabbi Yaakov, may he live, Zilberman wrote to me: his letter was received. As I see from your letter, it appears that he does not have a tradition passed down from person to person, but rather he is simply being precise about the form of the *parshiyos* he has seen. On the face of it, in matters such as these, one must hear it from a person who received it from a person—what is essential and what is merely incidental. It is worth searching to see if such people can be found.

3) Regarding the book *Darchei HaChaim* that he left here, I have not yet had the time to examine it as necessary, and perhaps this will be during the coming week...

With blessings—awaiting good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7996

B"H, 29 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, [Name]...
May he live.

Peace and blessing!

1) Regarding what you wrote concerning your son... may he live: It is understood that as for what he needs for his expenses or, at times, for medical matters, there will be no lack of this, Heaven forbid.

Regarding his general state of health: During his entire time here, he did not look much to his peers, and it was evident then that he could not adjust, whether because by nature he is not very sociable with peers, or because he was not accustomed to living conditions outside of his home.

Since, regarding yiras shamayim, thank G-d he is whole, and he has been learning here in the yeshiva for some years now—and consequently he is also at the age for shidduchim—it is a sound idea for him to travel home. There, it is easier to find a suitable shidduch. Most importantly, his adjustment in body and soul will be easier for him, both because he will be among his family and, primarily, because the conditions in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) are different than they are here.

Nevertheless, I told your son, may he live, in response to his question, that even if he travels to Eretz Yisrael, he should prepare a return visa to here. This is so that there will be no difficulties if, after his visit home, he wishes to return here for a period of time. Surely, the Ribono shel Olam will show him the correct path—correct in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

... 5) Enclosed is a letter to... may he live, and surely these days will bring him good news. Consequently, one should explain to him and his peers (may they live and be well), based on the story Chassidim tell about the holy Tzaddik... R' Hillel (of blessed memory) of Paritch—which I also heard, albeit briefly, from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (of blessed memory)—that when he traveled to Lubavitch, his wagon overturned. By that, he fulfilled his obligation [of suffering], and he lived long days and years thereafter.

The same applies to the matter at hand. Since our Sages (of blessed memory) said that whoever flatters a wicked person eventually falls into his hands, this must be fulfilled according to the interpretation of the Arizal at the end of Likutei Torah on the verse "He shall be satisfied with reproach." Through the reproach alone, one fulfills their obligation and is not struck. So too, in the present case, surely the Ribono shel Olam will grant success so that it will be sufficient in such a manner.

Regarding the other side, the explanation brought in Chassidus and also in books of mussar is well known: that a leech which sucks blood has already done its part and, consequently, is nullified from the world. May the Ribono shel Olam grant him merit and success to report good news as soon as possible regarding the above.

## 7999

B”H, 4 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn

Mrs. ... may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter of... as well as the previous one. When I am at the Tziyun HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention all the matters you wrote about, for each person according to their needs.

Regarding what you wrote about your daughter... may she live: I have already written to you several times that when a daughter is of age for shidduchim, the first thing parents—and especially a mother—must do is speak with her about how a Jewish home should be conducted, particularly regarding Taharas HaMishpacha (mikveh). Only when a Jew conducts themselves in the way of Torah can a Jew be truly happy.

Therefore, there is no place to be embarrassed or to refrain from speaking about this. Furthermore, one should not be satisfied with speaking about it only once. As it appears from your silence on this matter, little or nothing has been done in this regard.

Consequently, I do not understand why you are surprised that things are not going smoothly, when one is not doing what Hashem Yisbarach commands us to do.

I hope that at the very least, you will now begin to speak with your daughter about this. May Hashem Yisbarach help that your daughter, may she live, should have a good zivug, and that you should have much Yiddishe nachas from her and from all your children.

With blessings,

With a blessing to each of you and your household members, may they live.

#### ***7,600***

## 801

B"H, 24 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
Rabbi Menachem Zev Halevi, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 17 Shevat. My previous letter has surely reached you by now. Regarding what you write concerning... I have already written to you about this, and what benefit is there in repeating it once again, especially since I have also told you this orally? The instruction is that you should act according to the guidance of expert doctors, for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

May Hashem grant you success.

2) Regarding the students of the beis medrash in whom a lack of discipline and failure to keep to the schedule, etc., is evident: It is not appropriate at all that I should act as a substitute for the mashgiach or fill the role of each member of the administration, etc., as it is written, "Withdraw your foot from your neighbor's house." The maintenance of the schedule and the supervision—as in any educational institution—must be the responsibility of the individuals appointed for that purpose. If they perform their work faithfully, I do not understand why they should not succeed in that which they succeed in other yeshivos, especially since I have already spoken with some of the bochurim regarding the above, and they have certainly conveyed this to their friends as well.

3) And similarly to the above—also regarding the bochur... for why should he study simple explanations and commentaries on the "kretch" (sigh), etc., and as a result not know what to do? Since he asked explicitly and I also answered him explicitly that he should not stop, there is no room for doubt.

4) Enclosed is a copy of my letter sent officially to the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi L. Kramer, may he live and be well.

As was conveyed to you by telephone, it will surely be publicized on the upcoming Shabbos Mevarchim. Nevertheless, a copy is being sent to you as well, and I hope it will be received before Shabbos Mevarchim. You will surely utilize it as much as possible. I look forward to hearing good news.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 804

B"H, 6 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To my relative, Mrs. Zelda, may she live:

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I received any letters or news from you. It is already a custom among Chassidim, even from generations before us, that when all is well, one does not write. And although the Alter Rebbe already complained about this, it seems that the custom of the generations that followed did not fully heed his complaint, and the practice still persists.

In truth, I very much wanted to interpret your silence in accordance with the aforementioned custom, yet since it is possible to clarify, one does not rely on a presumption. I would be very grateful if you would write regarding yourself and your husband, may he live, as well as your mother, the Rabbanit, may she live. May it be Hashem’s will that you only report good news in your letters.

And since in your last letter you wrote that you might send what you have written and published, please fulfill this as well. Although, in general, one does not reveal oneself as much in what is published for the public—or at least, less so than in a letter—nevertheless, for the sake of completeness and the perfection of one’s character profile, every detail is certainly useful.

Enclosed is a copy of a letter I wrote in connection with the recent Yom HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, the content of which serves as a response to part of your letter to me.

With warm regards to your mother, the Rabbanit, and to your husband, may they live.

Awaiting good news,

## 805

B"H, 12 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of your wife, *tichyeh*. As you requested, when I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulal"h, navgam, zya*, I will mention her for a complete and speedy recovery, and I look forward to hearing good news.

On this occasion, I would like to urge you once again regarding what I have mentioned to you several times when we met face-to-face: the absolute necessity that you exert your influence upon your son, the Rabbi, *shiya*, whom Hashem has merited with being listened to to a significant degree within the circles of the young rabbis, *shiya*. Your son should influence them and...

...the organization of which he is a member, so that they emphasize and strive much more in matters of *yiras shamayim* and practical *mitzvos*, both regarding the synagogues and communities of the young rabbis, and regarding the various unions that they announce from time to time. Since a year ago there was a noticeable shift and movement toward the right, it is now easier to continue in this direction, and certainly not to allow room for any weakening, as has been felt in recent months.

I do not wish to detail and elaborate on the specifics of the above, as they are surely known to your son, the Rabbi, *shiya*, even more than to me. It is possible that your son, *shiya*, does not realize or does not believe that he can exert influence in this. However, considering that each of us, when acting in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, is an emissary of the Omnipresent, blessed be He, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, and "a person's emissary (the Supreme One upon the Throne, as it were) is like him" (see *Likutei Torah, Vayikra*, at the beginning), he must proceed with confidence in the path of influence mentioned above, and then Hashem will grant success. In any event, each of us must fulfill what is incumbent upon us completely, and Hashem will do what is good in His eyes.

The same applies to you, *ka"t, shiya*; surely, when you speak with your son, the Rabbi, *shiya*, whether orally or in writing, with words coming from the heart as mentioned above, you will certainly influence him.

With respect and blessings, awaiting good news.

## 606

606

B"H, 25 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the *avreich* [name], *sheyichyeh*,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you are dissatisfied with certain details regarding the *seder* of the *yeshiva*, and in your opinion, these details distract from the *hasmadah* in learning as it should be, and likewise regarding *davening*, and therefore you have a notion of traveling to the *Tomchei Temimim* *yeshiva* in Eretz Yisrael, *tizkeh lichonen*, and you ask for my opinion on this.

It is superfluous to elaborate on what is known and simple: that the matters which hinder Torah, *avodah*, or *gemilus chasadim* have as their source the "leaven in the dough"—that is, the *yetzer hara*—which confuses a person in many ways and manners. For even though it is called a "fool," regarding its *avodah*, it is an expert craftsman. As is known from the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navg"m, zya*, the *yetzer hara* approaches each and every person with arguments tailored to the specific character of that individual’s soul, to the point that it sometimes even cloaks itself in the mantle of a *tzurba merabanan*, a G-d-fearing person, and so on. Therefore, everyone must examine very, very carefully the thoughts that enter their mind regarding changes in the *avodah* of Hashem, and know who is making these arguments—whether they come from the right side or the left side. You are surely familiar with the story regarding the *tzaddik* of Chernobyl, which was printed in the *sicha* of Pesach 5743; one of the criteria is whether the change will cause a *bitul Torah* and *avodah*—or not.

Regarding your case: since you are in a *yeshiva* founded by the *tzaddikim*, the *nesi'im* of the generation, and conducted in their spirit—namely, the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*—it is highly probable, even without knowing the specific details, that studying there entails great benefit. Consequently, it is also understood that the *yetzer hara* will rise up against this with various types of schemes to nullify and distract you from conducting yourself in accordance with the requirements of the *yeshiva* in all details.

It is also understood that if the *yetzer hara* were to reveal its intention—that it does not want to let you be diligent in your study of *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*—you would certainly not listen to it. Therefore, consistent with what is said, "And the serpent was cunning," it comes with guile, claiming that the *yeshiva* itself is what distracts you from diligence in Torah and from matters of *avodas Hashem* with *yiras shamayim* as it should be. In this way, it hopes that its arguments will be accepted, and it will distract you from Torah and *davening*. And even though the *yetzer hara* must promise you that if you go to another *yeshiva*, it will not distract you and you will be able to be diligent in Torah and meticulous in *davening*, the *yetzer hara* is guaranteed that once you listen to its voice at the beginning—for "all beginnings are difficult"—it will certainly find a way afterward to draw you even further into its net.

For man has been given free choice, and two paths are before him, as the verse states, "See, I have set before you today life and good, etc." But together with this, man has been given special assistance to choose the good, as the verse states, "Therefore choose life." Certainly, in your case as well, even though the *yetzer hara* is extremely cunning, you have been given the strength to nullify all its arguments and to exert yourself with *mesiras nefesh* by completely diverting your attention from the distracting arguments that the environment is not suitable for you, and that everyone else is to blame for your *bitul Torah* and *davening*, and not yourself, etc., etc.

It is also understood that among your peers in the *yeshiva*, there are some matters that require correction, for there is nothing absolutely perfect except for the Holy One, Blessed be He, the Creator of the world. But the advice for this is that you should influence your peers to correct their ways, rather than you being influenced by them. This is also a *segulah* for your own shortcomings to be corrected through your peers, as it is said—and as is explained—regarding the concept that "all of Israel are responsible for one another," that they are one complete stature, and there is a quality in one that is not in the other, and through *ahavas Yisrael*, each one completes his peer.

The conclusion of all the above is that you should divert your attention from thoughts that distract from Torah and *avodah*, and **immerse** yourself in the study of *Nigleh* and *Chassidus* and in the *avodah* of *davening*—in accordance with the *seder* of the *yeshiva* and its requirements. Then, the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled in you: "I have labored—and I have found."

You do not mention whether your friend... *sheyichyeh* is also being distracted by these same arguments that you write about regarding your own affairs. If that is the case, it is understood that the above response applies to him as well.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*

## 807

B"H, 9 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing, and upright, R' Shmuel Tzvi, may he live,
Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I received the news via telephone, and subsequently in a letter from the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, R' Moshe Eliyahu, may he live, Gerlitzky, that his state of health is not as it should be. When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention him for a complete and speedy recovery. My hope is strong that he himself will be able to bring me good news regarding this.

It is surely unnecessary to point out that in every single thing one must see a hint from Above regarding the Torah of Hashem and His avodah. This is especially true when it is inscribed upon a person’s heart, for the heart is the dwelling place of the feeling of love for Hashem, etc., as it is written, "And you shall love Hashem, your G-d, with all your heart." When a Jewish person increases their spiritual health, they are granted an increase from Above in physical health.

The path to arrive at this love for Him, may He be blessed, is through hisbonenus in various ways, as is explained in several chapters of Tanya. Therefore, it is appropriate that he establish a shiur—at least a few times a week—in the study of Chassidus. He can certainly consult with R' Gerlitzky, may he live, regarding the order of study for this.

You are surely aware of the three daily shiurim for every person established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: 1) Reciting the daily portion of Tehillim—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month—each day after Shacharis. 2) Studying the weekly parsha of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary—on Sunday from the beginning of the sedra until the second aliyah, on Monday from the second aliyah until the third, and so on. 3) A daily shiur in Tanya—as the Tanya is divided for the days of the year.

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery, and awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 18

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter, in which you bring the good news that your wife—may she live and be well—has returned to her strength. Certainly, in accordance with the words of our Sages that we elevate in matters of holiness, may you continue to bring good news in both material and spiritual matters, both regarding yourself and your wife, and regarding your children and household—may they live—for it is a mitzvah d'oraisa to gladden the heart of one's spouse, which is part of the great principle of the Torah, as Rabbi Akiva said, as a general mitzvah: "Love your neighbor as yourself."

Thank you for what you wrote to your son, the Rabbi—may he live—regarding the content of my letter to you concerning him, and surely you added your own thoughts as well. Since I see in the letter from your son—may he live—that he will speak with you further regarding the above, you will surely take the next opportunity to strengthen and encourage him as well.

And in accordance with the well-known saying that time is a loss that cannot be recovered, and whatever can be done today should not be postponed for later—especially since it is known that every single day performs its own task, and every day must be filled with content appropriate to the capacity of that specific individual, especially if that person is a communal figure, meaning he has a circle upon whom he can influence and who accept his guidance.

And especially since this is also a matter of the day, for these days the Rabbis... and the Rabbis...—may they live—the heads and leaders of the Rabbinical organization, have returned from their trip to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established. Surely their visit to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—and the report they brought regarding the attitude of the members of the Rabbinical organization toward the questions connected to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—will have an impact, and this attitude will be expressed and come into action also in the sermons which, according to the custom of the country, will be delivered during the upcoming holiday of Pesach—on the first days, and especially on the last days.

With blessings to you, your wife, and all your household—may they live—for a kosher and happy Pesach, both materially and spiritually.

## 813

813

B.H. 6 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the day of the Hillula, 2 Nissan: Regarding your eldest daughter, she should live and be well, who is 16 years old, and you ask what she should occupy herself with now that she has finished her studies at the Yesodei HaTorah school:

I have heard that there is [...] a school for G-d-fearing young women as is proper, and certainly you can clarify this accurately on the spot. If this is the case, it is worthwhile to enroll her there. Surely, in time, in addition to the knowledge and self-improvement she will gain, she will certainly be able to influence her surroundings there as well.

Regarding your physical livelihood, surely the Ribono shel Olam will help. Generally speaking, our Sages have said that one should not be perturbed by temporary straits and pressures. This is all the more so when we consider the people of our country in the past, who witnessed open miracles and also saw that money is a lie and physical assets are vanity, etc.—there is no reason to be perturbed by this at all.

Even though it is understood that straits and pressures cause confusion and interfere with many matters, and primarily with the avodah of Hashem, one must pray specifically about this. For when "from the straits I called out to Hashem," then "He answered me with the expansiveness of Hashem"—first an expansiveness in spirituality, where the distractions of physical straits are diminished, and subsequently, an expansiveness is created in physical matters as well.

The days of Pesach are auspicious for this, as it is called the festival of the Exodus from Mitzrayim (Egypt)—an exodus from the straits and limitations of the sitra achra, and even from the straits and limitations of holiness, as is explained in Chassidic discourse in many places.

Regarding your involvement in the field of kosher education, you write that one goes around all day and comes home with almost nothing.

It is astonishing to what extent the sayings of our holy Nesi'im [...] even when they are known and contemplated, in the end, people think that it refers to someone else, not to themselves.

Surely you know the saying of the Baal Shem Tov about doing one favor, one time, in spiritual or physical matters. And if the Shechinah brings down a literal "part of G-d from above" to exert itself—as per the saying of the Rashbatz—in a sack of flesh and bones [...] for the sake of one action or one favor, how much more so should each and every one of us be happy with our lot when the Ribono shel Olam grants us the merit and success to perform such actions many, many times in a single day.

This is also explained in my general letter of 10 Kislev of this year.

Since others among anash are also in doubt regarding this, please be kind enough to publicize the content of these lines, and it will serve as a response to them as well.

As you requested, when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention all those you wrote about for whatever each of them requires. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit to bring good news regarding all of the above.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 814

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Leib HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the day of the Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab] n.e., along with your twenty pages of memoirs. You did the right thing by recording them, and you should certainly continue doing so. I have already written many times regarding such matters to your brother, the esteemed Chossid, etc., R' Refael Nachman, may he live, emphasizing the necessity and importance of this. Regarding your question as to whether to publish this in *Bitaon Chabad* or in the *Pardes HaTemimim* booklet—the time has not yet permitted me to read them, but in the course of time, I will, G-d willing, answer this as well. In any case, continue with the recordings, as mentioned above.

As we approach the upcoming *Chag HaMatzos*, I would like to wish you and your family, may they live, that you celebrate it with *kashrus* and joy. According to what is explained in many places, the *Yomim Tovim* bestow influence upon the days that follow them until the next *regel*, as is also explained in *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe HaZaken, *Parshas Bracha* 94b, may this influence be drawn into your home and surroundings throughout the days of the year as well.

Now, there (in the aforementioned *Likutei Torah*), the discussion concerns the level of *bitul* present in all the *moadim*, and consequently, it is only necessary to draw it down until the next *regel*. This is not the case, however, regarding the matters unique to each *moed*, which are drawn down throughout the entire year. This is especially true regarding *Chag HaPesach*, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, in a *sicha* from *Chag HaPesach* 5703: "The illumination of all the *moadim* shines every day, but the illumination of *Chag HaPesach* is drawn down constantly."

To explain this briefly: In general, *Shavuos* is the concept of Torah, the time of the Giving of the Torah. *Sukkos* is, in general, the concept of *mitzvos*, and their totality is the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, the *makifim* (see *Tanya*, Chapter 5), as it is written, "I have placed My words in your mouth and covered you in the shadow of My hand." *Pesach*, the time of our freedom, is the concept of *emunah*, as the *Zohar* states that *matzah* is the "food of faith." Now, the matters of Torah and *mitzvos* are dependent on time and place, whereas *emunah* is a constant *mitzvah* and the foundation of all Torah and *mitzvos*, and this is well understood.

With blessings for a kosher and happy *Chag HaPesach*,

**M. Schneerson**

I have just read your recordings; they are more suited for *Pardes HaTemimim* than for *Bitaon*. You should certainly continue with them.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 816

Following up on my first letter of today, it is necessary to clarify exactly the agenda of the Sephardic assembly you wrote about. It is understood that it would be difficult for those who fear Hashem to rely on a candidate who finds favor in the eyes of the aforementioned person—and a word to the wise is sufficient.

## 1817

1817

B”H, 15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
Rabbi Menachem Zev Halevi,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 10 Iyar and the one preceding it, dated 2 Iyar. Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in the students’ progress in their study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus, as well as the improvement in the situation of those for whom you sent a *pidyon nefesh* on my behalf. May Hashem grant you success in the future as well, so that you may always report only good news, in a revealed and manifest way, regarding all that transpires within your four cubits and in your portion of the world at large.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the addition of students to *Tomchei Temimim* in Montreal: It is already known from the commentary on the *Mishnayos* by the Rambam, and cited in Chassidus, that a child is drawn to study not through commands, and certainly not through the rod, but rather by giving him sweets, etc. And specifically, those for which **he** has a sense at the stage he is currently in, not for the sake of the future—even though a child in general is capable of matters of *kabbalas ol* and *kafiyah*, etc. And all the more so in our current case, where this is the order that must be followed...

This letter was delayed. In the meantime, I received the *sefer* *Vayaged Yaakov*, and your letters from the 14th and 18th of this month. I look forward to hearing good news regarding the visit with Mr. Shazar. Thank you in advance.

With blessings—awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 18

18

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Yesterday, your son, may he live, visited me, and we spoke at length regarding the matters I discussed with you, may you live. May it be the will of Hashem that it be for the benefit of the many, especially since in two weeks the convention of the Rabbinical Council will take place, in which your son, the Rabbi, may he live, is also participating. I requested of him and encouraged him to utilize his influence there in all these matters.

However, your son, the Rabbi, may he live, does not believe very much in his own influence. Furthermore, he assesses the situation in rather gloomy colors, which, as a result, weakens the energy for action in this regard—as is explained in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 26, regarding the effect of sadness (as opposed to bitterness, as discussed there in Chapter 31).

Certainly, you, too, from your side, will stir his spirit and uplift him. It is well known that when one engages in matters of Torah and mitzvos, one is fulfilling the mission of the "Supernal Man," and at such a time, "a person’s agent is like himself," as explained in Likutei Torah, Parshas Vayikra. Consequently, success is also added.

Seeing the relationship your son, the Rabbi, may he live, has with you, I am confident that your words on this matter will make a strong impression on him. It is already well known, as the prophet said regarding the generation of Moshiach, that even the weak shall say, "I am a hero," especially those who have merited to be influential among circles of the sons and daughters of Israel.

Your letter of 4 Tammuz was received, in which you write regarding your health. I will mention you for a complete and speedy recovery when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about the doctors' opinion, the statement of the Tzemach Tzedek is already well known: that the Torah gave the doctor permission **to heal**, but not, Heaven forbid, to make things heavy on the heart. When one strengthens one's trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, one draws this down into actual, visible, and revealed good.

With blessings for long, good years—for you and your wife, may they live—and for much nachas from all your offspring, may they live, in good health.

## 619

B.H., 11 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, etc., R. Zelig, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, I received your letter of 13 Sivan. I was especially happy to read that you have become engaged, and that your wedding will take place at the end of the summer, in a good and auspicious hour. However, you did not mention the exact date of the wedding.

Regarding your writing that you do not have time for *kvius itim* (fixed times for Torah study) beyond three times a week and on Shabbos—first of all, one must find at least ten to fifteen minutes every single day for *kvius itim* for Torah, and when there is a desire, one can find them. Furthermore, you should memorize several chapters of Mishnayos and at least one chapter of Tanya, so that when you go to work and return home, you can review them by heart. This will bring you success not only in matters related to your spiritual life, but also in your material life.

I hope to hear good news, and I wish you happiness, and especially my wishes of *mazal tov* on your engagement.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 21

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and diligent communal worker,
Rabbi [Name]… may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Some time ago I received your letter, which was a response to my own. Regarding what you wrote concerning the communal activist from your city who visited me, and that you do not know what he reported regarding [Name]… may he live:

The aforementioned individual spoke only well—regarding his talents, his conduct, and his affairs. However, he expressed regret that [Name] does not utilize his talents for communal matters in general, and for the cause of chinuch in particular. In this, I agreed with him, and even more so—knowing and having heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the magnitude of this matter in all places and at all times, and certainly in our generation, which is a "desolate place," and certainly when one is located in such a place. To this, I did not find a response in your letter either. Especially since you also write that his business is mired in large debts, and we thank Hashem that he is now paying off some of his debts; if so, the argument of "Why is this me?" [i.e., why should I be the one to take this on?] becomes even more prominent and emphasized.

Regarding what you wrote that he gives a shiur in Gemara, etc.—it is known that "the camel is loaded according to its strength." Furthermore, giving a shiur in Gemara—while the importance of this is understood—is not comparable to matters of chinuch, especially matters connected to practical mitzvos. For this is a *mitzvah overes* (a fleeting mitzvah), and not only that, but it is also a "fleeting generation"—that is, the youth—for if not now, when? Further elaboration for someone like you is surely superfluous.

And even though you speak in his defense regarding [Name]… may he live, my hope is strong that this is only in your letter to me, but regarding [Name]… may he live, you will use all your influence upon him, and also increase the number of friends [who will influence him], so that he recognizes his role and what is incumbent upon him in a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, which even overrides Torah study, as per the ruling of our Sages in Moed Katan 9b.

May it be the will of Hashem that he succeeds quickly, and as mentioned—for this is a fleeting mitzvah and a fleeting generation.

Surely you gathered during the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz, the days of redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the head of Israel. May Hashem grant success to each and every one, for "the body follows the head." May from here on in, the obstacles in the work of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and in strengthening and expanding the matters and institutions for which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, labored and toiled in particular, be diminished and nullified, and may we walk in his paths, *nesiah u’matan*.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Rabbi [Name]… may he live, visited me. He will surely convey my regards, and also regarding what he promised me to do, to the best of his ability, for the Yeshiva Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in [City]. Surely you, too, from your side, will strengthen and assist in this.

## 825

B"H, 9 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Committee of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure and joy that I read the minutes of your meeting, which indicate that you are already organizing a program and practical work. And although "joy is fixed in my heart" on one hand, "weeping is fixed in my heart" on the other, as there are many who are missing from the list of participants. However, it is my hope that in the course of time, these too will join you, for "the Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that could hold blessing other than peace." Naturally, they should join you without compromising on fundamental matters.

Regarding the present, I have come to urge you regarding the bright and clear day, the upcoming 18th of Elul. I am certain you will utilize it with the energy and vitality that are characteristic of the young, to spread the idea of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, whose birthday—spiritually and physically—is this day of the 18th. And to spread this idea in the widest circles, even those who, for the time being, are still far from our surroundings.

It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the difference between the "world's" [approach] and Chabad: the great ones of the "world" would sit in their homes and their places, and anyone who yearned for Torah would come to them to enjoy the radiance of their Torah. Not so the Baal Shem Tov and onwards; they established the order where the Baal Shem Tov would travel around to the towns, not waiting for people to come to him and say "we are standing to speak the word of Hashem." Rather, he himself, in his own honor, would wear out his feet traveling from place to place, from city to city, and from village to village, spreading the Torah of the words of the living G-d (Sefer HaSichos, Summer 5700, Acharon Shel Pesach at the day's meal).

2) Organize a work plan for how to utilize the upcoming month of Tishrei, as mentioned above, by traveling to various places—whether in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, during the Days of Awe, or during the days of our festival. The main thing is that it should be done in an organized fashion, and in a way that [reaches] the greatest number of people and the largest number of men, women, and children.

3) Special attention in all of the above is required for our brethren from Yemen, Persia, etc. On one hand, they currently have no knowledge of the Chassidic movement, its Torah, and its ways. On the other hand, they are highly capable—due to their fear of Heaven, their connection to the study of Kabbalah, and their faith in Tzaddikim—of receiving everything they are shown from the Torah of Chassidus that our holy Rebbes have bequeathed to us.

I am interested in knowing the details of the plan you have presented for this. It would be most appropriate to consult on the above with the directors of Agudas Chassidei Chabad. For although a large part of the aforementioned work, which involves the travel that requires extra energy and vitality, is placed upon the shoulders of the young, on the other hand, as our Sages said, "the destruction of the elders is a building," and all the more so, the "building of the elders is a building."

For the time being, I do not have sufficient means at my disposal to cover the expenses associated with this work. However, as my desire to participate from here in the expenses of such a lofty matter is strong, and since it is not possible for several reasons to send money from here, I am enclosing a certificate for parcels, and our Sages have said that "that which is worth money is like money."

In a separate envelope, I am sending you a segment from the Sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, as well as a booklet on Chabad public activism that was just published. All of this is via airmail; please acknowledge receipt of the above.

With a blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* to all the members, may they live, to them, their households, and all that is theirs—may they all stand [upon] the blessing for a good and sweet year.

Awaiting good news.

B"H, 11 Elul, 5714

Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Bnei Brak branch,

## 827

827

[18 Elul 5714]

Regarding your question asking for my opinion on participating in a Torah publication: it depends on the nature of the publication. If it is intended to legitimize various matters (as is well known, the approach of certain circles is to adopt the Chazal dictum "the power of leniency is preferable" as their slogan)—then we are already distressed by the earlier instances of this. However, if it is a matter of "magnifying Torah and making it glorious," then it is understood that the decision changes accordingly. In most cases, this can only be clarified through close acquaintance with those who are at the helm and those who determine the direction of the publication.

In the vast majority of cases, this only becomes clear after the appearance of at least the first issue. May Hashem guide you on the straight and good path, and there is no "good" other than the perfect Torah [studied] with fear of Heaven.

Published in the *Yagdil Torah* Jerusalem collection, issue 27, at the beginning.

By the way, please let me know if the copy of our *sicha* has been printed in *Machanaim*. The transcript was sent here from Tzeirei Agudas Chabad some time ago, and I am sure you interpreted the lack of a proper response as intended—namely, that it may be printed without changes.

I am sure you will publicize this in an appropriate manner as well, in order to "arouse the jealousy of scribes" in other places.

And as we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, may you and your wife—may they live—be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

With blessings,

P.S. I have received the *chovros* for the *Yomim Nora'im* and Pesach of 5713. Thank you for this, and a request for the future.

## 830

[1954]

...Regarding the question of whether it is possible to be a religious Jew without a beard: the phrasing of the question is consistent with the situation of your son, may he live, and I believe I have already alluded to this in my previous letter. Nevertheless, I will briefly address it once more:

Every person is a complete structure, **alive**. In resolving any question, one must take into account this living person, who is not an automaton; consequently, a general solution is not always applicable to him.

To explain my words further: a house with one story or two stories—it is still a house. When a second or third story is built upon it, that is an addition to the existing house. But if, after the construction, one wishes to demolish the additional story, it is understood that the demolition will destroy all the stories, and even the foundation, since all the stories have already been unified by mortar, etc. How much more so if one wishes to demolish the bottom story, for that demolition will destroy the stories that are above it.

Without entering into the resolution of the question of what place wearing a beard occupies among the 613 mitzvos of the holy Torah (and it is known to all that many G-d-fearing men among Ashkenazic Jewry and others are without a beard), when one approaches the resolution of the question regarding a private individual, one must take into account his own situation.

The decision to wear a beard was reached by your son, may he live, out of an internal *hisorerus*. It would be difficult to clarify whether this is, for him, the "first story" in the aforementioned analogy, or an "additional story" built upon matters that preceded it. I doubt whether it is even necessary to probe into his soul to clarify the matter, for any digging into the inner depths of a person's soul does not bring blessing, etc. But in any case, it is clear that in his current situation, all these matters have become a single cause that has brought him to an internal spiritual struggle, with upheavals, etc.

As I have written previously, it is incumbent upon all his relatives and friends, and all the more so upon his parents, to strengthen and encourage him with all their possibilities and abilities. My hope is that they, too, will act accordingly, since this is for the good of their son, and consequently, it is also for their own good.

And the good of their son is not merely from the standpoint that he should fulfill more mitzvos with *hiddur* according to the custom of Chassidim, but that this should add **tranquility** to his soul and strength in his walk along the path he has **chosen**, which is connected with many external obstacles and therefore requires additional strength and encouragement from every word that is precious in their eyes.

I await good tidings, and I sign with a blessing in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 831

B"H, 3 Tishrei, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Moshe, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 22 Elul, along with the two *pidyonos nefesh*—which I will read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—despite everything you have gone through, it is clear that there is no room for discouragement, Heaven forbid. Hashem is certain to fill what is lacking, and not only that, but there will also be the matter of wealth, both in *ruchniyus* and in *gashmiyus*, provided that you create the appropriate *keilim* for this—namely, by increasing your involvement in *Torah* and *mitzvos* and by engaging in the ways of nature, and by doing all of this with *simcha*, which breaks through boundaries and removes limitations.

Regarding the present matter, I have come to express my deep and great gratitude for the *Sefer Torah* that was brought about two days before *Rosh Hashanah*, and which was read from this *Rosh Hashanah*. According to *Zohar Chadash* 161b, just as Hashem looked into the *Torah* and created the world, so too, as it were, does the Jewish person—through *Torah*—create his world, and those who facilitate this are included as well, of course. May it be the will of Hashem that in this new year, you see your world renewed with goodness that is visible and revealed, regarding yourself, your wife, and all your children—may they live.

May Hashem fulfill the days of your wife’s pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time, properly and with ease.

With the blessing of *Chasimah* and *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## Chaleb

B"H, 20 Tishrei, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Yom Kippur, the main point is missing, and that is regarding your *kvius itim* (fixed times) for the study of *Toras HaChassidus*. And according to the ruling of our Sages, "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed"—to fulfill the guidance and conduct of *Toras HaChassidus*. It goes without saying that this includes keeping the three *shiurim* that are for everyone: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. Each person, according to their [ability], must add to this, especially those who do not yet have the worries of *parnassah* and can find themselves in the *ohel shel Torah* (tent of Torah).

Regarding the matter you wrote about, you must stop thinking about it entirely. If the *yetzer hara* comes with such thoughts, you should not enter into a battle with it, but rather begin to think about or study our holy Torah; for even a little light pushes away much darkness.

May Hashem help you that, in the end, you will become a *Chossid* and begin to obey.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,
Secretary

#### ***Chaleb***

Printed in the *kuntres* "Tzadik L'Melech" II, p. 141.

## 833

## 834

B"H, 14 MarCheshvan, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following yet another long hiatus in our correspondence, I have received your letter dated the 7th of MarCheshvan, in which you write that for various reasons, the number of students in your school is lower than the number of positions approved by the relevant offices, and you ask what should be done about this.

It is understood and simple that you must do everything possible—and even more than that—to increase the number of students. Regarding what you wrote, that this is not an easy task and that it is beneath the dignity of a teacher to plead with parents to have their children study in the school where he teaches:

All matters of Torah and mitzvos are not easy. Regarding all such matters, we have already been instructed by King David—even though it is said that a king who waives his honor, his honor is not waived—who said, "I will be even more lowly than this" (Shmuel II 6:22). This is especially true here, as I see no disgrace in this when the matter concerns the saving of the souls of the children of Yisrael by ensuring they are enrolled in a school with proper chinuch. When all the teachers mobilize for this purpose, they will surely succeed in filling the number of students. Only if, even after this—contrary to common sense and sound logic, and for reasons that are not understood at all—it does not succeed in filling a certain portion of the missing students, only then should you adopt the second option you wrote of, namely, for the school to "injure itself," which in human law is exempt.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

#### ***834***

From the Secretariat copy.

## 835

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, R' Avraham, may he live:

Following your long silence, I was pleased to receive your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Toldos. In it, you write that you have moved to Rishon LeZion and are engaged there in the holy work of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, bringing the hearts of Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. Surely, the attribute of Hashem is measure for measure, and even more so, that you should receive much Yiddishe nachas from all your offspring, may they live.

I was also pleased by what you wrote, that you give a shiur in the evening for the army on Neviim and Dinim. Surely, you strive to ensure that the Dinim are the halachos necessary for daily life, for this is "the whole of man: fear Hashem and keep His mitzvos."

Regarding what you wrote, that you have a shiur in the study of Chassidus on Friday night: it is surely unnecessary to remind you that this is not sufficient at all. This study must take place at least a few times during the week as well, and there is nothing that can stand in the way of the will.

With blessings,

## 836

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Avraham, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter regarding your visit to the Reshet school in Kfar Saba, and I was pleased by it. You should certainly continue to visit the other schools as well, and keep me informed of their situation.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that the visit should be conducted in ways of pleasantness and peace, without causing a stir on the spot, and certainly not in front of the students—even if you find matters there that do not align with your opinion, for it is essential that the students know to listen to the voice of their teacher and instructor.

The purpose of my writing now is to ask you to give to our friend, the esteemed R' Avraham Zvi Slonim, may he live, the seforim that he will request from you. Also, give to the esteemed R' Leib Zalmanov, may he live, the Tanya's that he will request from you, in order to give them as a gift to some of the military personnel. Thank you in advance for your efforts in this.

Surely there will be proper farbrengens in all corners of Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, on the upcoming auspicious day of 19 Kislev. I would appreciate it if you would share good news with me, in appropriate detail, regarding this.

Despite what you wrote regarding distribution, I am sorry to say that it appears it is not at the appropriate level at all.

Perhaps it would be worthwhile to conduct a sale under favorable terms for a period of time—a kind of *rasprodazha* (clearance sale)—for what benefit is there in the seforim simply sitting there, being sold in such small quantities? It is understood that even this sale—the *rasprodazha*—must be at appropriate prices, and one must be careful that people do not mistakenly say that this is the actual value of the seforim. I await good news.

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 837

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Kislev: Many thanks for the good news regarding the farbrengens held on the bright day of 19 Kislev—the day of the redemption of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), and the day of our own redemption and the liberation of our souls—both the farbrengen on the night preceding it and the farbrengen on the night following it.

According to the well-known adage from the early generations of Chassidus, that in a Chassidishe farbrengen one can accomplish great and hidden things that even the angel Michael, the minister of Israel, cannot accomplish, may Hashem grant that the aforementioned farbrengens bring to all the participants blessing and success in whatever they and their families may need.

As you requested, I will mention you and the participants at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Israel, at a time of favor. I will also mention the child... may he be healthy, and may his parents raise him to Torah, chuppah, and good deeds.

It would be appropriate for... to be meticulous in the observance of the laws of mikveh and taharas hamishpacha—that is, to immerse in a mikveh of rainwater or a spring, and not in city water that is measured and drawn through various pipes and machines. This, in particular, will draw down additional health for your children.

I trust you are reciting Tehillim every day after Shacharis—according to the monthly division—and that you are endeavoring to have your acquaintances observe this as well, as this is one of the takanos of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 840

840

B"H, 15 Teves, 5715
Brooklyn.

...moving to a new home. I reiterate my blessings that this change of place should bring a change of fortune for the good and for blessing, and that the move should be *me'ilah le'eilah* (from a higher level to a higher level), with growth in both material and spiritual matters.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the *chinuch* (dedication) of the home: although according to the *nigleh* (revealed Torah) there is room for discussion on this matter—see the *Acharonim* in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, siman 568; see there the *Magen Avraham*, sub-paragraph 5, and the *Yad Ephraim*; and also note the *Responsa Chasam Sofer*, *Yoreh Deah*, sub-paragraph 138, and *Toras HaShlamim* there [paragraph 19]—since this is a *minhag Yisrael* (custom of Israel), and there is a *maamar* from our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, "The reason for making a feast and celebration at the dedication of a home" (now found in print, and it is from the manuscript of R' P. of Shklov), one should follow the aforementioned custom. When you gather for a *farbrengen* (Chassidic gathering), it will be beneficial both materially and spiritually.

And surely you are aware of our custom to affix the *mezuzos* immediately upon entering the home. It is understood that this is done without a *bracha*. However, upon the completion of thirty days, one removes one *mezuzah* to have it checked, and it is permitted to replace it with a better one; consequently, one affixes the new one with a *bracha* and intends for it to cover those on all the other doors as well...

#### ***840***

A portion is printed in *Sefer HaMinhagim - Chabad*, p. 81, and in its entirety in the *kuntres* "Tzadik LaMelech" 2, p. 144.

**There is room for discussion:** See also *Igros Kodesh* of the *Admur HaTzemach Tzedek*, Vol. 2, Letter 12.

**Maamar of Rabbeinu HaZaken:** *Hanachos R' P.*, p. 79.

**When you gather:** See also above, Vol. 15, Letter 5329, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 841

[Supplement to letter 3202 above, Vol. 18]

B"H, 19 Teves, 5715
Brooklyn

To the illustrious Rabbi, man of action and many accomplishments, R' Nechemya, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your prompt letter of 18 Teves, as well as the one preceding it. I also received the sefer *Toldos Adam* that you published, and I thank you for the gift.

Regarding what you wrote in your latest letter: the meeting of the Vaad Hameuchad took place a few days ago, and with effort, the lobbying succeeded in allocating one thousand shekel for their yeshiva, according to the current situation.

It is understood that this information is "behind the curtain," and therefore I am in doubt whether it is advisable for you to publicize that you already knew about this beforehand—especially in light of the words of the Mishnah (Sanhedrin 3:7), "And from where [do we know] that once he has left..." However, in order to set your mind at ease, I am informing you of this.

After all this, I am somewhat surprised by you, for it is written, "You shall surely help him" (*azov ta’azov imo*), and judging by the discussion at that meeting mentioned above, it seems that on your part, there was no effort made.

In any case, may it be the will of Hashem that you utilize this support to increase Torah and glorify it, in such a way that your students will fulfill the instruction of our Mishnah: that their fear of sin precedes their wisdom, and their deeds exceed their wisdom, and may you see good fruit from your labor.

Regarding your comment and question—what is the basis, the interpretation, and the content of the title of the bright day, 19 Kislev, as "Chag HaChagim"...

I happened to read your article in *HaPardes* for the month of Teves 5715. You should examine the *Tzofnas Paneach* by the Gaon the Rogatchover on Rambam, *Hilchos Sefer Torah* and *Hilchos Megillah*, where, in his characteristic way, he explains several matters—including those you touched upon in your article—with wondrous flashes of insight.

Your observation regarding what is written in the sefer *Kadur Katan*, that it refers to Rabbeinu HaZaken—you observed correctly. The basis for those who garble the text there is incomprehensible.

- By the way: *Kadur Katan* is the name of the introduction to the sefer *Eis L'Daber*. Regarding Rabbeinu HaZaken, it is found inside the sefer in the glosses to part *Shaar Orah*, 6.

With blessings for success in your holy work, awaiting good news.

## 442

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu Harav Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter received after Shabbos Parshas Shemos, I was pleased to read that you have become more involved in the work of the Reshet of the institutions named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael. Surely, this will expand the channel and the vessels for success in this holy work itself, as well as for success in your personal matters and those of your entire family, may they live.

It is surprising that you do not mention that other members of anash also assist the Reshet administration from time to time in an appropriate manner. I hope that when you encourage those members of anash who are suited for this, they will assist even more.

Regarding the matter of the restaurant in connection with the school where they study, in my opinion, it is very important. Since, as you write, 200 liras are needed for this at present, I hope that you will surely be able to arrange for the appropriate offices to provide them. In any event, some scrip has been sent as a contribution toward the aforementioned, as well as toward the expenses connected with the students' gathering on the day of the Hillula, 10 Shevat. However, so as not to differentiate between one school and another—from here—and also so as not to alter the established procedures, the scrip has been sent to the esteemed Rabbi D. Chanzin, may he live.

I hope that you are working to expand your borders with students—both boys and girls—with the appropriate energy, and may Hashem grant you success.

Regarding what you wrote—that there is a proposal for you to work certain hours of the day regarding printing and printing type—this does not seem right to me. Aside from the fact that it will take away from your time, the main thing that will be lacking is your concentration and dedication to the work of the Reshet in its various departments; it causes a scattering of the soul (*pizur hanefesh*) through working in another field. Consistent with what I have written previously regarding your "gate," both in the way of *mil'eila l'tata* (from above to below) and in the way of *mil'tata l'eila* (from below to above), in my opinion, you should dedicate all your time to the affairs of the Reshet. And my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the owner of the Reshet, is guaranteed to pay your reward many times over...

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**
