## 844

844

*[Supplement to Letter 3,168 above, Vol. 18]*

B”H, 24 Shevat, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that so-and-so moved his residence from the village and is living elsewhere due to the incident, G-d forbid—in my opinion, he acted foolishly. This is, of course, understood from the copy of the Igros Kodesh in my letter to the village committee from two weeks ago.

The complaints regarding the Yeshiva... are increasing from time to time... and it seems that no attention is being paid to the needs of the bochurim, no attention is being paid to bringing in bochurim from other yeshivos, and all matters are handled in a haphazard, "if it happens, it happens" manner (aside from matters of finances and debts—which the creditors are pressing about. I have already written many times to several Anash institutions that, in my opinion, in an institution of the Rebbe, the order should be the opposite: one must improve the spiritual matters, and this is a **prerequisite** for improving the material conditions).

And in truth, this is not surprising, for one who is not under any authority and everything depends on his own good will, and who is gifted by Hashem with the power of speech and articulation—and consequently explains to others and describes absurd situations as if they were, on the contrary, necessary matters—then his punishment is measure for measure: that even regarding himself, he lives in error. As for what he is obligated to do with effort of body and soul, he comes up with a few excuses as to why he is exempt, and consequently, he does not involve himself with the bochurim. And if he sometimes grabs onto a promise that he will involve himself with certain students and will meet with other students, etc., it is like a plant that grows overnight and withers overnight, etc. Rather, since a new matter is dear to him, as is the nature of people, when a new matter arises he immediately volunteers that he will meet with the students and guide them, etc., and when a short time passes, the matter is nullified. And with his power of articulation, he explains to himself and to others the reasons for this, and it is understood that everyone is to blame except for himself.

And even after it was printed in *Hayom Yom* several years ago that the way to examine all these things is not the clothing or the style of the *surtuk*, but rather the test is—that if a matter of *avodah* and activity is nullified, the reason for this is from the *yetzer hara* and not the opposite (*Hayom Yom* for 23 Sivan)—and it is visible even to the physical eye that he is not guiding and not meeting [with students], etc., and the results of this are also visible in the students; despite all this, he swims around in the world of speech, happy with inventions and intellectual sharpness, explaining in letters what so-and-so should do, etc.

What will be the end of such conduct—I will admit and not be ashamed, I do not know. But the damage to the students... is visible in the past and the present, and if only it would improve, at the very least in the future, and at the very least in the coming months, if it is not possible in the immediate weeks.

It is understood that I do not want...

You surely saw my letter to Aguch before the day of the *hillula*. And may it be the will of Hashem that the ascent of the *baal hillula*—beginning from the Shabbos before the day of the *hillula*, and especially from the day of the *hillula* and onwards—will act upon us all...

#### ***844***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L’Melech* 3, p. 51.

**The incident:** Above, Vol. 18, Letter 3,168, that a student was killed by Arab infiltrators.

**It is understood that I do not want...:** As above, Vol. 18, Letter 3,168.

**My letter to Aguch:** Above, Vol. 18, 3,149.

## Chameh

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent individual, engaged in communal affairs, R’ Chaim Zusya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar, as well as the one preceding it, along with the enclosures. I mentioned you and your household, may they live, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during a time of favor.

I am grateful for what you wrote regarding the various matters, and surely you will continue to act in this manner in the future; whatever you detail in this regard is commendable.

Regarding what you wrote about distribution—printing prospectuses, catalogs, advertisements, and so on: It is understood that since there is apparently no income from the entire distribution effort—and in any case, it is not known here to be otherwise—one should not increase the aforementioned expenses. What I wrote regarding advertisements and the like was not intended to mean that expenses should be increased significantly, but rather through notices in shuls, at bookstores, and similar venues. It was not intended to print prospectuses and the like, which, according to the experience with all the affairs of anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, has always resulted in expenses immediately mounting to hundreds of liras, and in the vast majority of cases, within a short time, to thousands. This has already occurred in matters where several people wrote to me clearly that the expense would be such-and-such, providing signs and proofs for it, yet two months later, when the matter was put into practice, the expense was **five** times that amount. This is not an exaggeration, but an actual occurrence; I have experienced this myself. The same applies to articles in newspapers regarding the seforim—in every country, the custom is that when one copy of the sefer is provided, an article is written (provided, of course, that the sefer is interesting and there is an acquaintance with the editorial staff). If it is possible to do this in the aforementioned case as well, that is good; but if this will incur additional expenses, it should not be done, for then there is no restraint to their spirit, and it appears there is nothing to hold them back.

The gathering of the students of the Reshet schools in Kfar Chabad is a very great thing. In accordance with this, it is understood that the lack of communication—even in such a matter—between the other schools and the school [in Lod] is most painful.

Regarding what you wrote, that the reason the initial thought and goal was Lod, and in the end they found a place in the Kfar—this is irrelevant to the aforementioned, for just as they came from other schools, they [from Lod] could also have participated. It is already known from the letter of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe that one must be extremely careful to avoid machlokes, especially a machlokes which, according to the opinion of those who are arguing, is "for the sake of Heaven," particularly in our Holy Land, whose destruction in the time of the Second Beis Hamikdash was due to Kamtza and Bar Kamtza, etc. I fear that the lack of development of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod is partly due to this very thing—that anash cannot communicate among themselves, and consequently, the concept of "salvation through many counselors" is absent.

Surely you will continue in the future with the matters you wrote about, and may the others you mention as being active in this also increase their efforts.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, as well as regarding your personal matters, and especially for the health of your wife, may she live.

**M. Schneerson**

***

**Chameh**
From a photocopy of the letter.

**Letter of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe:** Printed in Igros Kodesh, Letter 32.

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5715

## 848

B"H, 19 Adar, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... Regarding the general customs of the Chabad leadership, the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: one must apply these things to oneself, not to others...

May it be the will of Hashem that from here on, the idea will be internalized (*zal zich opgleign*) that the Reshet institutions are educational institutions for the children of Yisrael, and that for this type of education, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, dedicated his will, his life-force, and his energy. Those who have any connection to this—at the very least, during their free time, when they would otherwise read a newspaper or engage in idle talk—should curtail such activities and instead contemplate the affairs of the Reshet. They should dedicate those moments to taking an interest in the matters of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in order to improve and develop them, rather than engaging in criticism for its own sake, without purpose.

It is understood that in all of the above, my intention is not directed at any single individual, but rather at many of anash who are abroad, and even at anash who are in Eretz Yisrael, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year...

## 849

B"H, 3rd day of Chol Hamoed Pesach, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Menachem Zev Halevi, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby confirm receipt of your note, together with the *Siddur Tefillah Tefillah L’Moshe*, which, as you requested, has been returned to you by registered mail and has surely arrived by now.

By the way, regarding the author: you have surely seen his book *Mishkanos Avir Yaakov*, which contains astonishing stories. Several years ago, I showed this book—which had come into my hands at the time—to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. From his words, I understood that in Lubavitch, they did not hold of this author, though I do not know the reasons clearly.

Also, your registered letter—which you began writing on the 11th of Nissan—has been received, along with its enclosure.

You have surely seen the supplement to the *Haggadah Shel Pesach* containing the transcript of the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the *matzos* and the six species placed upon them. My intention in what I wrote there regarding those who struggle with this is also in reference to the *Responsa* printed in the book *Kocho D’Rabi Eliezer* by the Rashbi. Perhaps it is worth informing the author of this, for the excuse brought in the aforementioned *Responsa* is, with all due respect, not acceptable.

I was pleased to hear that the aforementioned individual is studying *Tanya* with his group and is also beginning to disseminate these *maayanos* in his surroundings—and therefore, I hope that the aforementioned [book/matter] will also be received by him in the best possible way.

With blessings for success in all his endeavors and for good tidings in revealed goodness.

Due to the sanctity of the *Moed*, the Rebbe did not sign personally, and I sign on his behalf,

**A. Quint**
**Secretary**

## 57

B”H, 11 Tammuz, 5715
Brooklyn.

...I have already said to several of Anash that I am astonished by their conduct over the past five years (though it is possible they acted this way even before, but I am unaware of it). It is written and simple in our holy Torah, the Torah of life, that first and foremost, every individual must concern himself with what he is obligated to do, specifically in matters of Torah and mitzvos. Yet, I see that their contemplation is only on what *I* should do. Every morning, they wake up with various desires and strange and unusual suggestions regarding what I can add in the matters of the teachings of Chassidus—such as saying maamarim, printing maamarim, printing sichos, etc., etc., with innovations in the revealed Torah, in public communal work, etc., etc.

And not only has it not occurred to anyone that perhaps they, too, could do something in this regard, but they even strengthen their own sense of satisfaction: "I have fulfilled my duty completely, for it is a wonderful suggestion, and if the suggestion is accepted, the situation will be rectified immediately, etc., etc." Consequently, they can return to their own affairs, etc., etc. When one considers the actions on the part of Anash, it is truly staggering.

Especially since it is surely known to each of them what our Alter Rebbe demanded in his response to the holy Rabbi, Moreinu HaRav Shneur of Karlin: that every Chossid must act for himself. And not as the simple interpretation of the verse, "The tzaddik shall live by his faith"—read not *yichyeh* (shall live), but *yechayeh* (shall give life). And if in the time of the Alter Rebbe they were required not to rely on him to fulfill their obligations for them, how much more so in these days.

At first, I judged them favorably, as per the instruction of our Sages, that this was due to the strength and intensity of their faith. But then I saw that regarding their own households and regarding material matters—such as issues of parnassah and health—their faith is not so strong, and they do not rely on [others], but act themselves and also take other measures.

What I know of how it used to be is that they would come with detailed suggestions and ask for an opinion and a blessing, etc., and nothing more. All the rest—that is, finding a suitable proposal and bringing it to fruition in the appropriate manner—was done by Anash, by friends, and by those whose hearts were touched by the explanation of Chassidus on "Love your fellow as yourself." And in the course of these five years, I have not had the merit to see this movement and activity among the baalei batim, among those who are mekushar, etc.

I have written at length about all this because it is an *eis ratzon*, a time of favor, when there is certainly no element of *kapida* (strictness)—similar to what is explained in the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Toras Shalom, p. 61), regarding Simchas Torah. The main thing is that since it is an *eis ratzon*, perhaps these words will have an effect, as they have been drawn down into the world of speech and also into the world of action (in writing), and will lead to an improvement of the situation in practice. From this, it is understood and simple that you have permission to publicize this in the appropriate circles.

With the blessing of Chag HaGeulah.

## 8558

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5715

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of this date: I was pleased to hear that you are strong in your bitachon in Hashem and are not at all impressed by the [...] that has arisen due to the purchase of your home, for there is no basis for such concern, chas v’shalom. Regarding what you wrote about Mr. ... and the way to influence him: it is well known in such matters to speak again and again, etc., as in the well-known story from Avos D’Rabbi Nosson, etc., that even water wears away stone—and how much more so the "heart of stone" of Bnei Yisrael, where the description of "stone" is merely a borrowed term, and those who are familiar with this require no proof.

With blessings for a healthy and happy summer and for good tidings in all the above.

## 861

B"H, 1 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, R' Yitzchak, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your urgent letter of 26 Menachem Av, and those preceding it:

1) Regarding your question as to whether to approach party representatives in the municipality to support your requests: It is surprising that you ask this, as this has been the practice for several years regarding the various affairs of Chabad, which are non-partisan. This is despite the fact that it is understood and simple that your school must be without any partisan affiliation whatsoever, as I have written many times.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the differing opinions concerning the hiring of teachers: This, too, is not the first year this issue has arisen. All members of the Reshet administration must decide, for just as in other matters of institutional management—there is an expert for every profession, but the matter is not a dictatorship of one individual, as is understood and customary in many institutions and affairs throughout the world.

3) Regarding the matter of your secretariat: Here, too, I am puzzled by a question regarding a simple matter: the role of a secretary is to record and report on everything that occurs, but it is not mandatory that he himself participate in all delegations, meetings, visits to various offices, etc. He can receive the information regarding this from those whose responsibility it is, and then write it down. This, too, is what is practiced and customary throughout the entire world.

4) Regarding your son, Yosef Simcha, may he live: Consult with a doctor among your friends, and if he agrees, then he may begin attending cheder. May Hashem grant him success, together with his wife, may she live, in raising all their children to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Surely you are holding meetings with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., R' Binyomin Avrohom Gorodetzky, may he live, regarding all matters of the Reshet, as he will surely do everything in his power regarding this.

2, 5, 6 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

## 854

B"H, 19 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter asking for advice on how to better understand your studies: The advice has already been provided by our Sages of blessed memory: "If one says, 'I have labored but not found,' do not believe him," and conversely, "If one says, 'I have found without laboring,' do not believe him." Thus, the matter depends solely on one's will—to exert oneself with all of one's strength.

And since in all things one requires *siyata d'shmaya*, be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, giving a *frank* or two to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*, reciting *Tehillim* every day according to the monthly division after morning *davening*, and studying *Torah* of *Chassidus* with desire and will, and influencing your friends to do the same. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With blessings for success in *Talmud Torah* with *yiras shamayim*, and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

And even for the male teachers—naturally, topics appropriate for them.

## 658

[1955?]

Notes regarding the book as a whole.

The manner in which the subjects are presented in the book assumes that the reader is already "deep in the thick of things" regarding this problem, and merely requires a dialectical analysis (*shakla v’tarya*) to clarify the conclusion, resolve contradictions, and so on.

Understandably, only a select few possess such knowledge. And even they, after a short time, will not retain in their memory all the details necessary to understand the matters.

It would be highly worthwhile and correct to include an introduction at the beginning of the book, in which the question is explained (for the vast majority of *bnei Torah*, the very existence of this question will be the most surprising revelation in the book), as well as the main points of the various approaches to its resolution.

Through this, the circle of those who understand the subject matter will be greatly expanded.

It should be explained in the preface or introduction—or at the very least, noted—that the discussion of the core question is found (and begins) in the **last** quarter of the book. If there were no difficulties in doing so, it would be worthwhile to change this, in order to facilitate, as much as possible, the grasp and understanding of the scope of the material.

And I offer my appreciation for the fact that you bring the words of the authors being discussed in their entirety, so that there is no need to search for the books themselves.

Surely you will have the proofs proofread once more, as they are riddled with errors of omission and addition, etc.

Regarding what you wrote—that by crossing the International Date Line at the moment of *neshikah* (sunset) on *Erev Shabbos* and *Shabbos*, and doing this several times, the *os* (sign) of *Shabbos* would be nullified for him—this is impossible.

It is *tzarich iyun* (requires further study) what the practical difference is whether there are seven days without *Shabbos* or seven hundred days without *Shabbos*. And why is this impossible? Especially according to the Ramban (*Shemos* 20:8), that every day there is the mitzvah to "remember the day of *Shabbos*." (Although even according to him, this remembrance is not a complete *os*, as one is still obligated in *tefillin*).

And it is obvious that one cannot forbid this crossing, nor compare it to delaying a *bris milah* so as not to subsequently desecrate the *Shabbos* with the necessary preparations (according to the *Ra’ah* and *Rashba*, cited in the *Ran* to *Shabbos* 134b), or to the prohibition against departing on a caravan if it will lead to subsequent *Shabbos* desecration. See also Rashi (*Sukkah* 25b, s.v. *shechal*): "One who is engaged in a *mitzvah* is exempt..."—for in all these cases, the obligation exists, but a cause delays or permits it, which is not the case here.

There is a slight similarity to *Menachos* (41a), "a trick to exempt oneself," etc. See there in *Tosafos* and in *Hagahos Maimoniyos* at the end of *Hilchos Tzitzis*.

See also *Shu"t Tzemach Tzedek*, *Yoreh Deah* 92; *Tzofnas Paneach*, 2nd edition, 57, end of column 4.

Nevertheless, it is not the same; in the aforementioned cases, the *mitzvah* exists in reality, whereas here—there is no *Shabbos* on the sixth day or the first day.

I have since seen what you cited in your book to the *Mishnah Berurah*.

***

Regarding what you wrote above—that it is possible for all of *Bnei Yisrael* to cross the Date Line at the aforementioned time and for this *Shabbos* to be nullified entirely:

One should note the *Mechilta* at the beginning of *Parshas Tisa*, which emphasizes: "Behold the nations that surrounded *Eretz Yisrael* and the *Yisraelim* desecrated [the *Shabbos*]..." Regarding this, the *Tzofnas Paneach* of the Rogatchover Gaon (the book is not currently at hand) explains that it is specifically in such a case, where *Shabbos* is nullified entirely, that a verse is needed (as only based on this can one understand why the *Mechilta* cites such a remote possibility). Similarly, it is *tzarich iyun* in such a case—did *Yisrael* put on *tefillin* on the *Yom Kippur* of the year the *Beis Hamikdash* was completed, given that they ate and drank on it (*Moed Katan* 9a)? See *Tzemach Tzedek* on *Moed Katan* (Chapter 3, Mishnah 4) that the *os* is for the prohibition of work, and it is possible that even on this *Yom Kippur*, they did not perform work (except for the *Kohanim* offering the sacrifices; and perhaps also those cooking, etc. (but not **all** of *Yisrael*)—is that considered *melachas ochel nefesh*?). But this is not the place to elaborate.

However, this situation where all of *Yisrael* would cross the Date Line at once is impossible, according to what is written in the *Sefer Hamitzvos* of the Rambam (Positive Mitzvah 153), that Heaven forbid for Hashem to do this, for He promised, etc. In *Tzofnas Paneach*, *Hilchos Kiddush Hachodesh*, end of Chapter 5, he points to a source for this from *Bava Basra* 115b and *Horayos* 6b. His intent is *tzarich iyun*, for even if the tribes of Ephraim and Menashe are found at the ends of the earth, the land of their inheritance stands forever, and if so, the tribe is not destroyed.

***

Regarding what you wrote to resolve the words of the *Chazon Ish* in his interpretation of the opinion of the *Ra’ah*, etc., and his conclusion regarding the question of the Date Line: he enters into immense forced interpretations, and yet he does not provide a remedy, as he writes in many places in his book...

Regarding the logic of "dragging" (*grirah*)—even though a distant example is found for this regarding one who sanctifies a limb upon which the soul depends.

A closer example is found in *Hilchos Eruvin*, where once one enters the *techum* and the city—the entire city is like four *amos*, etc. However, regarding the beginning of the day, it is simple, by consensus, that it depends on sunset and sunrise; meaning that every **point** is absolutely independent.

It is mind-boggling to say and innovate that in the counting of **these** days, thousands of miles would be dragged after a single point.

***

Seemingly, the greatest difficulty with the opinion of the *Ra’ah* is this: since, according to him, the Date Line is between Jerusalem and the location of those dwelling at the edge of the East, and the expression of our Sages "for us and for them" (*Rosh Hashanah* 20b) refers to these two points—meaning that there was a settlement of *Bnei Yisrael* at the edge of the East at the time of our Sages—if so, how is it that not a single ruling is found in the *Shas* regarding the multitude of questions connected to the Date Line? One must conclude that even though he explains "for us"—[meaning] Bavel—nevertheless, there was not even **one** of *Bnei Yisrael* there.

Regarding what you wrote and copied from several books about the matter of the holiness of *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov* above, after below the places are divided—see also *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Orach Chayim* 61, section 7. And *Sefer Torah Or*, end of *Parshas Beshalach*, page 758 and onwards.

## 867

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 6th of Tishrei, in which you write regarding your situation in avodah and the struggle of "one nation shall be stronger than the other," which consequently leads to sadness, etc.

It is clear that thoughts and contemplation which lead to despair, laziness, and weakness in the avodah of Hashem have an impure source. They are among the stratagems of the *yetzer hara*, which disguises itself in the cloak of *yiras shamayim*. Consequently, one must fight against all of its machinations. This is especially true given that this matter has already been addressed in Tanya in several chapters, among them Chapter 27 and onwards. It is a pity to waste time on thoughts that are patently absurd, at a time when one could be utilizing it for the three pillars of Torah, avodah, and mitzvos. May Hashem grant you success to increase in diligence and persistence, and to serve Hashem with joy, in accordance with the instruction of our holy Nasi, may his merit protect us.

With blessings for success in all of the above and for a *gmar chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 868

B”H, 18 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished communal worker, engaged in communal affairs, R’ Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Elul and those preceding it: It is surprising that once again, reports have ceased regarding the progress of the matters you write about, particularly concerning the Reshet, the appointment of teachers, etc. And in the finest detail—for you mention the scheduling of the study days during the festival of Sukkos, yet we already saw last summer the results of a lack of proper preparation for the study days, and despite this, there is no progress or preparation for this.

Regarding what you wrote, that in one school it is necessary to add 17 hours at the expense of the Reshet—seemingly, it is not understood what makes this school different from the other schools, especially after the proposal that each of the teachers add teaching hours for the benefit of the Reshet. Nevertheless, if the situation is as you describe, they should do it—and may it be Hashem’s will that it be successful.

Regarding what you wrote, that the children who lived in Kfar Saba have moved to various places: I have already noted many times that it is **essential** to have a Chabad educational institution that will serve as a continuation for the students of the Reshet schools.

It is my hope that through a special collection of my own, a portion of the necessary budget for this will be provided. Certainly, there are many offices in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) that support such schools, and the matter depends only on the energy of the Reshet activists to bring the matter into reality, and the sooner, the better.

Regarding your question as to what I mean when I say that the Reshet institutions need to be expanded, and whether large sums of money should be invested in this: While in principle this is not ruled out, according to the current situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), it is not required at all. Consequently, the resources that can be raised should be used for improvements and the advancement of the Reshet. What I write—that this is not needed—is based on your own experience and what is known to all: that if registration had begun at the appropriate time and in the appropriate manner, and not in those places linked to politics, etc., you could have established many schools within the framework of the Reshet.

To my regret and sorrow, you began with a delay. As the saying goes, "a pot belonging to partners" [is neither hot nor cold]—the situation was such that people relied on others to fulfill their obligations for them. Consequently, the primary activity took place in those locations where there was local politics; they were pressured and their peace was disturbed. And as is the way of politics—which in the vast majority of cases is not pure—the opponents were immediately stirred up on the spot, and the results were what they were. In some places, the situation is still unclear because the local politicians are still running about, etc.

I do not know if "the lecture" is timely, as it seems there is no longer the possibility of establishing a new Reshet school in a new place. Perhaps this is still possible in the new settlements, provided that they choose the matter not because of political competition and not through outside pressure. Then it is possible that all aspects will fall into place—meaning that the necessary resources will come from the offices whose job it is, and your task will only be to organize the matters, or at most, to raise resources for improvements and completions. If you reflect on the history of the Reshet this summer and last summer, you will find sufficient proof for all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings and with the blessing of the festival.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed, and I sign on his behalf,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 873

B"H, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal affairs, R' Yitzchak, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

We acknowledge receipt of your letters from Rosh Chodesh, the 10th (22nd of Mar-Cheshvan), the 12th, and the 16th of Cheshvan, along with their enclosures. You will surely busy yourselves with the preparations for the Chanukah study days with the **greatest** vigor. Regarding your question as to who should handle this, it is imperative that you hold a general meeting and divide the responsibilities among yourselves, without deferring the discussion and negotiation of this to a second meeting, etc.

The forms that have been introduced in one of the Reshet schools should be discussed at a general meeting of the teaching staff. Following a discussion, a uniform format for these and similar forms should be adopted in all Reshet schools.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not understand what I wrote concerning increasing the number of Reshet schools and that they would not be forced to invest funds in this: I do not understand the practical difference at this moment, since the opening of new schools is certainly only possible in the middle of the coming summer, and by then, many conditions and circumstances will surely have changed. As for the past, aside from the fact that one does not cry over the past, in several places where they began to conduct registration—and there are many such places—if they had started in time, they would certainly have succeeded in establishing more schools, even in places in close proximity to Tel Aviv and Jerusalem, may they be rebuilt and established.

Regarding what you wrote about establishing an institution that will serve as a continuation for those graduating from the Reshet schools: the most viable path is to enter into discussions with those involved regarding the Kfar and the buildings that are becoming available, or the expansion of the framework of Beis Rivkah in the Kfar and the institutions for boys in the Kfar, in a manner that will allow them to also absorb these students. If you begin to contemplate and discuss this in good time, you will certainly be able to rectify the shortcomings that caused Reshet students not to be absorbed into the institutions in the Kfar and to scatter to various places.

Regarding the curriculum and the teaching of tailoring and the like for the boys, one should research such a program in the existing Charedi schools, which, with appropriate adjustments, can surely be arranged in a similar fashion in this institution as well.

I was pleased with what you wrote regarding the preparation of a program for 19 Kislev, and it would be best if it were uniform—as much as possible—in all Reshet schools.

The teachers for all the Reshet schools have surely been appointed by now, or at least the vast majority of them. Please be kind enough to send that list here. If there are some whose positions are not yet fixed, please note that on the sheet as well.

My hope is strong that regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter concerning the proposal of Rabbi Chanzin, may he live, regarding Kfar Saba, etc.—each one of them will do **everything** in his power, etc. Without a doubt, this is also for his own benefit, and to elaborate on such a simple matter is superfluous.

All of the above is written officially to you as the secretary of the Reshet, and you will surely propose all of the above at the meeting of the Reshet administration. Thank you.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Your letter of the 22nd of Mar-Cheshvan was received. If it is possible, it would be better if the study days for teachers lasted more than one day. Bringing students from the Kaplan neighborhood should only be done if you are **guaranteed** that this will not exacerbate relations with the municipality, the political parties, etc.

N.B. I was pleased with what you wrote, that your son Yosef Simcha, may he live, has begun attending Cheder. May it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife derive much nachas from all your children, may they live—an abundance of Chassidishe nachas—and may he grow to be a G-d-fearing Chassid and a scholar.

## 875

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Yoel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, I acknowledge the arranging of a Melaveh Malkah—the *Seudata d’David Malka Meshicha*—on the eve of the bright day, the 19th of Kislev. This is the day of the redemption of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya—the arbiter of the *nistar* (hidden) dimension of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the *nigleh* (revealed) dimension of Torah—who "redeemed his soul in peace, for there were many with him" (Tehillim 55:19), for he benefited the many (see Sefer Chassidim, siman 607, and the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes on Tehillim 55:19). This day marks the victory of the teachings, guidance, and customs of Chassidus, and the beginning of its widespread dissemination among the children of Israel.

Surely, the day itself causes this, that during the farbrengen that you, may you live, are arranging, words of Chassidus and inspiration will be heard regarding the "candle of mitzvah, the Torah of light, and the light of Torah"—which is the inner dimension of the Torah. May it be the will of Hashem that these words emerge from the heart and enter the hearts of the listeners, regarding their day-to-day lives.

With blessings for success.

## 878

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you write about your study schedule in both Nigleh and Chassidus. Surely you are fulfilling the ruling of our holy Torah that we must always ascend in matters of holiness, and when one exerts oneself and labors in this, the ruling is fulfilled: "You have labored and you have found."

And surely this point is engraved within you: that your presence in Montreal is intended to be a living testament to what a student of Tomchei Temimim must be. This testament must exist not only during the times of learning, davening, and strictly observing the yeshiva’s schedule, but also to serve as an example and a living testament to how one must conduct oneself during the times between learning and davening. As is explained in Chassidus, a servant serves his master even when that master is nothing more than flesh and blood—and how much more so, many times over, when the Master is the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. The servitude must be evident throughout the entire day, [even] in eating [and] in sleeping.

And regarding all of this, the Sages have stated the ruling: "You have labored and you have found," and "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

With blessings for success in Torah study, in yiras shamayim, in the performance of mitzvos with hiddur, and in the avodah of tefillah in particular.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

879

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who engages in communal needs, a man of fine character, etc.,
R' Avraham, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of 17 Kislev and those preceding it.

I am pleased that you have begun to be present at the meetings, and surely you will continue to do so in the future and write to me afterward in detail; the more detailed, the better.

Regarding what you write about the resignations—that this one is resigning and that one is resigning, etc.—you should have explained to those resigning that one does not play games with work for the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory. For, at the end of the day, one might actually accept the resignation, and then, Heaven forbid, one is left on the outside.

Furthermore, it should have been made clear once and for all that those who resign internally also resign externally, and they have no authority to speak in the name of the institutions and matters as if they were in their previous positions. And let there be an end to playing games and engaging in politics with the Rebbe’s affairs...

May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you the merit and success to say these things specifically with pleasant words, and may it be effective upon those who hear them...

And as we now approach the days of Chanukah, the law of which is to increase and continue [the light], and to illuminate even outside one's home, may the light and radiance of Chassidus increase and continue in all Chabad institutions—in every place... until we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "The night will shine like the day."

With blessings for success in all the above, and awaiting good news.

The dispatch was delayed, and therefore your letter of 25 Kislev was received. It is surprising that you are so brief regarding the farbrengens of Yud-Tes Kislev in the various locations. I wish that, at the very least, you would urge others to write about this with the necessary detail.

## 851

## 882

B"H, 7 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that you feel a decline in your spiritual state, etc.: naturally, for any such feeling, one must increase in persistence and diligence in the study of Torah. This is especially true regarding the study of the inner dimension of Torah—*pnimiyus haTorah*—which provides vitality and light to all of a person’s matters of *kedushah*. And even a little light dispels much darkness.

Furthermore, one must be careful not to exaggerate, *chas v'shalom*, the extent of the decline, as is also explained in the *maamar* "Mizmor Shir L'Yom HaShabbos" by the Mitteler Rebbe, which has just been published. Afterwards, you should study with the appropriate focus chapters 27–29 of the *Tanya Kadisha*.

It would be very good for you to make yourself known to the *mashpi'im* of *Chassidus* at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and discuss your concern with them. In this way, the teaching of our Sages regarding the verse, "If there is anxiety in a man's heart, let him speak of it," etc., will be fulfilled in you.

With blessings for Torah study with vitality, for increasing in *Chassidus* through guidance and customs, and for good tidings.

## 883

B"H, 7 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
Tel Aviv Branch,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters, dated the 2nd and 30th of Kislev, along with their enclosures. Thank you for the reports regarding the farbrengens of 19 Kislev. I am certain that more detailed reports—whether from you or from your shluchim—will arrive regarding the other locations as well, of which you only mentioned the main points. Thank you in advance.

It was a pleasure to see that you have finally been stirred to organize Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Kfar Chabad and [other locations], as this ensures greater permanence, in accordance with what is explained in Chassidus regarding the concept that "if a woman conceives first, she bears a male."

It is my strong hope that after initiating the organization, you will continue to stir them from time to time and strengthen them, in accordance with the experience you have already gained in your activities until now.

For the sake of order, I am enclosing a copy of my letter to Agudas Chabad, of which they are surely already aware.

I read that you provided tallis and tefillin through the G-d-fearing, etc., R' Dovid Hellman, may he live, to the one who requested them. Surely, in the future as well, you will fulfill R' Hellman’s requests in such matters completely. You may draw one hundred liras from the special collection for the Mitzvos Fund—that is, for tzitzis, tefillin, and mezuzos.

Regarding what you wrote about the youth group studying in Kiryat Shalom, it is surprising, since Rabbi [Name] wrote to me that he would involve himself in this and make efforts in this regard, etc. Therefore, it is incomprehensible that both the recruitment of the students and the expenses are entirely on your shoulders. It is worthwhile to speak with him and clarify the situation thoroughly, and to make a decision accordingly. For it is understood that Tzeirei Agudas Chabad does not have the capacity to spend one hundred liras a month on a group of ten children in a place where there are several rabbis, public activists, synagogues, and so on.

I am interested to know if you are in communication with the representatives of Moshav Chefetz Chaim, since some of the leaders there visited me some time ago, and we parted on friendly terms. Surely they still reside there now.

What comes to mind now are: Mr. Pepper, Mr. Kula, Mr. Gross, Mr. Greizman. As mentioned, it is possible that not all of them reside in Chefetz Chaim, but some surely do. It is understood that you have permission to say that you are conveying my regards and asking the aforementioned question.

For the expenses of the 19 Kislev farbrengen and the fifth night [of Chanukah], you will surely participate with three hundred liras from the special collection.

As I believe I have already stirred you many times, one must find ways and even strategies to utilize the meetings and the opportunity of having gathered together—even after 19 Kislev—for matters of strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit.

For this is the Rosh Hashanah of the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, its customs, and the ways of Chassidim. The concept of Rosh Hashanah is to draw [vitality] from the head to all the limbs—that is, to all the days of the year. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

With blessings for success, awaiting good news.

## 884

884

B”H, 13 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 5th of Chanukah, in which you write that I should explain to you concretely what *achdus* (unity) is.

In general, the *avodah* of our generation is that, notwithstanding the fact that one is required to study deep concepts of Torah in general and of *Chassidus* in particular, the primary work consists of dealing with oneself and influencing one’s surroundings in very simple matters and in daily life.

Regarding the *Anash*... in general, the intent of *achdus* is the opposite of *machlokes* (discord), and the effort to love the other person, even when it costs one something personally. And certainly, when it is a matter of not encroaching upon another’s domain—and as mentioned, I am referring here to simple matters as well, from which one must begin, and subsequently ascend higher and higher.

As someone who finds yourself in... you see the friction that occurs between one person and another, whether regarding... etc. I would like to elaborate on this in a heartfelt manner (and this expression is merely to convey the feelings regarding this).

It goes without saying—and no one would suspect me of this—that I wish to seek out faults in Jews in general, and in... in particular, and in *Anash* in the most specific sense.

However, when one reflects upon the situation of you all... and one sees the success that is granted from Above, that one receives help from those from whom one did not expect it at all, and such help that one did not anticipate, and yet, seeing what the situation is in practice, and wishing to conceal the cause of this—by doing so, one is not doing any good. On the contrary: when a patient wishes to be healed, the advice is not to deceive oneself and convince oneself otherwise—and certainly when the illness is obvious—by pretending not to see it. As the principle is known, that uncovering the condition is already a great part of the *refuah* (healing) for the patient.

I am writing all of this in general terms, without highlighting the details of the incidents, for it is not my way to write to one person about another regarding negative matters, where it is not absolutely necessary for their benefit. And in this case, it is certainly not necessary, for those who are on the scene all know exactly what the situation is where they are. Nothing is missing but the appropriate measure of will and energy to rectify this; at which point, in a very short time, the situation of... would change, and the people of... and the *mosdos* (institutions) that exist there would be for a name and for glory.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your husband, *shichyu*, with *parnassah* in abundance and with *harchavas hada’as* (peace of mind).

I hope that you, as well as the others to whom you will show this letter, will receive my letter not as rebuke or complaint, but as an effort—again and again—to convey to those who can rectify the situation... my perspective on the situation as it truly is.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in reporting good news regarding all that was mentioned above, and from the *peulos tovos* (good deeds) in daily life...

With blessings.

## 85

B"H, 17 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Yitzchak, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 7 Teves and those preceding it, I await further good news regarding how all matters have been arranged in the Reshet, particularly in Kfar Saba and Zarnuga. May it be the will of Hashem that you be privileged to share good news regarding all that was mentioned, as well as regarding your personal matters.

Regarding what you wrote about the results of the examinations: one should not be overly impressed by this, and surely the preparation on your part was merely *fun yotzei vegen* (done just to fulfill the obligation). Consequently, you will rectify this next time. In your current situation, this is like other matters of *reshus* (optional matters)—that is, *klipas nogah*—where, when the intent is to utilize them for *kedushah*—in your case, improving the situation in the Reshet—the preparation itself is elevated to *kedushah*. May Hashem grant you success.

Regarding the professional development of the teachers in the Reshet, one should ascertain when appropriate courses will be opened, whether by Agudas Yisrael or groups further to the right. It is worthwhile to urge the aforementioned regarding this, as such encouragement might lead them to expedite it as much as possible, especially if the Reshet participates symbolically in the expenses.

I was pleased with your response regarding the rejection of the proposal—suggested to you by someone—to accept the schools into the Reshet, especially since, based on the *shtimmung* (mood/atmosphere) here, I fear that this involves nothing more than politics and *siksukim* (incitement/strife), and not matters of *po'al u'ma'aseh* (actual practice). *V'da'il* (and to the wise, a hint is sufficient).

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned, in true health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 886

B”H, 27 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Teves, in which you write about your spiritual state—that it is not satisfactory—and you wish to rectify it and are requesting guidance in this matter.

The beginning and foundation of all avodah is the concept of kabbalas ol, prioritizing "we will do" (the fulfillment of instructions) over "we will hear" (intellectual understanding and comprehension). This depends entirely on you; once you resolve within yourself to act in this manner, you should turn to the senior rabbonim of anash in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established) and explain your situation to them, and then fulfill their instructions. The Ribono shel Olam will grant you success so that you may accomplish this in a way that is truly your own, and consequently, the statement of our Sages will be fulfilled in you: "You have labored and you have found."

I trust that you are keeping the three daily study portions that were established by the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, for every soul—the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and at the very least, you will keep them from this point forward.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 887

B"H, 28 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

You have surely already received my letter responding to your previous one. In response to your letter of 15 Teves:

It is surprising and puzzling that, apparently, there is not a single matter on which the opinion of all, or even the majority, is in agreement. Furthermore, they maintain a policy whereby every small or large matter must specifically be decided from "across the sea." It is impossible for this policy not to hinder the development of the institutions, especially since the question and answer process from there to here and from here to there takes about two weeks. One must find a way to rectify this, for after all, all the members of the Reshet are from Anash and Chassidim of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in whose name the Reshet institutions are called, and they must be conducted in accordance with his intent, etc. And this is understood.

I have also received your letter of 20 Teves, and thank you for the good news (following the order of your letter): that the prospects for organizing the Kinus for the day of the Hilula, 10 Shevat, have improved; that the relations regarding the school in Zarnuga have improved; and most importantly, that it seems you have abandoned melancholy and are viewing the development of this school with a more positive eye. As is known, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: when an army goes to war, it must march with joy and victory, and this in itself adds strength, fosters, and hastens the victory. The analogy is understood.

With blessings for good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and regarding all the matters about which you write, as well as your personal affairs,

**M. Schneerson**

Your urgent letter has been received (and see carefully above, the heading "It is surprising"). I have already written to R' Dovid Chanzin, may he live, that now is not the time to decrease the number of students in the schools; on the contrary, the opposite is true, even if the number of classes is not as significant.

- Regarding participation in "study days" (yemei iyun) — one should avoid this by all means if at all possible, but in a diplomatic manner, and not by "stretching the string" with sharp words, and also not by saying that this is a decree from "across the sea." It should be understood and simple that the outlook of Chabad teachers is not the same as the outlook of the Poalei Agudas Yisroel, or even the Mizrachi, who are the ones managing these "days." Furthermore, it is not their role to enter into arguments with them regarding this.

- Regarding participation in the expenses for erecting the barracks and the like — according to my knowledge of the Reshet's treasury status, this is possible only in a symbolic manner, but not in large sums. One must increase efforts in the appropriate offices, and it will be rectified, step by step, with the help of Hashem.

## 8,088

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 2 Shevat and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

This is especially true for one who possesses a correct understanding of the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, from which it is understood what the meaning of "expulsion," Heaven forbid, truly is—to be cut off from the inheritance of Hashem. To elaborate on such a simple matter is entirely superfluous. It is a pity to waste time on such back-and-forth regarding matters that are distressing and simple in their own right, at a time when that time could have been utilized for matters of an entirely different nature.

I trust that you have prepared the students, may they live, in a manner appropriate for the upcoming *yom hilula* of 10 Shevat, and all the more so on the day of the *hilula* itself. May it be the will of Hashem that the merit of the *baal hilula* protect each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, to guide us on the path that ascends to the House of G-d, and to assist us in walking upon it until the fulfillment of the prophecy, "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 890

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and refined individual, a man of character, etc., R' Elchanan, may he live, HaKohen.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah La'ilanot. It is well known what is brought in various sefarim of drush in connection with the spirit of awakening of this day, which is based on the expression in the pasuk, "For man is the tree of the field" (Devarim 20:19). When a person attains health in ruchniyus, health in gashmiyus follows as a matter of course. For since Yidden are "one nation on earth," in every place they carry out the concept of "one," which includes the general unification of gashmiyus with ruchniyus, the body and the neshamah.

This is also one of the explanations of the shitas of the Baal Shem Tov: to serve Hashem Yisbarach with simcha using the body, not by afflicting the body, but specifically through its—the body’s—assistance.

One can see this even with one’s own eyes: when the body is healthy—naturally, in a Yiddishe way, through kosher foods, etc.—it does not hinder one from learning Torah and fulfilling mitzvos, provided that one truly desires to do so.

And according to the well-known statement of our Sages, by making peace between the body and the neshamah, and within the neshamah itself between the nefesh ha'elokis and the nefesh habehamis, one also awakens and draws down peace in one’s immediate surroundings and in the further surroundings, and through this, peace in the world as well.

This is also a preparation for the ultimate peace, for the time of which the prophet Yeshayah said, "Nation shall not lift up sword against nation, neither shall they learn war anymore" (Yeshayah 2:4).

With blessing.

May it be Hashem’s will that all the above be with outstanding success.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to do everything in your power to increase and promote the work of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad... in the Tel Aviv branch, and also in the Jerusalem branch, may it be rebuilt and established.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings in all the above.

## 893

B"H, 26 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters from the 3rd, 11th, and 22nd of Adar. It is astonishing to see the gaps between one letter and the next, and even more so that all matters, without exception, are proceeding with **alarming** sluggishness, and without any sufficient reason for it (unless the reason is that the matter is of no concern to them. Yet, this "reason" is indefensible even to common human logic, and certainly to the logic that should be expected of Temimim, or even ordinary Chassidim, or even ordinary Anash, or even ordinary observant Jews).

What is even more alarming is that I know—and they certainly know—**many** of Anash who have acted and achieved results in communal matters in various places in Eretz Yisrael—but not in the vineyard of Chabad.

And when they gather together, they vent their frustrations to one another, and then they disperse until the next meeting. I have already grown weary of writing about this, and even weary of writing that I am weary of writing.

Surely you are familiar with the story from the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "Rabota nye vidna" (the work is not visible)—that they speak, and write, and stir things up, yet the matters do not budge from their place...

When you receive this letter, meet with one or two of Anash, and when there is news, write to me. I will wait another week and another, and I will stir things up again, and again I will receive a response along these same lines.

It should have been explained to all the "activists" that this is not my private business... And if they would reflect even slightly, without personal bias, perhaps they would reach the conclusion that it is not my role to preach morality, nor even to stir things up, but rather—to assist...

## 896

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Iyar, the birthday of the Rebbe Maharash, in which you write:

1) That by your nature, when money comes into your hands, various expenses arise, and you spend your money until, because of this, you are forced to borrow.

It is already well known that conduct according to nature is the conduct of natural beings who do not possess a *nefesh elokis* that transcends nature. This is not the case for every Jew, who are called children of Hashem; for in the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, the *nefesh elokis*—which is the second soul in a Jew—is literally a part of Hashem from above. The *avodah* of man, which is the purpose of his soul’s descent below, is to change nature, or at the very least, to rule and have mastery over nature, as is explained at length in *Tanya*, Chapter 15 and onwards. This applies even to a nature that does not cause much harm; how much more so when the nature leads to the squandering of money as mentioned, with the result that one becomes a borrower—and as the verse states, "the borrower is a slave to the lender." Certainly, one has been given the strength to overcome this aforementioned nature, and this matter depends solely on one's own will.

2) Regarding what you write that you do not have success in your affairs—you should arrange from now on that every weekday morning, before *davening*, you set aside a franc or two for *tzedakah*. And after *davening* each day (weekdays, *Shabbos*, and *Yom Tov*), you should recite the *shiur* of *Tehillim*—according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month. Through this, success in your affairs will increase.

3) Regarding what you write about your health... The illness you mention in your letter now has several remedies. When they are taken at the times prescribed by a specialist doctor, one does not suffer from this illness, and over time, one is healed. It is surprising that you are not aware of this; perhaps you have not yet found the specialist doctors in the field who surely can be found in a large city...

The *pidyon nefesh* enclosed in your letter will be read at the holy resting place of the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*. You must have your *tefillin* and those of your brothers checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home. May Hashem grant you success to report good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 897

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5716

...Regarding what you ask about the *hidurim* (extra stringencies) you have been accustomed to for many years, which your husband does not currently practice: I am confident that if you explain to him the *hidur* involved in the matter, not only will he not hinder you from your practice, but on the contrary, he will also conduct himself in this manner. For this is a clear instruction from Above that this *hidur* is relevant to him. As is known from the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that everything a Jewish person sees or hears contains an instruction for him regarding his *avodah* to his Creator. And since, in one way or another, this *hidur* has entered his *daled amos*, it is certainly within his capacity to practice it, and it is relevant to him.

It is understood that this, too, is subject to what is said regarding our Torah as a whole, that "its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace." When you explain all of the above without agitation, and in ways of pleasantness and peace, peace will surely increase in your home, and through this, the blessing of Hashem as well—for peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the *Ribono shel Olam*, as our Mishnah rules.

## 809

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and upright man, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of 12 and 14 Sivan.

It was a pleasure for me to read that you are making preparations for the upcoming celebration of 12 Tammuz.

This is certainly the case in all the schools of the Reshet, and it is most appropriate that they all cooperate together. May it be the will of Hashem that this also influence the drawing together of hearts among the staff of teachers—both men and women—of the Reshet, as well as the administrators and members of the board, drawing all their hearts together as one to do His will with a complete heart.

Regarding what you wrote about the manner of the performance: this question has surely already been addressed in the various circles of those who are G-d-fearing in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) in recent months. Consequently, it is known how they conducted themselves and how the public reacted to it, and the decision should be made accordingly. However, it is understood that this must be discussed and decided upon in a meeting of the Reshet administration, since this is a general matter that concerns not just one school in its own location, but all of them.

Regarding what you wrote—that I did not specifically demand of you involvement in the Reshet and in Chabad in general, so that you could become established in your work as a director and focus on your professional development—while I did not "specifically demand," as you put it, I also did not exempt you from doing as all the other directors and activists of the Reshet do. This is especially true regarding the matter of the summer camp, which is a time-sensitive issue. Experience from the past has shown what a good thing this is and how much great benefit is hidden within it, especially if it is planned as thoroughly as necessary. Conversely, it has also been observed what damage is caused by the lack of an organized plan and the lack of cooperation, and a word to the wise is sufficient. May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, everything mentioned will now be arranged...

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***809***

From a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Yitzchak, may he live:** Ginzburg. Additional letters to him—above 842, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 8101

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write once again regarding the matter mentioned in your previous letter, and in connection with the response you received from me, you ask for my opinion once more on this very same question.

The matter has already been addressed at the beginning of the second chapter of Berachos, where the discussion concerns the reading of the Shema, in which we are commanded **every** day, and at the beginning of the day, that we must accept the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven and the **yoke** of the mitzvos. See also Tanya, Chapter 41. If you will listen to my opinion, present your matters once again before your Rosh Yeshiva and your Mashpia, and fulfill their instructions—both for your own sake and for the sake of the truth—with an attitude of *kabbalas ol*. Then, all the illusory *he'lem* and *hester* (concealments) will be nullified; they have no reality other than in the absence of the will for *kabbalas ol*.

Regarding your notification of your upcoming birthday—may you be blessed to be a G-d-fearing Jew and a Chossid—the choice is given to everyone, as are the strengths to walk in the good and straight path, as it is written, "And you shall choose life." However, it is required of you to use your power of choice not to fulfill your own will, but to fulfill the will of the Ribono shel Olam, which is revealed in our Torah—the Torah of life—and for which one receives guidance from those who are greater than oneself in Torah and *yiras shamayim*. A yeshiva student receives these instructions from his Mashpia. May it be His will that this be a year of success for you in the study of our holy Torah and in the performance of its mitzvos with *hiddur*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

#### 8101

From the Secretariat copy.

## 8102

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Sivan, in which you write about where you are learning for the new zman, and primarily that until now you have not shown a suitable desire to learn and are requesting a blessing:

It is self-evident that one does not fulfill one's obligation merely by asking for a blessing. Rather, one must exert oneself to learn as one ought, and not only on the day one receives this letter or the day after, but for a much longer time. Once one does this for a certain period, one will no longer need to force oneself, and one will acquire an ever-increasing desire to learn.

You should have consulted with Rabbi [Name] regarding this and your other problems, and told him everything you wrote to me. Since he sees you constantly, he will likely be able to help you in these matters. May Hashem grant you success.

I hope that you are keeping up with the daily Tehillim, as Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month, and that you will continue to do so.

With blessings.

## 8103

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’... may he live,

Peace and blessing!

Following the longest of interruptions, your letter of 22 Sivan was received. Regarding what you wrote concerning my remarks about the explanation of "I will be sanctified by those who are near to Me" (*b'krovai ekadesh*), I stated clearly even then that I do not understand at all the justification provided by that explanation. For "justification" implies that this is an explanation according to the intellect. Yet the entire matter of *b'krovai ekadesh* is a subject of great wonder—how can it be explained according to the intellect even in the context of the verse itself, and certainly in our current situation?

And as for why I said the aforementioned in public, specifically at a *farbrengen*—this is for an understandable reason. For if more of an explanation were to be publicized regarding this, there is a concern that the *Sefardim*, and even others, might say "neither them nor their reward," and a word to the wise is sufficient.

- Thus regarding what you wrote in your letter; from here on, concerning what is missing in your letter:

My hope is that you are also aware that the older *bochurim* of Tomchei Temimim in... are despondent, even though they cite various reasons (one says he lacks a *chavrusa*, another says he is not succeeding in his studies, etc., etc.). This is at a time when I receive reports and even letters from students of other *yeshivos*, where the very fact of writing to me from another *yeshiva* indicates that the student is not entirely satisfied with the place where he is located, yet nevertheless, one senses a vitality and a *farkackeit* (fervor) in the study of the *nigleh* or in *mussar* and the like—which is not the case with the aforementioned.

And in all the *pidyonos* and letters that are received, I do not find even a single word discussing this. This indicates one of two things: either they know and are not discussing it, or they are unaware of the matter. Both possibilities are alarming, and it is difficult to elaborate on such a distressing subject.

May it be the will of Hashem that finally, even though as you write in your letter, "in all generations it was not accomplished," at the very least they will do what is possible.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 804

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter in the month of Adar, in which you write about your efforts to influence your friends—may they live—and those you encounter, to inform them about our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos, and to explain to them that it is for **their own** greatest good to walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos. Fortunate is your portion that Divine Providence has provided you with such opportunities. The Creator of the world is faithful to reward you with what you need, both materially and spiritually.

It is my firm hope that you will continue to act in these matters in the future, and even increase your courage and efforts in this regard, as the needs of the hour demand in general, and in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—in particular. Certainly, the members of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad will continue to assist you and help you to the best of their ability.

I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding all of the above, and with the necessary details. I also hope you will share the good news that the health of your father—may he live—has improved.

With blessings for progress and increase in all the above, and for success in the avodah of Hashem, and may you be elevated in accordance with your standing, your situation, and your environment.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8106

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Your letters of the 17th and 21st of Menachem Av, the newspaper clipping, and the book *Bechirah B'Eretz HaBechirah* have been received.

It is surprising to receive complaints here that the publicity regarding my visits and the activities of the shluchim, may they live and be well, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, is not sufficient at all. The wonder is directed at the entire administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad—how they are not taking advantage of this opportunity, which is not something that occurs at every moment, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is understood that the intention here is not for cheap publicity, but rather publicity that will bring benefit to the dissemination of the wellsprings in particular, and to matters of Yiddishkeit in general.

Regarding what you wrote, that Mr. A.S., may he live, wishes to add a section, etc., and that you gave him unedited transcripts—certainly, first and foremost, you should provide him with the edited transcripts, and only as an addition, the aforementioned transcripts. After all, the edited materials are also numerous in proportion, such as those printed in the *Kovtzei Lubavitch* journals, the booklets that appeared 13-14 years ago, the general letters and the letters regarding specific details, what has been printed in the bulletin, the introductions to the *kuntreisim* of the years 5710-5711, the indices to the *Sefer HaSichos*, and much, much more.

We await good news regarding this as well.

You should certainly confirm receipt of this letter immediately upon receiving it.

## 8107

B"H, 29 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 2nd of Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av and the 12th of Menachem Av, as well as the note from the 17th of Menachem Av, all of which were enclosed in one envelope.

Regarding what you wrote about two students who should travel here because "they are not listening," etc.—proposals such as these are made from time to time by members of the administration of Tomchei Temimim in Lod. It is understood and simple that this is not the way to educate students: that because there are difficulties in their education, one should send them to another place (and to a place far removed from their families, who can also influence them for the good, at least to some extent). Surely they, too, are aware that even in the United States there are challenges, etc. I have already written many times that among the *avreichim* who came here from Eretz Yisrael—even though they had a virtue, as they did not travel here for the aforementioned reason, and on the contrary, they were the elite—to my great regret, I did not see them make progress. It must be explained to all members of the administration of Tomchei Temimim in Lod that the issue is not to find another place to send students who are not the elite, but rather that contemplation is needed on how to educate them on the spot. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

I received a letter from the *avreich*... may he live, who writes that he transferred from Tomchei Temimim in Lod to Toras Emes. Please be kind enough to inform me of the details of this matter, and whether this was done with the full consent of the administration of Tomchei Temimim in Lod.

In general, regarding the transfer of students from Toras Emes to Lod and vice versa, do they consult with each other in advance and cooperate?

Thank you for your letter regarding the visit of the *shluchim*, may they live and be well. Surely you will continue in this vein, and the more one details, the more praiseworthy it is.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote about a *mashgiach*, etc.—one must find this specifically from the students of our *yeshivos* in Eretz Yisrael (or, at most, from France), for several reasons.

Regarding what you wrote about small expenses for the students—I will consider this in the coming days.

Regarding what you wrote about traveling here—it is highly questionable whether it is worthwhile, given the expenses (in money, effort, etc.) involved, and most importantly, the disruption of the order during the time until he returns. Experience has already shown that the damage caused by this requires a long time and great effort to repair, and one is not always successful.

***

## 8108

B"H, 6 Elul, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal affairs, R' Yaakov, shlita.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the end of the month of Menachem Av, in which you write about the visit of the shluchim, the avreichim and rabbanim, shlita, to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and the content of the discussions and the impressions made. May it be the will of Hashem that all the words of hisorerus that were spoken and heard be drawn down into actual practice and daily life, for this is the whole purpose of man. I have already written at length to Aguch in Eretz Yisrael that the visit and the hisorerus during the days of the visit are [like] plowing and sowing, and it is incumbent upon anash on the spot to bring all these matters into actual practice in the days that follow, until they reach a successful conclusion in reality. It is understood that this also includes the central point of "spreading the wellsprings outward." Since only the beginnings are difficult, the avodah will now be easy if they approach it with the necessary vigor, and the sooner, the better, while the impressions of the visit are still fresh. And this is clear.

Enclosed is what has been published recently, and surely you will merit to benefit the many through its content, and the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 811

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to the letter containing a *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at the auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your question: concerning the removal of the cataract, since a specialist doctor has stated that there is still some vision remaining in the eye and that there is no need to rush into surgery, the principle of "sit and do nothing" is preferable. However, from time to time, it is appropriate to visit him or ask him in advance when to return, so that he may monitor the situation. May the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, guide you in the best possible way, in a manner that is good in both the revealed and manifest sense.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding the contents of the *pidyon nefesh*, especially since we are now in the month of Kislev—the month of miracles, redemption, and the victory of the matters of Chabad, of which all *anash*, the Chassidim and the *temimim* *sheyichyu*, are integral and essential parts.

With respect and blessings.
