## 813

B"H, 2 Teves, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter informing me of your excellent decision—and there is no "good" other than the perfect Torah—to increase your fixed times for Torah study, to strengthen your avodah of tefillah, and to add to your study of Chassidus.

May it be the will of the Giver of the Torah, the living G-d, to strengthen your minds and hearts so that you may ascend in holiness from level to level and from strength to strength, in accordance with the instruction of the Torah. This is also the lesson of the days of Chanukah, from which we learn to be "adding and increasing" from day to day—to increase the light that shines after the sun has set and illuminates the entrance of one’s home from the outside, which applies also to "external" matters, meaning in one’s conduct throughout the entire day.

There is nothing that can stand before the will, for regarding this, too, it is said: "You have labored and you have found."

May it be His will that you bring good tidings in all of the above, and may your parents and teachers, may they live, derive from you much true nachas—that is, traditional, Chassidic, Jewish nachas.

## 8114

B"H, 24 Adar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Schneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter containing a *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the content of which mentions that you received a letter from our former country requesting medicinal remedies. After inquiry and investigation here, it has become known that since these remedies are potent, they cannot be administered without seeing the patient.

There have already been several such cases, and the standard practice in such matters is that along with the remedies, one also sends the pamphlet that explains the methods of using these remedies and the cases for which they are most suitable. Such a pamphlet can be obtained by a doctor who is an acquaintance or friend of theirs from the factory that manufactures these remedies, or through the journals of medical associations and the like. Surely they know several doctors in their camp now, and through them they will be able to obtain all of the above and send it along with the remedies.

Furthermore, it should be noted that several of these journals are also received in our former country. If, along with the medicinal remedies being sent, they write which pamphlet discusses these remedies, there is room to say that the doctor there will be able to obtain the pamphlet. However, it is understood that it is better to send the pamphlet from here as well. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8116

B"H, 22 Adar Sheni, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, R' Yitzchak, may he live:

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from Shushan Purim, in which you write regarding the Purim celebrations.

May it be Hashem’s will that you hear good news in both personal and general matters. The merit of the many will surely assist them. However—after asking their forgiveness for the expression that follows—they themselves provoke the Yetzer Hara, as per the interpretation of the phrase in the *Al Chet* prayer, "for the sin we have sinned before You with the Yetzer Hara." This means that there are matters that even the Yetzer Hara would not dare to use to incite a person, were it not for the fact that they provoke him themselves, etc.

With blessings for good news,

**M. Schneerson**

Since you have known him for some time, you will surely eventually find the appropriate way. In any case, setting a fixed time for the study of Chassidus—and in particular, speaking about the "environment of Chassidus"—is one of the primary paths in this regard.

*[8 Nissan 5717]*

## 818

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Menachem Ben Zion, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters from 20 Nissan and those preceding it, in which you write the main points of the farbrengens and activities during the days of the festival of Pesach—I am certain that you will continue with such things in the future, and in greater detail, and thank you.

Regarding what you wrote about the avreich Y.K., may he live, who wanted to prevent him from meeting with his friend in the past, and in the end, it did not work out, etc.—surely from this, too, he will learn the truth of the teaching of the Mishnah, that "a mitzvah leads to another mitzvah," and the opposite. For the fact that he did not want to participate in the Melach [Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch] gathering in Kfar Chabad—even though he surely knew that the purpose of the gathering was to discuss the dissemination of the wellsprings outward and matters of tzedakah—this led to another matter of this type. For had he traveled, not only would the aforementioned individual not have come under an undesirable influence—even if only a passing influence—but he would have performed a second mitzvah, as it would have been in his power to influence the friend of the aforementioned individual as well.

It is understood that the intention is not to preach morality, but rather to awaken him regarding the future concerning the statement of our Sages: "Do not sit and weigh the mitzvos of the Torah, saying, 'This mitzvah is light,' and there is no need to campaign for it, and the effort of the journey is not worthwhile," etc.

Regarding what you wrote, that you do not always see complete success in your learning, and it seems to you that you do not remember what you learn:

I believe I have already written to you that all of the above is from the enticements of the Yetzer Hara. It is a pity to waste your time arguing with him and entering into a back-and-forth debate as to whether this is the truth—at a time when you could be learning in practice. As I have written to you before, especially when one learns in a group of friends, for then one succeeds more, as the Mishnah states.

And regarding what you wrote, that the reason for the lack of complete success is because you lack the power of hiskashrus, etc., etc.—since the halacha is decided that every Jew is sworn and stands from Har Sinai to fulfill everything that was said at Har Sinai, this gives additional strength to fulfill the mitzvah. Especially according to what is explained in Chassidus regarding the statement of our Sages, "They adjure him" (*mashbi'in oto*), which is from the language of *shevuah* (oath) and also from the language of *sova* (satiety/fullness), that the *sova* comes through the *shevuah* (see the glosses of the Tzemach Tzedek to Tanya—printed in the book *Kitzur V'He'aros L'Tanya*). And if you only desire it, Hashem will help you to learn and succeed in learning, observing, doing, and fulfilling.

## 819

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5717
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your telegram.

It is surprising that there has been a cessation in your letters and news, both from you and from your family and household. I only learned from an outside source that the matter regarding the city... has not yet been concluded, though I am unaware of the details.

Although it is certainly unnecessary to prompt you regarding your assistance to Anash in their private matters—and all the more so in general matters—nevertheless, since it appears that Anash in Melbourne are struggling regarding the Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch and Bais Rivkah institutions, I am writing these lines based on the dictum of our Sages that one only prompts those who are already diligent. This is intended only as an encouragement to do everything in your power, and even more than that. As is well known from the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, when a person below resolves to give to tzedakah, even if the decision is beyond his current means, at the moment of that decision, additional channels are opened from above so that he may fulfill his good resolution completely. It is understood that all these things apply to spiritual tzedakah as well.

My intention in this is not only regarding your own assistance, but also regarding help through influencing those who listen to you, so that they too will assist the aforementioned institutions and their related needs as much as possible. Our Sages have already stated that words that come from the heart enter the heart.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and with the blessing in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8120

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5717

In general, as I once heard a good word from a merchant: a business where luck plays a role is not worth chasing after. This is true in general regarding matters connected to the stock exchange, and especially in our time, which is not always built upon true calculations and solid accounting.

Regarding the question about a *gemilas chasadim*—unfortunately, the merchants here are so preoccupied that they do not consider a *gemach* or support in another country.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that you should report good tidings regarding all of the above, in good health for yourself and all your household members, may they live.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8122

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished *avreich*, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Yisroel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification regarding your engagement with your bride, may she live, in a good and auspicious hour:

May it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and that you build an everlasting edifice upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is Chassidus.

With blessings of Mazal Tov.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the concept that "everything that is lower has a higher root above":

The explanation in the teachings of Chassidus is not regarding the things themselves, but rather regarding the *nitzotz Eloki* (Divine spark) that is found within them. The distinction here is understood and fundamental, especially through the contemplation that the *nitzotz Eloki* can be in a state of *shevi* (shattering) and *galus* (exile). Furthermore, it can even be in a state regarding which it is said, "The lamp of the wicked shall be extinguished"—meaning, it is extinguished entirely.

Based on the above, it is also understood that there is no contradiction in saying that a certain thing is more spiritual and holy in comparison to another, yet the second thing has a higher root. This is because the intention is toward the *nitzotz Eloki* within it, for in many matters, the thing that gives it life conceals that vitality, opposes it, and even battles against it.

See regarding this also *Torah Or*, *Bereishis* 4a; *Likutei Torah*, *Re'eh* 21b; the *maamar* beginning "Acharei," and its explanation at the end of *Derech Mitzvosecha* by the Tzemach Tzedek, and elsewhere.

The conclusion of the above is that in its most supernal root, Yaakov—the firstborn—the *nefesh Elokis* and the *yetzer tov* precede the *nefesh habehamis* and the *yetzer hara*, etc., as is explained in many places. Among those in print, see *Sefer Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*, page 48 and onward. And as it is written, "Is not Esav a brother to Yaakov... yet I have loved Yaakov."

## 8124

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I am writing today regarding two points:

a) It is reported that many are traveling from our country to Poland, and they say that there are several possibilities to ease their status and situation there, and also to facilitate their relocation from there to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and the like, if some of the activists were to visit there. It appears that among those traveling are several of Anash.

b) The director of the Yiddish Institute there, Prof. Berel Mark (as well as the Rabbi there), mentioned during their visit to Eretz Yisrael that in the library of this institution there are more than one hundred Chassidus volumes. According to what was said, these include manuscripts in the holy handwriting of the Rebbes, but I doubt whether they understand or know how to distinguish the manuscripts.

According to the director of the aforementioned institution, it is not far-fetched that they would give over the volumes if there were a request from someone who would have the sense to be given the volumes. It is possible that in such a case, even monetary compensation for those mediating to obtain the necessary permit for this could be effective.

Perhaps it would be worthwhile for you to take a few days to visit there regarding the two aforementioned points. If that is not possible, perhaps there is someone else in your circle who has at least some knowledge of Chassidus volumes and also some understanding of public affairs, who could visit there.

There was a rumor that the aforementioned professor, who is the director of the institution, is scheduled to participate in some conference in Eretz Yisrael, and it is possible that he will also pass through France on his way there or on his return. Naturally, the trip to Poland must be at a time when he is there, so that they can meet with him. Surely the Federation or the editorial office of the Yiddish newspaper in Paris knows about the timing of his travel.

From the Joint, a check and a third were received without instructions as to which matter they belong. And another 4,540 B.A.

Your letter of the 16th of 20 Tammuz was received, and your requests were fulfilled.

With blessings for good tidings and for success in your holy work.

## 8126

B"H, 1 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, engaged in communal needs, R' Pinchas, may he live:

May it be the will of Hashem that your mind be set at ease, just as you have set my mind at ease with this joyous news. It is possible there is room to interest B.M. in such a way that he derives some benefit from this, perhaps even a simple benefit—that is, monetary payment. As is tangibly evident, when the *nefesh habehamis* also derives pleasure from a matter, in addition to the pleasure of the *nefesh ha'elokis*, the matter is brought to fruition sooner and more completely.

Since in two weeks the esteemed R' Y. Weinberg, may he live, will be visiting Eretz Yisrael, and he is flying from Eretz Yisrael to here—and he is a citizen of the United States—it would be appropriate for him to deliver the aforementioned items. Surely he will also have with him the *bichlech* from the estate of Rabbi Slonim, of blessed memory, regarding which you wrote some time ago and have already brought a portion of them. For several reasons, it is better that the *bichlech* be brought here not by one person all at once, but rather divided among several people. I believe I wrote similarly regarding the *bichl* of Chassidus that is with Mr. Shmerling, may he live. Many thanks in advance for all of the above.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all that was mentioned, as well as in your personal affairs, and in this, of course, first and foremost, with improved health.

## 8127

B"H, 5 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn.

Mr. Nassan Nuta, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha,

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the *hishtadlus* for the strengthening of the holy Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lod, and for the strengthening of Kfar Chabad.

May Hashem help that this *hishtadlus* should be met with great success. This is the greatest pleasure for the one making the effort—to see good fruits from his exertion. This will add to the blessings of Hashem that one is in need of, and included in this is that you should be able to act in the aforementioned matters with longevity of days and good years, and in an ever-greater measure, in accordance with the directive of our holy Torah: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

It is self-understood that it is a proper thing to provide updates regarding the aforementioned, for when one provides pleasure to a fellow Jew—even one who is located on the other side of the sea—this is the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of "Love your fellow as yourself." Especially since one sees tangibly that the very fact that one knows they will be writing to someone about these *peulos tovos* (good deeds) strengthens those activities, and one adds to them, as is evident tangibly.

Surely you are aware of the *takanah* to recite the monthly *shiur* of Tehillim, where the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month, each day after morning *davening*. In any case, you should do so from now on and moving forward.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*,

## 8128

B"H, 10 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the Vaad of Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom and Blessing,

I have received alarming news, namely:

That another incident has occurred of raising a hand against a fellow, and apparently it even reached the point of action, G-d forbid. Furthermore, this took place in public, without any protest from those present.

It is possible that what I wrote regarding a similar incident that occurred some years ago has already been forgotten, or perhaps the people of the village have a copy of my letters. And if my words are not sufficient, then surely the words of our holy Torah regarding the gravity of this matter will suffice. And the wise will understand.

I have come to emphasize further that this is not merely a private matter between the one who raised his hand, etc., and the other party; rather, it is a matter that concerns the entire collective living there, and in this specific case—all the residents of Kfar Chabad.

In the case of Kfar Chabad, the matter is even more alarming (and consequently, the gravity of the matter is greater) because it is in absolute contradiction to one of the foundations of Chassidus in general, and the Chabad school of Chassidus in particular, which was emphasized by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the arbiter of the hidden dimensions of Torah and the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the revealed dimensions of Torah—that "Love your fellow as yourself" is one with "Love Hashem your G-d." This love is the root of all 248 positive mitzvos, and from it they are drawn, etc. Included in the positive mitzvos is also the mitzvah of the fear of Hashem, which is the root of the 365 negative mitzvos, for one fears to rebel against the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. Thus, in general, love is the root of all 613 mitzvos, the "body of the King." And from the positive you can infer the negative, etc.

I do not wish to dwell at length on such alarming matters. I will await a **detailed** letter from you regarding the particulars of the incident, and also whether you have taken any measures as a protest against the matter. Please inform me by telegram immediately upon receipt of this letter of the name (and mother's name) of the man who raised his hand, so that we may arouse Heavenly mercy, etc., for him and his family, may they live. The sooner this is done, the better.

May it be the will of Hashem that, finally, a period of providing Chassidic nachas from Kfar Chabad and its affairs will begin.

With the blessing of Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8129

B"H, 13 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and learned R' Yisroel Menachem, Shochet and Bodek,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, which you began writing on the 15th of Av—a Yom Tov, as our Sages of blessed memory tell us—and completed about two weeks later, which has just now been received.

It gave me pleasure to read that you have established a shiur in the study of Chabad Chassidus. Certainly, for one such as yourself, it is unnecessary to awaken or remind you of the statement of our Sages regarding our Torah in general, and it is self-evident regarding the teachings of Chassidus [Chabad]—that "great is study, for it leads to action." This means that the study of Torah is not the primary goal; rather, the action is the primary goal: to walk in its guidance and its conduct. This applies to all matters of Torah and mitzvos, since the inner dimension of the Torah is called in the Zohar "the soul of the Torah," and an increase in vitality within the soul affects all the limbs of the body, and this is a kal v’chomer.

There are several of the elders of Anash in your vicinity, and you can speak with them about this—in accordance with the saying of the Mitteler Rebbe, that when two Jews speak together about matters of Torah and mitzvos, it creates two G-dly souls against one natural soul.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

You are surely aware of the three daily study portions established for every person by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and in any event, you should maintain them from here on.

As we approach the new year, may it come for us and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your entire household: a blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

## 8131

24 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, a man of energy and many accomplishments, R' Tzvi, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is somewhat surprising that since you departed from here, we have not heard from you, even though it is known that when two of the Bnei Yisrael meet, it certainly brings about a change and an increase [in holiness], and not only regarding themselves, but also regarding their surroundings—especially when speaking of those who have been gifted with the power to influence others and are engaged in this work. I am certain you will make up for this at the next opportunity.

Recently, I received a letter from my friend in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, which writes as follows: "There is a breach in the religious youth organization, and in several settlements that do not have a permanent shul, to daven in a mixed setting, Heaven forbid, without a proper mechitzah according to the law, and at times this is done based on an ideology. Please turn to Rabbi Neriah, as he has the ability to influence [the situation] there to rectify it."

End quote.

And if our Sages said regarding undesirable matters that "a person is not considered [a sinner] unless he has [the capacity for it]," how much more so is this true regarding a good quality, which is [always] greater. And even if you were to say that for the time being you do not feel that you have the power to influence such matters—even though you surely recall that in our conversation we touched upon this point as well—since everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, and they write from there to here, and through this from here to there, surely your honor, in the language of Chassidus, will **clothe yourself** in this matter:

1. To rectify it as much as possible, and my hope is strong that you will be able to rectify the aforementioned. And surely you will not withhold the good of informing me of your success in this.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings in the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 611

B”H, 27 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Koren

Following the longest of intervals, I received your letter of 19 Elul, in which you write that you are in contact with the representatives of Kfar Chabad regarding the stabilization and development of the agricultural situation there. Surely the benefit will be greater if there is a joint effort involving all the various groups within Kfar Chabad, as this will certainly preserve and enhance its character, allowing it to fulfill its role in the best possible manner.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send you my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing.

## 8132

B"H, 27 Elul, 5717
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Chaim Zusia, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 16th, 19th, and 22nd of Elul, along with their enclosures. I have enclosed my response to your sister-in-law, may she live. It is surprising that you are so brief regarding the recent gatherings.

Regarding what you wrote about merging the tracts of land with the new village, you did not clarify your intent in your letter. You wrote that if they speak only about the abandoned old village, it will undermine the entire position; this is not understood, and you will surely explain this further in your next letter.

In general, one can surmise that since partisan politics dominate in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and the power of the parties is also measured according to the settlement points of each one, it is difficult to say that a party will relinquish one of its settlement points to join another moshav. This is different when the matter concerns only a specific tract of land, which does not reduce the number of settlements of that party, where it is possible to accomplish the matter without entering into contentions, etc. It is understood that all of this is written only as a conjecture, since the details are not known here. And as I have already written, everyone must consult together, rather than each one pulling in a different direction.

I have already written to several of anash regarding the necessity to prepare, well in advance, a detailed plan to utilize the days of desire and joy of the upcoming month of Tishrei. May it be His will that, at the very least, promptness in this will be effective now.

Approaching the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours, with the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, materially and spiritually.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8133

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5718

...Regarding your question on behalf of many as to whether the Keren Hashana is the same as Kupas Rabbeinu: this is not the case. Kupas Rabbeinu was established many years ago, even during the time of my grandfather, the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe; this is not the case with Keren Hashana.

Regarding your second question—whether one who contributes maaser to tzedakah is required to also donate to Keren Hashana—your question is difficult to understand. It is obvious that Keren Hashana is also a tzedakah fund, and consequently, one may take from maaser kesafim for it. On the other hand, for one who gives tzedakah to other tzedakah causes, Keren Hashana is a distinct matter, as explained in the sicha at the time this initiative was publicized.

#### ***8133***

Published in the journal *Yagdil Torah* (Jerusalem), issue 27, p. 8.

**Kupas Rabbeinu was established:** See *Sifriyas Lubavitch*, p. 128, and the sources cited there.

**In the sicha:** Of Shabbos Bereishis 5714, published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 652. See also letter 7959 above.

## 8334

B"H, 5th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Chaim Zusia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following the longest of interruptions, your two letters were received together (the first begun on 11 Tishrei and finished on the 27th, and the second from 28 Tishrei), along with the previous one. We await further good news regarding all the matters you write about.

Regarding your question about the interpretation of merging the areas: it is difficult to instruct from here which block to merge and which not to, as this requires seeing the situation and deciding on the spot. The general point regarding this has already been written: in order to prevent the trait of contentiousness, one must strive for the merger in a manner that also leaves some areas unmerged, so that it cannot be argued that it is impossible to concede on points of settlement, etc.

It seems there was a bit more order in the activities of the month of Tishrei due to the fact that you consulted beforehand, and apparently prepared some sort of plan, even though it seems that it, too, was not as detailed as necessary. Consequently, some details remained like "a pot belonging to partners" [i.e., neglected]. Surely, based on this, you will plan a detailed program for the upcoming month of Kislev, and primarily for the celebration of 19 Kislev.

It is my hope that by the time you receive my letter, the health of your family, may they live, has already improved, as well as that of the other residents of Kfar Chabad, among all of Klal Yisrael. May it be His will that you only bring good tidings for the community at large and for each individual.

With blessing and regards,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8145

B"H, 10th of Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the venerable Torah scholar, the G-d-fearing Chassid, distinguished and renowned, R' Shaul Yissachar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the order of "V'hayah Bracha" [the week of Parshas V'eschanan] and the one preceding it. I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during a time of favor. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding matters of physical health and matters of spiritual health, for the two are interdependent.

Since you have merited to serve for a time as a *moreh hora'ah* in Yisrael—which is to say, you have been gifted with the power to influence others—it is understood that you cannot fulfill your obligation as an individual until you influence your entire environment to disseminate matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and the *maayanos* in particular. There is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8135

B"H, 14 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and engaged in communal needs, R' Boruch, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter arrived in due time, and I also confirmed its receipt in my *Shanah Tovah* letter. During the weeks of the month of Tishrei and the first weeks thereafter, it is generally only possible to respond to letters that pertain to *ma'aseh b'fo'al* (practical action). Therefore, the response to your arguments regarding the state of *Yiddishkeit* in the United States was delayed until a later time, as, unfortunately, it is not currently a matter of immediate practical urgency.

A general response is that all such arguments do not exempt anyone who is capable of taking action. Furthermore, the fact that someone else is not doing what they ought to do, or is not doing it to the fullest extent, does not justify one in following their example. Perhaps, on the contrary: since someone else is not doing it and I see this, it is proof that I must act in that area—including the other person’s share—since I am capable of doing so. Understandably, this does not apply only to you, but also to me and to the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*; and on the other hand, you are also included in that collective.

Regarding what you write at the end of your letter, that you are exhausted: I have already written to someone else that now is not the time for that. That is fine in quiet times—when one goes for a walk or reads papers, one can afford to be exhausted and not act. But in a country like America, where the largest concentration of Jews is found, there is no time to be exhausted. As for the question of where one draws the strength from, the answer is that for everything that *Hashem Yisbarach* has commanded us to do, He provides the strength. The difference lies only in the order: sometimes the strength comes first and the actions follow, and sometimes the order is reversed—the work must come first, and the strength reveals itself later. It is not worth the effort to ponder which should come first; one must utilize the time to **throw** oneself into the work, or into the continuation of the work, with more strength. Then, one will find within oneself more strength than one had imagined beforehand, as explained in my *Michtav Klali* for *Rosh Hashanah*.

I was pleased to hear that a *Seudas Malka Meshicha* was organized by you, and may *Hashem Yisbarach* help that very soon we should celebrate such and similar gatherings together with him.

With blessings for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8138

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 MarCheshvan. I trust that in the meantime you have received my letter responding to your previous correspondence, and it is surely unnecessary to remind you once again of the necessity to pursue all the negotiations you are writing about with the greatest possible energy.

It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter who the candidates are for the apartments in the housing project that is to be built, as the nature of the terms and much more depends on this.

Regarding your question as to whether the committee should also add a certain minimum percentage, it is understood that this is necessary, since over time changes are liable to occur—including those that may increase the committee's expenses—and it will not always be possible for the committee to increase its demands upon the residents.

It is also my understanding that the custom in such matters is to create a certain reserve for those who will not fulfill the terms in full, as I have written previously regarding such matters.

It is also surprising that you are not investigating what is done in such cases in other places in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), as they are building housing projects in many places, and there is certainly a standard contract format, as well as calculations regarding the housing projects, the price of the apartments, etc. Why should you be an exception to the rule if there are no special reasons for it? Furthermore, it is possible that some of the terms might provoke grievances, whereas if they know in advance that this is the standard practice in Eretz Yisrael, there is no room for grievances at all.

I will await good news regarding the above, and it goes without saying regarding the upcoming 19 Kislev as well, since time is short and the work is complex and also extensive.

## 839

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, R' Chaim Zusia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters—from the 2nd of Kislev and the one preceding it—as well as your four *pidyonos nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is a great wonder that, given the news received from the other side that preparations are being made for a youth gathering in Kfar Chabad, followed by a study day for the IDF, and then—the following day—a general *farbrengen*, your letter does not mention a word about the first two gatherings. It is a necessity that for such matters, a structured plan be made **well in advance**. As I have written many times, negligence in this regard and beginning preparations at the last minute has caused great damage until now, and furthermore, it prevents the potential success of the *farbrengen* and the gatherings—both success in material matters and success in spiritual matters. This is especially true at this time, when several plans related to Kfar Chabad are on the agenda; bringing hearts closer together will be of great benefit in this, and even regarding general relations—even if they are temporary, the memory of that closeness will remain.

Regarding what you wrote about the housing and the vocational houses: for my part, I requested that both the vocational houses and the housing be built. Since you are included in the category of a professional, it is worthwhile to remain within this framework.

Regarding what you wrote about the addresses in Eretz Yisrael of those who correspond with us here: they are located at Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Tel Aviv, as the New Year greetings—which were sent to almost all those who correspond with us here—were sent through them. It is understood that you may show them this letter of mine so that they will permit you to copy the addresses. However, it is understood that in your correspondence regarding books, etc., you **must not** mention the connection through letters to here. There is also no necessity for this.

I await good and detailed news regarding all that was mentioned, and also that the stolen item regarding which you wrote is found.

With blessings for a joyous and active *farbrengen*.

On behalf of the Rebbe,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 140

140

[19 Kislev, 5718]

The essence of the victory of 19 Kislev is that our Torah is a "Torah of life," relevant to every day and to all its parts; each and every one of us is connected to it and obligated in it, out of the Creator’s love for us.

May it be His will that this should ignite our youth—our future—especially those in the Holy Land, to direct their lives toward the light of Torah and mitzvos and the "light" within them, and to disseminate them in their entire surroundings with Chassidic warmth. Then they will be truly happy, living lives full of the substance of joy and peace.

May it be His will that you find your path through *kabbalas ol*, cooperation, and the recognition of the individual, whose conduct influences—and at times even determines—the fate of the many, and for the building of the Land of Israel and its protection; for "your camp shall be holy," and Hashem your G-d will dwell in your midst.

With blessings for a successful *farbrengen*.

## 8143

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the group of residents of Kfar Chabad engaged in agriculture,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write that in your opinion the farmers in Kfar Chabad and their affairs are being neglected, and the reason for this is that there is no special committee for agricultural matters.

It is understood that it is impossible to create a special committee for every single matter in the village, for if so, there would be no end to the matter. Instead of a unified administration—which, for the time being, has not succeeded in preventing division of hearts, etc.—there would arise several committees, which would only cause further division of hearts, and so on and so forth.

I have written to the village committee with my suggestion: that when they deliberate on agricultural matters, they should include, during the discussion, a representative of the farmers in Kfar Chabad. That is to say, the farmers will be represented by a spokesperson—**to explain** (but not to vote, etc.) the details of the situation regarding this matter before the committee, from the perspective of the farmers.

However, it is also understood that just as it is necessary for the general and private benefit that the committee take an interest in the welfare of the farmers, it is likewise necessary—and also for the general and private benefit of the farmers—that the farmers take an interest in the other residents of the village as well. Through the cooperation of everyone together, this is the vessel for success in all matters, both for the farmers and for the other affairs of the village, and for the increase of the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam in this.

May it be the will that my strongest hope begins to be realized: that the number of farmers in Kfar Chabad increases, and that the situation of the farmers improves within the context of the other affairs of the village, both in quantity and in quality, and in both matters in a way that is ever-increasing from time to time and from period to period, and in a good that is revealed and manifest.

With blessings for the expansion of the mind and the expansion of livelihood, both materially and spiritually, and for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

P.S. **Copy to the Village Committee.**

## 8144

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I have come to add to what was written regarding the matter... that there was no time to consult. It is obvious that it is no justification at all to decide on a matter that concerns the many based on the opinion of one individual. Especially since, if there was time to ask the opinion of three [people], there was certainly time to ask the opinion of the remaining three. And primarily, how is it possible that there was no time, when they ultimately drafted a telegram and decided to wait for a response from here, etc.?

Regarding the future—there must be order in the affairs of Chabad; it cannot be that each person acts according to what comes to his mind. For even regarding the greatest of Israel, it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is safety," and "Do not judge alone," for there is no "alone" except for One, and the "One" refers to the Holy One, Blessed be He, and not to someone who is "another." This is understandable in private matters—that is the way of the world—but not in general matters. Especially when a political party is involved, and in a period where partisanship is prevalent in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

From this, it is understood that my request to instruct how to conduct oneself in this regard in the future means that such questions must be brought for discussion before the administration of... and similarly, if a question such as this arises in another place—within the appropriate framework.

It is obvious that all of the above does not detract at all from the merit of this or that person who has been entrusted with a special task of energy and vitality, etc., for the infusion of energy and vitality does not necessitate individual rule or a dictatorial approach.

It is a pity that he does not at least mention the main points of the *p'shat* (explanation) that he delivered from here. My hope is strong that he chose those points that can bring about practical results and activities for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and the *maayanos* (wellsprings) in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. And surely he will also fulfill this at the next opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 145

2, 5, 6 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated to communal needs, R' Yitzchok, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Mikeitz and those preceding it, in which you write regarding the idea of a teachers' seminary.

Here is a general directive, and specifically in a case such as this: It is not the way of Chabad to compete for the sake of competition, but rather to act for the sake of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and the spreading of the wellsprings in particular. Furthermore, as with every matter in the world, resources (funds, as well as personnel, and the like) are limited; when they are diverted to one area, it is inevitable that it will affect another. From this, it is understood that in a field where there are already sufficient people engaged in Torah-true education, it is not the way of Chabad to push itself into that space. And it goes without saying that it is not our concern if the matter requires the greatest of efforts, both in terms of resources and personnel. It is understood that a teachers' seminary requires experts in the field of organization, and even if we were to assume that there would be a sufficient number of people wishing to attend a seminary that would bear the name of Chabad, there are even greater difficulties: Who would be the teachers in the seminary (who must be experts in the subjects they teach, and surely must be recognized by the appropriate offices, and there is a concern that they would specifically require certificates testifying to their expertise)? These difficulties are compounded if we assume the seminary would not be in a large city, but rather in a village or a moshav. Regarding a teachers' seminary, every one of the conditions for obligation is **absent**—my meaning is that there are already Torah-true teachers' seminaries, and I do not see experts who would teach in this seminary, especially if they would have to travel to Kfar Chabad. The matter would require the greatest of resources to organize, and I am doubtful whether the number of students would be close to one hundred or the opposite, as one candle serves one and one candle serves a hundred. Based on all the above, the entire matter is not understood. It would be worthwhile to recruit all those who are qualified to study the craft of teaching in those existing seminaries, and at most, to enter into discussions with the existing Torah-true seminaries and demand improvements from them, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about youth hostels, you do not explain what the matter is, its goal, its method, etc. You will surely fill this in at the next opportunity.

In response to the telegram regarding his candidacy and that of Uri Ben-Shachar, may he live, concerning Sdei Micha: I telegraphed today that it is worthwhile for him to take this upon himself [my intention here is primarily for the initial period until the matter is organized as needed, i.e., until the end of the school year, and surely he will be able to arrange the matter in a way that will not affect **at all** the preparations regarding the summer camp, as well as other general matters of the Reshet that he has begun to engage in]. The reason is that, based on what I spoke about with Mr. Levnon, may he live, regarding the expansion of the Reshet building in Jaffa as required, it is not worthwhile to introduce changes now to the school there, so that there will be no room for any pretext to delay the promise, etc. And another reason, which is the main one, is that my hope is strong, based on having known him here, that he will work on the Sdei Micha matter with the necessary vigor and will succeed in establishing the matter well. Indeed, there is room to say that the way this institution is established will determine the relations with the appropriate offices, and the wise will understand.

With a blessing for success in his holy work and for good tidings regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**R' Yitzchok, may he live:** Ginsburg. Additional letters to him appear above, 142, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 8196

B"H, 17 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

It is astonishing that the matter of the housing project—and even the preparations for its planning—has dragged on for such an excessively long time. In such matters, there is room to say that the longer the matter is drawn out, the more the difficulties and concealments surrounding it multiply.

It is understood that the order of priority regarding the housing is: 1) for farmers, 2) for those engaged in the work of teaching. And it is simple that one who has no dwelling at all in the village takes precedence over one who wishes to exchange his home for a better one.

It is understood that the above are general guidelines; in such matters, one does not set hard-and-fast rules, and there may be exceptions.

Following the above, it is a wonder that, on one hand, you write to me many times about the very small number of those engaged in agriculture, yet on the other hand, when I advise someone to engage in agriculture, he answers me that all the agricultural plots, all the fields, etc., have already been distributed, and there is no available land. Yet, in the planning of the village, there were areas sufficiently large for dozens of people to engage in agriculture—what has become of them?

Awaiting good tidings in all the above.

## 8149

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Vaad of Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 26 Shevat, 10, 12, and 19 Adar. I look forward to hearing truly good news—that is, good for Heaven and good for people, as per the instruction of our Sages (Kiddushin 40a). It is, of course, very distressing that the discord among hearts does not seem to be diminishing, and on the contrary.

It is surprising to read what you wrote regarding the lack of assistance for the expenses of the farbrengens; surely there is some misunderstanding in this matter.

It is understood that since you spoke about a loan and your request was granted, you must accept it and utilize it in a good and productive manner, consistent with the purpose for which the loan was discussed. For if, for whatever reason, you were to withdraw from the loan, there is reason to fear that doors will be closed to such requests in the future.

I have already written this several times, and I reiterate it now: it is imperative that Kfar Chabad not lose, G-d forbid, its character as an agricultural settlement. While it is understood and simple that this does not mean the exclusive dominance of agricultural matters over all other affairs of the village—there is certainly enough room for mutual benefit between the field of agriculture and all other areas. Moreover, as I have written many times, the Mishnah rules that "one mitzvah leads to another." Through the drawing together of hearts and cooperation, every advancement in one area of the village brings benefit to all areas of the village. Indeed, even with physical eyes, one can see the truth of the Mishnah, that "peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He."

Regarding the question of whether to deposit the funds designated for housing into the authority and treasury of the Vaad of Kfar Chabad: considering the current situation, which is still not one of abundance, there is a great fear that there will be a very strong temptation to refrain from lending these funds for other communal needs of the village. Especially since there are those who will find a justification and say that since the housing project is being postponed from day to day, from week to week, and from month to month, what difference does it make if it is postponed for a bit longer, and they will use the money for the village's needs, which also must be met, etc. This is particularly relevant since the housing project was announced publicly, in the presence of several representatives from government offices last 19 Kislev, and until now, it seems that there is **not** even any tangible movement toward its realization, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding the loan for water-based crops and the other matters mentioned in your letters: my perspective is as stated above—that any loan offered should be accepted. If there is a concern, as you write, that there is no one to manage this work, you should accept the funds for a period of time and then return them. You may even return them before the due date, provided that you do not establish a pattern of requesting a loan and then not utilizing it.

With blessings for success in establishing and developing Kfar Chabad in all its areas, both materially and spiritually, with true peace of mind, and for a kosher and happy Pesach, with body and soul.

## 8,152

8,152

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

A letter was received here from an individual who, although distant from Chabad circles, is a friend and supporter of its activities. He claims that a member has leased some of the village’s fields to a contractor who employs Arabs, and he is concerned about the impression this will make within the public sphere, etc.

I have no information regarding the accuracy of this matter, nor whether the concern is well-founded, but in any case, I am bringing the matter to your attention.

With respect and blessing.

#### ***8,152***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L’Melech*, Vol. 3, p. 74.

## 8,153

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Raphael Pinchas, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a delay, your letter of the 11th of Nissan, the month of redemption, was received, detailing the highlights of your activities and those of your colleagues, may they live.

May it be the will of Hashem that, out of joy and goodness of heart, you increase such activities for many years to come, in a manner of "ascending and adding."

It is certainly unnecessary to remind you and your colleagues, may they live, of what is written: "Is it not to share your bread with the hungry..." and "do not hide yourself from your own flesh." As explained by our Sages in Tanna D'bei Eliyahu Rabbah: "If you see the naked" (in Torah and mitzvos), "clothe him" (i.e., activity with others), and "do not hide yourself from your own flesh"—this refers to activity within oneself. My intention is simple: perseverance in the study of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus, and the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, with the central point of all this being tefillah. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for success in the holy work of spreading the wellsprings (until they reach) the outermost reaches.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8154

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5718

It is well known that the words of the Tzaddikim and their actions endure forever, and they exert their influence in a very literal sense in daily life. Surely, these influences will further increase the blessings of Hashem in all the matters mentioned above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8155

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Iyar, my telegram has surely been received by now.

I emphasize once again that not only am I pained, but I also do not understand the position of Anash regarding the aforementioned matter. This is especially true given that they view themselves as if they are dependent on the goodwill of those who fight against them, and therefore feel they must accede to all sorts of strange demands (as I wrote to [Name]), which are also contrary to simple, healthy common sense.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, that they promised to change their attitude, etc.—I do not know who promised this. According to the information I am receiving, the opposite is true: the attitude is only deteriorating. Although one could find a merit for them, seeing as they do whatever their hearts desire while Anash come with bowed heads and ask them for permission—asking whether it is permitted for Anash to engage in chinuch as commanded by our Rebbeim, or if so-and-so does not wish for it, and therefore they should withdraw—furthermore, some of Anash even send their children specifically to those who have adopted a line of opposition to Chabad and its interests.

It is sheer chutzpah to open an educational institution within the four cubits of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, and even more so—to then demand that Chabad shut down its own school.

It is possible that the reason for the conclusion of your letter is fear of who will win in this matter. But as has already been the case, others have risen up against the interests of our Rebbeim, and we see **tangibly** who ultimately wins. It is a source of shame and indignation that the situation has reached the point where the opposing side feels they can speak in a tone of command and requirement, as if we are dependent on their favor, and not only is there no response to them, but people even grovel before them.

My hope, as I wrote in my telegram, is that at least now **all of Anash** will mobilize for the interests of our Rebbeim, for we are doing their shlichus. When they proceed with strength in this, they will immediately see that this was nothing more than a test—meaning, that there is no reality to the opposition, only chutzpah without any merit.

I am not emphasizing in this letter which school the children of Anash should attend, because it is inherently wondrous and **incomprehensible** that it should be necessary to send a telegram across the sea to state that Chassidim of our Rebbeim must enroll their children in the schools of our Rebbeim. It is self-evident that they must distance themselves from any school that opposes our Rebbeim.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

I await good tidings regarding the above in your reply.

P.S. Due to the urgency of the matter, this response is being sent without waiting for the regular turn.

## 8159

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 10th of the month of redemption and joy, along with the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of the master of the celebration, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I was very pleased by the opening of your letter, which comes this time with joy to inform me, etc. May it be His will that with this beginning, your affairs will proceed in ways of joy, in goodness that is visible and revealed from here on in, both in spiritual matters and in material matters—for the one is dependent upon the other—and likewise in general matters and in specific matters, for these too are dependent upon one another.

And since we are commanded to "increase in holiness," may all of this be in a manner that is ever-increasing, both regarding the actions of man and regarding the blessings of Heaven from above—and naturally, in matters of the body and its health, for it is specifically regarding the body that it is said, "And You have chosen us from among every people and tongue," as is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 49.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Regarding the treatment of your son, *shlita*—follow the instructions of a specialist physician for success in body and soul.

## 8,558

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter informing me that on the 15th of Menachem Av you reached the age of twelve, the time of Bas Mitzvah.

May it be the will of Hashem that you accept upon yourself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and the yoke of the mitzvos with a whole heart. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success in your studies and in your conduct, and may you grow to be worthy of the name "daughter of Chabad," in accordance with the will of our holy Nesi’im, may their merit protect us.

May you also influence your friends in this regard, through speech, and even more so by being a living example of a daughter of Yisrael educated in the ways of Chassidus. This will bring you spiritual and material happiness.

With blessings.

Regarding your question about where to continue your studies and your path—

In my opinion, since the education of youth—especially during the years of your age—influences the entire duration of one's life, and since one's independence and strength depend upon it, enabling one to withstand the trials that exist in the life of every individual,

And since we are in a period of many changes, where it is impossible to estimate at all the nature of life's conditions a few years from now, and therefore it is also impossible to know the magnitude of the trials then, so as not to stumble in matters of justice and integrity, faith and religion—

Therefore, every young person must and is obligated to receive a religious education to the maximum degree, so that they may be able to withstand any danger that might arise, Heaven forbid.

And even if such an education involves some inconvenience or the like for a period of time—what does that count for in comparison to the fortification and added strength one receives, specifically through this education, for the entire duration of life?

#### ***8,558***

From the Secretariat's copy

## 595

[Late Elul 5718]

...Regarding what you wrote about how "yoke" (ol) is applicable to angels—that is, performing a matter that is the opposite of the intellect and understanding of that created being—this is possible only through their kabbalas ol. After all, even angels do not grasp anything beyond the level of their own cause, and nothing higher than that (see Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, chapter 2, halacha 8; chapter 3, halacha 5). See also Sanhedrin 110a, bottom of the page, and elsewhere.

## 8160

8160

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, R' Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters in due time, dated the 1st, 2nd, and 20th of Elul. To my great astonishment, I have learned that you are not taking care of your health.

It is surprising that one must write about such simple matters from across the sea, at a time when the **demand** of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, regarding the preservation of the body is well known. According to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, "You shall surely help [the animal] with **him**" (*azov ta'azov imo*) — specifically with him. Among Chassidim, there is no distinction regarding the nature of the directive of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im; it is simply a matter that must be fulfilled completely. Given the simplicity of the matter, I will not elaborate further.

I trust you will inform me that, regardless of how the situation has been in the past, from here on you will conduct yourself according to the aforementioned directive regarding the preservation of the body. After all, having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem.

With the blessing of a *Chasimah V'Gmar Chasimah Tovah* and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 861

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Eliyahu Akiva, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

After a long interval, your letter from Erev Yom Kippur was received, along with the enclosed check, which has been handed to the secretariat and will be addressed.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter that you feel a drawing together of hearts, even though, as you write, it is naturally not yet to a sufficient degree for the time being. May it be G-d’s will that this movement grows increasingly, until it reaches the state of "all of you," as the Alter Rebbe says regarding "uniting as one" (Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Nitzavim). This is especially pertinent as all these days of the month of Tishrei are generally connected and linked to Rosh Hashanah, regarding which it is said, "You are standing today... all of you."

Regarding what you wrote about your situation, and that you are losing a certain sum annually because of your work for the Kerem Chabad institution: if this is indeed the case, it is a great foolishness on their part. Furthermore—and this is the main point—you will certainly not lose out materially because of this. On the contrary, you will only gain more, just as we have seen tangibly with all those who have involved themselves in the affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe; in the end, they succeeded in both spirituality and materiality alike. And this is well understood.

Since we are approaching our festival [Sukkos], when all the matters that were brought about during the time of the "hidden moon" and the Ten Days of Repentance in general are revealed, then in this matter, too, it will be revealed in a revealed good, even "below ten handbreadths," etc.

Wishing you good tidings and a happy holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

## 863

864

B"H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is surely superfluous to emphasize that for Bnei Yisrael in general, and regarding students of the Yeshiva in particular, and regarding students of Tomchei Temimim especially, every matter of kindness from the Ribono shel Olam has the purpose of causing one to increase his avodah to his Creator: the study of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus, and the performance of His mitzvos with hiddur. Included in these is the great principle of the Torah: "Love your fellow as yourself." This means that study and action should be in a manner that serves as a living example to one's peers and surroundings, so that they, too, will increase in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos. And there is no greater love or tzedakah than that which brings a person to the life of this world and the World to Come.

## 8165

B"H, 28 MarCheshvan, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Cheshvan, I am replying promptly, without waiting for my turn, because of the point it raises regarding organizing a fundraising campaign for a new, additional purpose. Regarding this, there are two points to consider:

1) One should not conduct a fundraising campaign in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) for Chabad institutions abroad, at a time when there are several Chabad matters in Eretz Yisrael that are in need of funds and lack them. From the above, it is understood that no fundraising campaign should be conducted for the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch. Only Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and the Building Fund, as until now, or matters of the Reshet and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, should be taken into account. But, of course, regarding this, you must consult with the institutions in Eretz Yisrael—in general and regarding the practical methods of implementation.

2) In any matter of fundraising, it is impossible for the person who is the collector to also be the one in charge.

As I wrote in my previous letter, in financial matters, one must be even more careful to fulfill one's obligation toward people, in addition to fulfilling one's obligation toward Hashem.

In general, I must point out that experience has shown tangibly that when one jumps every time to a new task, it is not beneficial for any matter, but rather causes a scattering of the soul. From this it is understood: since you are already occupied with the Building Fund and the distribution of Kehot books, you should not specifically seek out new matters. For in any case: if you exert yourself properly and in an organized manner, there is a channel for blessing and success in the areas in which you are occupied. And if there is a need for improvement in the methods of work, this will be lacking as well, even if you choose new areas of work...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

866

In response to your letter of 9 Kislev... As for us, we shall continue our work without paying heed to those who oppose the matters of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his holy institutions. As for all those who obscure and conceal this, who oppose and fight against it—may it be His will that they turn back from this path in good time, especially when they contemplate the end of all those who have fought against my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It is known that the Heavenly Court ruled that because of this *mesiras nefesh* (of the Alter Rebbe) for the teachings of Chassidus, the Heavenly Court decreed that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are *mekushar* to him and follow in his footsteps shall be on top...

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 867

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Eshel-Tzeirei HaAnash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established,

Peace and blessing!

That is to say, in the manner of the statement of our Sages: "He who has one hundred wants two hundred"—an increase of one hundred only; but "he who has two hundred wants four hundred"—an increase of two hundred, and so on.

May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize the influence from Above in all these matters to its fullest extent. As is well known, the verdict from Above is that because of this mesiras nefesh (of our Alter Rebbe) for the Torah of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are his followers and walk in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

And this is also the channel and the vessel for your own matters—for your success in the study of Torah with yiras shamayim and in the performance of mitzvos with hidur. And through this [...] in the avodah of tefillah of each and every one, [you will achieve] the most sublime inner dimensions of these activities.

With blessings for success in all that has been mentioned, and for good and detailed tidings.

## 8160

B"H, 5th of Chanukah, 5719
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Tel Aviv branch,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

Thank you for the good news regarding the farbrengen of the bright day of 19 Kislev — the Rosh Hashanah of the Torah of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus.

May it be Hashem’s will that you continue to hear good news in both general and personal matters.

Furthermore, it is ultimately necessary to work tangibly to establish the financial situation as required for all these activities and for those that will be added to them. Likewise, there must be interest — and activities in accordance with its results — to ensure there is **continuity** and lasting impact from the visits, farbrengens, etc., by establishing a shiur in Chassidus, maintaining contact through correspondence, encouraging enrollment in Chabad educational institutions, and the like.

## 1770

1770

B"H, 11 Teves, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... It was a pleasure for me to read about your establishing a regular study of Chassidus in public, and also that you are exerting effort in spreading Chassidus in various ways. You will certainly not be satisfied with this, for in all matters we are commanded to ascend in holiness, and especially in the Holy of Holies—the inner dimension of Torah—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Regarding what you wrote, that you have begun studying Tanya with a class of adults and started with the first chapter of Sefer Tanya—experience has shown that regarding certain types of people, they are more successful when they begin with Part II of Tanya or Iggeres HaTeshuvah, and only afterwards study Part I. Although, of course, one cannot set hard and fast rules about this, and a person should study in the place where his heart desires.

## 171

B"H, 18 Teves, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and upright individual, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc.,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of the 9th and 13th of Teves, in which you write regarding the improvements in certain areas of the Oholei Torah school, which Divine Providence has privileged you to manage.

May it be the will of Hashem that this improvement continue to grow and increase, and may the situation in the other areas you mention also improve, and in all matters may there be a continuous increase, going from strength to strength, until it is very great.

It is understood and simple that not only is it permitted for you to write about all the matters you mentioned, but it is also your duty and your privilege. However, it is appropriate that you also add a proposed solution for the points that require correction and improvement. Naturally, these proposals must be made in a way that will not lead to destruction in other areas, especially since we see tangibly that sometimes the destruction is clear, while the correction and improvement will only become apparent after some time—sometimes for the better, and sometimes, etc.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the farbrengen in Kfar Chabad this past 19 Kislev. However, there is one point that causes me distress, which in my opinion is significant—assuming, of course, that the report is true—and that is that it seems some of the youth arrived and were not permitted to enter the place of the farbrengen, and they wandered outside the venue without anyone showing any interest in them at all. Surely it would have been possible to arrange things in some way so that there would be a farbrengen outside the main venue as well. Especially since, as I recall, this has been done several times before, where men farbrenged in one place and women in another building, and the like.

A possible correction for the above: If these youths are from organized groups, you surely know their contact information, and there is room to explain the reason to them. It is also possible, at the next farbrengen, to do something special for them in order to appease their minds, or at the very least, to establish a connection with them via letter, etc.

My intention in writing this to you is comprehensive, as it is worthwhile that you also arouse others who are involved in this matter. It has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8172

B"H, 26 Teves, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter regarding the utilization of the ten-year anniversary of the founding and inception of the Kfar, and your request for my opinion on whether to focus on this.

Regarding the above, the starting point must be from the other end—that is, are there suitable people who will occupy themselves with organizing the aforementioned in a specifically appropriate manner? If so, then it is a proper endeavor.

Regarding the above, a detailed and well-founded plan is necessary in advance, even more so than for other matters of the Kfar, since such a thing can only be done once every so many years. Therefore, the effort must be made to utilize the celebration to its fullest, and this is understood.

It is understood that "who can discern errors" applies to everyone, but that is only an excuse after one has exerted all the effort that depends on man, or at the very least, an approximation close to certainty.

It is surely superfluous to add that if the appropriate attention is given, one can hope for the most elevated and important results from such a celebration.

It is also superfluous to point out that this is not necessarily tied to a specific day, for it has already become customary in our times that even matters connected to a specific time, the celebrations and their utilization are possible even after that time has passed.

And many reasons can be found for changing the date, provided there is benefit in doing so.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***8172***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L’Melech* 1, p. 106.

## 8173

B"H, 28 Teves, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the avreich [name]... may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following a very long hiatus, I received your letter dated 24 Teves, the hillula of the Alter Rebbe, in which you write about your current situation and regarding the people you have met during this time.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you to maintain your connection with them, even though you are not in the same place, by means of letters and the like. The purpose of this connection is, naturally and simply, that through it their connection to Hashem, the G-d of Yisrael, will increase—a connection that reaches the level of dveikus, as it is written: "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today." And there is a presumption that outreach will not return empty.

And even though you write that those who wish to learn are not learning lishmah, etc.—why concern yourself with the hidden ways of the Merciful One? You must do your part, and the Torah will do its part to eventually return them to the proper path.

Since your friend [name]... may he live, is with you, it is understood that all of the above is directed to him as well; "each man shall help his brother" in the dissemination of true Yiddishkeit and all its matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8174

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 5719
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos, Tomchei Temimim

Blessings and Peace!

Regarding your notification that this coming Tuesday, 11 Shevat, your annual event will take place for the benefit of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshivos:

I send my greetings and blessing to the leadership and members, as well as to all participants and guests—shlita—that the event should be successful in both a material and a spiritual sense.

In a material sense—to generate the anticipated support for the yeshivos and to strengthen your work in this regard.

In a spiritual sense—recognizing the great zechus of being active for such a holy cause, to create a strong connection for each of you to the spirit of Lubavitch, and with Chassidishe warmth and light, to bring some of that spirit—the spirit of ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael—into your own homes and the surrounding environment.

And since the event is taking place the day after the yom hahilula (yahrzeit) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder of these yeshivos here in America—and everyone knows that *divrei tzaddikim uvirchosaihem kayamin la'ad* (the words and blessings of tzaddikim endure forever)—

May the blessings of the baal hahilula stand by each and every one of you and your families, shlita, both generally and specifically.

With blessings for success in all that is needed, in gashmius and in ruchnius.

## 151

It is somewhat surprising that, apparently, you did not consult regarding the entire matter with our dear Anash who are in Casablanca, who have been there for several years and are familiar with the doctors and their expertise. I look forward to hearing good news, and I sign with abundant blessings, both materially and spiritually.

**M. Schneerson**
