## 8176

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the Organization of Students of the Yeshiva Erev in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure, I received your letter of 10 Shevat, the day of the Hillula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, Nasi of Israel.

Its content included good resolutions regarding an increase in the study of our holy Torah—Torah of life, the revealed Torah, and the Torah of Chassidus.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you fulfill these resolutions in practice. And, in accordance with the teaching of the Mishnah, "a mitzvah draws another mitzvah," may you add to them many times over.

My hope is strong that this, too, will be fulfilled: "The jealousy of scribes increases wisdom." My meaning is that this conduct of yours will arouse a "holy jealousy" among your friends, acquaintances, and peers.

As the Sages of blessed memory stated, and as it is written, "Do not let your heart envy sinners, but rather [be] in the fear of Hashem all day" (Mishlei 23:17). This is explained at length in the sefer *Orchos Tzaddikim* and in *Or HaTorah* by my revered ancestor, the Tzemach Tzedek (Vayetzei, 217b and onwards). May they, too, increase in all of the above, each and every one of them [becoming] a Chassid, a G-d-fearing person, and a scholar.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8177

As is precisely explained, it does not say "you have understood" or "you have grasped," but rather "and you have found"—in the manner of a *metzi'ah* (a windfall), which is beyond one's calculated estimation. ## 8178

8178

B"H, 9 Adar, 5719

Undoubtedly, such a report will also clarify several points regarding future activities.

Surely you are preparing in good time a plan to utilize the upcoming days of Purim in an appropriate manner. May it be the will of Hashem that it be with success, reaching the level of *ad d'lo yada*, as explained in the writings of the Arizal and Chassidus.

## 8179

B"H, 19 Adar I, 5719
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Purim Katan regarding the arrangements for the third memorial day, etc., in which you ask for my opinion on the matter:

It seems to me that I have already written regarding such matters, that the general point is that any such positive activity is good. Certainly, from a lack of action, there will be no results at all, not even the most minor ones. However, it is also understood and simple, regarding the organization of such an event, that it **must** be done in a manner that is properly arranged and planned as required.

Furthermore, I must add—as I have prompted you many times—that the time has long since arrived for Anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, to occupy themselves not only with plowing and sowing, but also with harvesting and gathering the fruits. Similarly, regarding the aforementioned matter, one must determine the specific purpose toward which the institution and its practical development are aimed—whether in physical terms (through fundraising, or increasing the number of supporters and active participants, etc.) or in spiritual terms (publicizing the matter so that the number of students actually increases, etc.). In accordance with these possibilities, you should make your decision, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
A. Quint, Secretary

## 8180

B”H, 6 Adar II, 5719
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 28 Adar I, along with the enclosures.

It is understood and simple that what I wrote to you regarding the plot where the Chabad school building will be constructed was merely a general observation. The decision in this matter depends on the possibilities, the local conditions, etc. It is also understood and simple that a location without electricity, etc., is not under consideration at all. The very doubt regarding this is surprising.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the plans for the construction of the new Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim building in Kfar Chabad:

I believe I have already written that the only instruction that can be given from here is that it is desirable to build in a way that can be done stage by stage—meaning, as long as all the necessary funds are not available, at least a portion of a wing should be completed that can be utilized. However, it should be done in such a way that when additional funds are acquired, you will be able to add to the building, and it will fit and integrate with the part of the building that preceded it, and so on.

Regarding what you wrote about organizing courses:

I believe that regarding this, too, I have already written that it is more desirable to utilize the courses that already exist at the time. Consequently, their advantages and disadvantages are known, as well as what one must be careful about. Do not begin with the idea of founding your own courses in great haste, when it is unknown who the lecturer will be, etc., and so on and so forth. And I believe this was also written: If there is a sufficiently significant number of participants in these courses from Chabad, you will surely be able to effect a change in the curriculum and the like, if there is a need to demand these changes.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8181

B"H, 16 Adar Sheni, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Yaakov, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you outline the places you have studied until now, your study schedule, the recent challenges you have faced, and your moving from place to place, and noting that you have now returned to Tomchei Temimim in France, and detailing several considerations regarding your place of study and your future arrangements.

Since we have heard the instruction from our Rebbes, of blessed memory, that a yeshiva student in general, and a student of Tomchei Temimim in particular, must conduct himself in accordance with the guidance of the yeshiva administration,

And this is also understood from the ruling in the revealed Torah, "And you shall teach them to your children"—these are the students—and a person is obligated to honor his teacher, etc.

Therefore, you should detail your matters and all your reasoning and arguments to the administration of Tomchei Temimim in Brunoy and act according to their instruction.

It is understood and simple that since one needs Siyatta Dishmaya for every matter, any addition on your part in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus will increase the blessings of Hashem and your success in all the matters about which you write.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8182

B"H, 23 Adar II, 5719
Brooklyn.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that as one increases in matters of Torah and mitzvos—and however good the situation may be in this regard, there is always room to add more in matters of goodness and holiness—one thereby increases the blessings of Hashem for what a person and his household require.

In particular, your efforts to instill Yiddishkeit and its values in your surroundings, especially in the field of pure, holy education—and as you wrote, that you have worked and exerted all your strength for the benefit of the Chabad religious school where several of your friends are also involved—will stand for you and your household, and for them and their households, in increasing the blessings of Hashem for what is needed, both materially and spiritually. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the matters you wrote about in your letter, as well as regarding general matters, and in this specific area—the consolidation and development of the Chabad school, both in quality and quantity.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

P.S. Since you mention in your letter the pressure regarding your livelihood, the advice of Chazal in this regard is well known: to increase in tzedakah and to divide the amount to be given into many small portions. One of the auspicious times for this is every weekday before the morning davening.

## 8184

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5719
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Nissan: Regarding what you wrote about distracting thoughts, the known advice for this is to daven and to learn from inside a sefer. Even when your eyes are closed, the sefer should remain open before you, as the letters hold the thought (halten ein di machshava).

Regarding what you wrote about influencing the avreich... shlita with whom you are learning, to influence him in matters of Torah and yiras shamayim: you should consult with those who know the nature of the young man’s soul. It has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation" (Mishlei 11:14). Furthermore, Chazal have taught us another point regarding this: that whoever possesses yiras shamayim, his words are heeded. This means that as you increase in your own yiras shamayim, there will be a corresponding increase in the one who listens to your voice, and this is well understood.

At a time of ratzon, you should mention all those you wrote about at the holy tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, zatzukal-lah-h, navgam, zya. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that was mentioned—namely, that you are increasing in the study of Torah with diligence and persistence, in the performance of mitzvos with hiddur, and that you are successful in the aforementioned.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,
Secretary

The magnitude of this matter cannot be sufficiently explained in a letter. The vehemence of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (shortly after his arrival in the United States), is well-known, as are his most sharp words against the heads of the Yeshivos and the G-d-fearing activists here—all for the sake of adding **one** hour to the study of holy subjects; and how much more so is this the case in the present matter.

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5719
Brooklyn

Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, Tel Aviv branch.

Shalom u’Bracha!

Enclosed is a copy of a response to Mr. Alexander Z. Bonin regarding the fact that Mr. Mordechai Epstein wishes to donate a plot of his land to Chabad, in order to establish an appropriate educational institution upon it—one that will include not only the study of Torah, but also the study of a trade.

It is appropriate that you establish contact with Mr. Bonin as soon as possible, first, and subsequently with the aforementioned [Mr. Epstein], after you have learned all the details from Mr. Bonin.

Regarding the question of what should be established on the site, we await your proposals—that is, more precisely, what type of institution, etc. It appears that the matter is urgent, as the aforementioned [Mr. Epstein] is impatient. Furthermore, there is someone who apparently wishes to dissuade him from donating the land, etc. You will also learn the details of this from Mr. Bonin.

We await confirmation of receipt of this letter, as well as [a report on] what is being done regarding this matter, as soon as possible.

## 8188

B"H, 28 Nissan, 5719
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from after Pesach.

...Regarding what you wrote about the *avreich*... may he live, and his question concerning a *shidduch*: I have already stated my position, in the style of our Sages that one does not mix one *mitzvah* with another. Similarly, one should not mix the matter of a *shidduch* with the education of the person in question to bring them closer to Torah and *mitzvos*. Especially as you write, neither she nor her household know anything about matters of religion. People of this type cannot fathom the extent to which matters of Torah and *mitzvos* are relevant at every single step, and not—as is the common misconception—merely a matter for the morning during *davening*, or on *Shabbos* during *Kiddush*, and the like.

If the discussion between them has already reached a point where "it has gone far"—meaning that one must support the matter as much as possible—then at the very least, it is imperative that he speak with her as soon as possible regarding the essential matters as he knows them. In this, first and foremost, is that which depends primarily on the mistress of the home, namely:

a. *Taharas Hamishpachah*, *tznius*, the *kashrus* of food, etc.

Furthermore, and this is no less essential than the above: as soon as possible, she should move to live within a G-d-fearing family, so that she can see with her own eyes, every single day, what the essence of a Jewish daughter is. And if it is impossible for her to live there full-time, then at the very least, she should be in that environment whenever possible. Also, she should study, or have someone study with her, at least the *Kitzur Dinim* and the necessary *halachos*. Only after a few weeks pass in this manner of conduct should they meet again and discuss whether she accepts upon herself, one hundred percent, everything she has learned regarding all of the above.

It is surprising that you do not mention a word regarding the days of Pesach in the Tomchei Temimim *yeshiva* and its students. Even though a significant portion surely traveled to their homes, I still hope that they received instructions regarding their conduct, especially those who remained within the walls of the *yeshiva*.

With blessings for good tidings and in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *tzu a gezuntn zumer* (for a healthy summer),

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. As you requested, the letter is being sent without waiting for its turn.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the pills from Switzerland, I believe I have already written to you that their use must be strictly under the supervision of a doctor and according to his instructions regarding the dosage, etc.

## 8190

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of many accomplishments and fine character, R' Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 7 Iyar with the good news:

1) The increase in the number of students, may they live, at Beis Lubavitch, and also the organization of a minyan.

May it be His will that the principle of "the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself" be fulfilled in this, such that there will be more and more—meaning an increase in quantity, a greater number of students, as well as in quality, the standard of learning, and the impact that the learning should bring about, leading to action, as the saying goes: "Great is study, for it leads to action."

2) Regarding the improvement in the state of health of your wife, may she live and be well, may it be His will that, according to the saying of our Rebbeim, it should go from good to even better. It is well known that the halachic ruling is that "a healthy and whole body is among the ways of Hashem" (Rambam, Hilchos Deios, beginning of Chapter 4).

3) And last but certainly not least, that your daughter, may she live and be well, is expecting a child. May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time and with ease.

And since we are in the luminous day of Lag B'Omer, the message of which is to bring the hidden and the inner into the revealed (the deepest secrets into the open), may it be that all the good that Hakadosh Baruch Hu grants to everyone within Klal Yisrael should likewise be brought down in a revealed manner, below ten tefachim.

May the merit of your involvement in *hafatzas hamaayanos* in your country, and especially in Beis Lubavitch, stand by you to provide additional blessing and success in all of the above.

Looking forward to good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8191

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the students of the evening yeshiva in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem keep them and may they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the days of *Hagbalah* of this year, which is a *Shabbos Shabbaton* unto Hashem. Its content is the acceptance—by the students of the yeshiva—of good resolutions regarding matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that He fulfill the requests of your hearts for the good in all that was mentioned, and even more.

Certainly, as I have written to many yeshiva students, and especially to students of Chabad yeshivos, you should do everything within your power to be a living example befitting the aforementioned regulations, and in general, to be a *yungerman* and a yeshiva student in the spirit of Chassidus, as is the desire of our *Rebbeim Nesi'im*. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since we have been promised by our Sages of blessed memory that one who comes to purify himself is assisted, and that if a person sanctifies himself a little below, they sanctify him greatly from above.

With blessings for success and for good tidings regarding the above.

## 8192

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the continuation of your studies: it is understood, and indeed simple, that you must study in a yeshiva where both the revealed Torah (Nigleh) and Chassidus are studied together. And the matter of **together** is understood, for in the study of Nigleh, it must be evident that the one studying it has a portion in the study of [Chassidus] as is fitting.

And this is understood from what is explained in various places, among them in Likutei Torah regarding the concept of "fortunate is he who comes here with his learning in his hand," that in the years [of our Sages] they were precise in this matter: it must be "his learning" (literally, in Nigleh) and "in his hand" specifically, so that it does not remain below in this world (Tanya, beginning of Chapter 3). And this is easy to understand.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***8192***

Printed in the booklet "Tzadik L'Melech" 3, p. 96.

**In Likutei Sichos:** Va'eschanan 6, 3; Shir HaShirim 22, 4.

## 8193

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about your daughter, tichyeh, at a time of favor I will once again mention her at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your writing that they are suggesting to repeat the insulin treatment—in general, it is common to repeat the aforementioned treatment. However, recently several different methods have emerged regarding treatments for such an ailment. Some say to continue as until now with insulin and electroconvulsive therapy, etc., while lately, the method of relying solely on medication and therapy sessions is spreading.

May it be the will of the Healer of all flesh, Who performs wonders, that He hasten her recovery through the treatment most appropriate for her.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

It is understood that regarding the practical course of action, you must follow the instructions of the local doctor, though you may (diplomatically) raise the aforementioned points.

## 8194

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5719
Brooklyn

To the avreich Menachem Ben Zion, shichye,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of the 13th and 20th of Sivan, in which you propose expanding the activities of the evening yeshivos, and you yourself add that the matter involves significant expenses, etc.

It is not clear from your letter whether this was written on your own initiative or as a representative of the entire administration of the evening yeshivos. It is understood and simple that while it is correct for each person to explain the situation as it appears to him, and likewise to add suggestions that seem appropriate to him, it is better and more correct regarding such proposals to emphasize each time whether the other members of the administration agree or disagree. This is especially true in a case such as this, where you write that it has already been discussed among the members of the administration.

In any event—as you describe the matter in your letter, and assuming you are writing on behalf of the members of the administration—one must note the magnitude of the expenses involved in this matter. Furthermore, this is the main point: ultimately, one must consider the inner purpose of the evening yeshivos. Even though Torah study in and of itself is a great purpose and essential, it is in the nature of things that the students should continue in the very institutions intended by those who are involved, rather than moving on to other places after a month or a year.

As for the examples you write about, it appears from this that this point is currently on the agenda: how to rectify and improve this. It will not be improved by providing evening meals and the like (even if the funds were readily available, and especially since that is not the case).

At a time of favor, please mention all those you write about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding this.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 895

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5719
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, active in communal needs,
R' Yehoshua Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 Tammuz, along with its enclosure.

Regarding your question concerning the publication of [information about] the "all-day learning" program: Since there are those who oppose this and fear it may cause harm, it is understood that, at least initially, it is not advisable to publish it. In time, you will see whether or not to begin publication. Regarding what you wrote—that it is necessary to preempt the possibility of others initiating such a program—even according to your own letter, it is questionable whether publication would hinder them or, on the contrary, encourage them. Especially since the absence of publication does not imply that the Chabad Yeshiva does not have this program; it only means that money is not being wasted on advertising it. Consequently, there is no basis for the claim that someone else "beat them to it."

Regarding the second question, concerning the general studies at the two schools, etc.: Based on your description of the situation, it is worthwhile to connect with the school that does not consider itself so "prestigious." For in addition to avoiding a waste of time, etc., you will more easily accomplish various matters with them—matters that may even be fundamental—which is not the case with the first school, which, as you write, is prestigious in its own eyes. The difference in the reputation of the two schools will surely not influence parents who want their children to learn [in a Chabad environment], as they are already willing to forgo several things for that purpose.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the change in attitude of... may he live. This is certainly a clear instruction and proof that with the appropriate approach, one can influence many who, for the time being, have not drawn as close as necessary to the Chabad institutions in their camp. This is provided that it is done with ways of pleasantness and through diligent effort.

May it be the will of Hashem that all matters of concealment and confusion be nullified, and that these days be transformed, speedily, into joy and gladness. May we merit, in the immediate future, the fulfillment of the promise that from these "straits" (Mitzrayim) we will come to an inheritance without boundaries (bli metzarim).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8197

B"H, 1 Elul, 5719
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of fine character and many accomplishments, engaged in communal needs,

May Hashem Yisbarach help that for long, good years, you should be able to report good news regarding yourself and regarding each member of your family, may they live and be well—good news in material matters, and also good news in spiritual matters.

As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov’s teaching on the verse, "When you see the donkey... you shall surely help him," is that even with material matters, one can and must serve Hashem Yisbarach. And Avodas Hashem must be specifically with joy and a good heart (see Rambam, end of Hilchos Lulav, and in the Tanya in several places, as noted in the index at the end).

And especially since Divine Providence has granted you success and the merit to exert yourself and work to strengthen and expand the "Beis Lubavitch" in the holy community of London—which, surely, as with all good things, you will go from strength to strength and ascend in holiness—this will surely add to the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach and His success for you and for every member of your family.

And with this, it is understood, and it is also simple, the blessing of the chapter of Tehillim that you will begin to recite: "His years are like generation and generation... so I will sing to Your name forever."

With blessings for good news in all the above, and for a good inscription and sealing for him and for every one of his household members, may they live and be well,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1998

B"H, 14 Elul, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, whose work is work of Heaven,
R' Yehoshua Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 9 Elul and those preceding it, along with the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in the health of your son, Aharon, may he live, and thank you also for the good news regarding the success of the dinner.

Regarding what you wrote about the counter-propaganda, etc.—it is a great wonder, as I have already pointed out several times the importance of making an effort to obtain from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, clippings from newspapers that publish articles about Chabad. Much of their content could also be published in the newspapers in your camp, which would thereby nullify many false and mendacious claims, etc. In such matters, there are agencies in Eretz Yisrael, just as in all countries, that specialize in collecting such newspaper clippings, and in any case, it is worth doing this now...

Regarding what you wrote about the arrival of a *shadar* (emissary) from the Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt—you are correct in what you wrote, as many emissaries do come and are also successful. Regarding your concern that since *anash* will assist, there might be a shortfall [in other areas], etc.—this is something that can be discussed (regarding percentages, etc.). However, in such matters, in order to avoid any resentment, this should not be done based on the opinion of any single individual; rather, it should be done with the knowledge and agreement of several *baalei batim*, and they should consult among themselves regarding the appropriate timing, the conditions, etc.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good news in all the aforementioned, especially since we are now in the month of Elul, the month of mercy, in which, as our Alter Rebbe states, the thirteen attributes of mercy—which are without limit—shine. May this be drawn down in a revealed and manifest good, both in general matters and in personal matters alike.

With blessings for good news and to be inscribed and sealed for good,

**M. Schneerson**

#### 1998

From a facsimile of the letter.

## 8199

B"H, 17 Elul, 5719
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with great energy, R' Shlomo, may he live:

This strengthening should begin immediately, for we find ourselves in the "meritorious days" of the month of Elul, and in the parsha of *Atem Nitzavim Hayom Kulchem*. As the Alter Rebbe emphasizes and explains in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of the parsha, [the goal is] "to be united as one," etc., and "to become a *reshus hayachid* for His unity, may He be blessed." This draws down the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in all matters, as we say three times every day: "Bless us, our Father, [when] we are all as one," etc., as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 32.

**M. Schneerson**

## 801

B"H, 24 Elul, 5719
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a long hiatus, I received your letter along with the *pan*, which will be read at a time of favor at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about your brother, may he live: I believe I have already written to you, and we have also spoken with his mother, may she live, that there is no need to be so distressed if his portion lies in the *avodah* of *Zevulun*—that is, supporting those who study Torah and supporting Torah institutions, while also setting fixed times for the study of *Nigleh* and *Chassidus* for himself. For we do not know what the portion of each person is in this world. Since your brother has already tried, exerted himself, and labored to increase his Torah study and encountered so many difficulties, one should try the path mentioned above. Perhaps the most suitable way is for him to study in a *yeshiva* where they also teach a trade, or that alongside his studies in a *yeshiva*, he should spend some hours learning a trade—naturally, in a *chareidi yeshiva*. May Hashem, who watches over each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*, guide him in what is good for him, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* and for good tidings.

## 802

B"H, 12 Tishrei, 5720

In response to your letter of 7 Tishrei, in which you write about your study schedule, your participation in the evening shiurim, and your study of the necessary halachos—and surely, even though you do not mention it, you have also begun to keep the three known daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and to engage in Chassidus in a manner appropriate to your overall situation.

May it be Hashem’s will that you succeed in all of the above, and that your study be in a manner of *yegiah* (for then our Sages have informed us: "You have labored and you have found"). This is especially relevant since you write that you have begun to put on tefillin (and surely according to our custom, after a few days, with the bracha), for the concept of tefillin is the submission of the heart and the mind (as explained in the Shulchan Aruch and cited in Tanya, Chapter 41) with the necessary persistence and diligence.

May it be Hashem’s will that you also influence your friends, *sheyichyu*, in these matters.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy holiday.

## 8173

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...To add even more, I emphasize the great work that you have invested and are investing **even now** among our Sephardic brethren in Morocco, in a manner of *mosif v'holech* (increasing and continuing), even though this involves the exile of several of anash, they and their families, far from their place of residence and surroundings, etc. And all the more so, it is incumbent upon anash to do as much as they can regarding the aforementioned, and surely there will be further good fruit from this effort to draw hearts closer and unite them, for every action in this regard—even a physical one—is important.

As is known, the saying of the Baal Shem Tov—this year being the two-hundredth year since his histalkus-hilula—is that a soul comes into this world and lives in a body for seventy or eighty years in order to do a favor for a fellow Jew, whether in physical or spiritual matters.

This surely requires no length or explanation, as the above is part of the holy work of "spreading your wellsprings outward" even among our Sephardic brethren. Although for ages there have been matters of the inner dimension of Torah among them, it is only in these **very** last years that the wellsprings of the Chassidus of the Baal Shem Tov and his students in general, and of his student’s student, our Rebbeim and Nesi'ei Chabad in particular, have spread there.

Through paths of pleasantness and drawing near in many areas, the dissemination of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov will surely grow, and it will be accepted and absorbed more and more deeply.

May it be His will that, since we are in *yomin zakain* (meritorious days) and we "bring about merit through a meritorious day," you will bring good tidings of good that is visible and revealed in all the aforementioned. For the month of Tishrei is the seventh month, which is entirely (and not only the Yomim Tovim within it) called "seventh," and as our Sages explain, it is "satiated with all good." The words of our Rebbeim and Nesi'im are well known, that this is a general month for the entire year, and we draw its matters into all the days of the year.

May it be His will that it should be so in all matters... both general and specific, to draw from the blessing and goodness of this month into the coming days, with joy and goodness of heart, and to increase in good deeds and also to influence others in this.

With blessings for the expansion of... in this matter, and in a manner of "spreading forth," etc.

Awaiting good tidings in the aforementioned.

#### ***8173***

Printed in the booklet *Tzadik L'Melech* 1, p. 109.

**The words of our Rebbeim are well known:** See *Sefer HaSichos 5750*, Vol. 1, p. 72 and footnote 18.

## 6105

B.H., 9 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

*[Letter from the Secretariat regarding the above matter]*

B.H., 12 Sivan, 5719

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

In a special package, we are sending you the *kovetz pilpul* of the students that was published on the eve of Shavuos. We hope that in time, more such *kovetzes* will appear.

This *kovetz* contains seven *shiurim* in *nigleh* and seven in *Chassidus*, which were delivered by fourteen students. Beginning in the month of Kislev of this year, they were organized—according to the suggestion of the Rebbe—into two groups, one in *nigleh* and one in *Chassidus*. In addition to their studies in the regular Yeshiva schedule, they dedicated themselves to study with greater intensity in a manner of *u'fartzta*.

Further details regarding the founding of these groups, their method of study, the dedication and diligence of the students, and their success, with the help of Hashem, are surely known to you by report, etc.

We hereby suggest that you organize two such groups among the students of your Yeshiva as well. It is understood that the students chosen for this must be among those worthy of this mantle, and that they do this not out of any compulsion, but of their own good will.

The number seven is not absolute.

After you organize these groups, you will surely also pay attention to what is practiced here: that the students deliver a topic in *nigleh* and a topic in *Chassidus*, each according to his group, and afterwards put it into writing in such a way that the students' *pilpulim* can be brought to print, whether as a special *kovetz* or as part of a general *kovetz*.

Please inform us of everything done in this regard. Thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8,208

B"H, 20 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following a long hiatus, your letter of 15 Teves was received.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the administration of Tomchei Temimim in Lod. From it, you will see my perspective and opinion regarding the reasons you wrote in opposition to including a section on Chassidus in the students' pilpul journal.

I would add that the letter was written after **great** restraint, as there is much more that remains on the pen.

The main point, which is **beyond doubt** to me, is that had the aforementioned journal been printed several months ago (naturally, together with both the Chassidus and Nigleh sections), there would be more students learning Toras HaChassidus today. Even if I do not know exactly how many, or whether they would reach the greatest depths, it is well known how much our Rebbeim, our Nesi'im, exerted themselves and commanded us to disseminate the study of Chassidus, without first requiring a guarantee or assurance that a specific number of people would be impressed by the repetition of a maamar, and specifically in a way that would make them the greatest ovdim and maskilim.

I must say that your opposition to the entire matter is not understandable to me at all. For, as is obvious, the reasons you write—that there is no student who would be suitable for this—are **not at all** appropriate. This is as I wrote in my letter to the Tomchei Temimim administration, following my conversation here with the students who came to us from Tomchei Temimim in Lod.

It is understood that there is room for other reasons, but reasons of this type—the very existence of such a reason—only further increase the recognition of the benefit of printing the aforementioned section.

May it be the will of Hashem that, despite all the obstacles, delays, concealments, and hidden factors from within and without, our Rebbeim, our Nesi'im, will be victorious, in a manner of "breaking forth," with kindness and mercy. May the study of Toras HaChassidus spread in a manner of "increasing and going, increasing and illuminating," until "the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea."

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

***

**8,208**
From a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Shlomo Chaim:** Kesselman. Further letters to him appear above, 7,816, and in the references in the notes there.

**Copy of my letter:** Above, 8,192.

**In the students' pilpul journal:** Above, letter 8,205, and in the references in the notes there.

## 8190

B"H, 22 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the illustrious Rabbi, the distinguished Chassid, who is involved in communal affairs and the dissemination of Chassidus, etc.,
R' Shlomo Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 18 Teves, I have requested the Kehot management to reply as soon as possible regarding the printing of the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe.

Regarding what you wrote about the young man... may he live—it is difficult to know what can be done in this matter. Pressure is effective in matters that depend on willpower, but only rarely in matters that depend on ability. Since you have already involved yourself in this matter, you have surely seen the correspondence; and although I am not familiar with the customs of Jerusalem, the Holy City, in such matters, it seems that the demands are excessive, even among those who are prone to exaggeration.

Regarding what you wrote about the illustrious Rabbi, etc., R' D. may he live, Chanzin—it is strange that he does not mention his rabbinical position. Especially since Rabbi Gelernter, may he live, visited me recently, and in the course of our conversation, he mentioned that in his meeting with you, he also brought up this issue. Furthermore, I have not received any information on this from R' D.H., may he live...

Regarding what you wrote about the Talmudic Encyclopedia, my position on this project is well known, and I will therefore act in the appropriate manner should the request you mention be made. However, I must reiterate what I said several months ago in my discussion with the representatives of the Claims Conference: I expressed my surprise that they do not provide more assistance for the printing of the Encyclopedia. They replied that, on the contrary, they would be very happy if the publishers were more diligent, as they would then increase their grant. When I asked if they had informed the management of the project of this, they answered in the affirmative.

It is my hope that in connection with the Yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the tenth of the coming month, there will be an increase in all Chabad activities in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, as well as in Chabad activities everywhere. For to my regret, I am not yet receiving good news and reports of joy as I should, and perhaps not even a fraction of that.

And regarding the more immediate future—concerning the Reshet school committee in the Jerusalem area, which apparently has not yet begun its activities, and also regarding the Chabad housing project there, which I believe has been in the "talking stage" for over a year—they informed me... that they hope... that by the end of the month of Shevat there will be... the laying of the cornerstone! This sorrow is added to the sorrow regarding the situation in the Holy Land concerning the Toras Emes Yeshiva, etc., etc.

Since we are commanded to conclude with good, and the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal harshly with His creatures, surely the conclusion and seal of all the above will be as the phrasing of the prayer in which we ask and act before the Master of Blessings: that which is good for us.

May it be His will that this happens in our immediate future.

With respect and blessing for good news regarding all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

Due to a reason, the shipment was delayed. In the meantime, representatives of the Mafdal (in the Holy Land) visited me with a proposal and request: It is (nearly) certain that there will be no candidate from the United States for the position of Chief Rabbi, and they requested that I influence you to agree to be a candidate. If you do, they will (according to the negotiations they are currently conducting) cancel the age limit proposal, and your election would be guaranteed.

I replied that you are surely aware of what I said to their leader in our conversation this summer—that in my opinion, you should not desire the aforementioned position. Nevertheless, since they say the situation is critical, affects many, etc.—I will ask you about the situation regarding the above, what has changed recently, etc., and when you answer me, I will be able to say if my opinion on the matter has changed. This is the essence of the conversation in general.

It is understood that in such a matter, the more detail, the better.

## 811

B"H, 24 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

Some time ago, I received the list of students who were given Chanukah gelt. According to the directive, this is intended for those who study the teachings of Chassidus—which, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) of blessed memory, is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov of blessed memory. The list contains approximately 140 students—may they increase.

It is understood and simple that among such a number of students—many of whom have been studying for several years in a Yeshiva where, since its founding, the study of Chassidus, specifically Chassidus Chabad (i.e., through understanding and intellectual grasp, unlike the approach of the Chassidim of Chesed-Gevurah-Tiferes, and so on)—there should naturally be many who understand concepts in Chassidus with appropriate explanation. The test of this is whether they can explain it in their own words (*mit aygene osiyos*), rather than merely reciting it by rote in the language used in a particular place, without having any connection to the content of the ideas.

Since in the teachings of Chassidus there are many books, *kuntreisim*, and *maamarim*, and as a general rule in our holy Torah, "words of Torah are poor in one place and rich in another," it is certain that through this method of study—which is the **only** one that aligns with the will of the Yeshiva’s founders and administrators—there is room to fulfill what is stated in one place through the explanation found in another.

From what has been said, it is understood that when the proposal was made to publish a collection of the students' *pilpulim*, and that at the beginning at least seven of them would suffice, the difficulty should have been: out of all the aforementioned eligible students, which ones should be chosen as the first seven?

Yet, the opposite is the case: although many months have passed since this was discussed and proposed, there appears to be no movement on this, and it is obvious that there is no actual activity, at least according to the information here. The main obstacle is, **as it were**, with the students who study the teachings of Chassidus.

I would appreciate it if you could explain this contradiction: how can there be a list of 140 recipients of Chanukah gelt, yet an inability to find at least **seven** who are suitable for the aforementioned task?

I would be grateful if the response is received before the 10th of Shevat, the day of the *histalkus* and *hillula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—who is the active administrator of the Tomchei Temimim and Toras Emes Yeshivos in all corners of the world, Yeshivos whose study program is **known** according to what is explained in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) of blessed memory.

With respect and blessing,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 8111

B.H., 17 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter of 12 Shevat, and those that preceded it.

At an auspicious time, I will mention those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote about the summer camp—that it requires running around to offices and a great deal of time, etc., many weeks before the camp begins, and that consequently it will cause disruptions in the school as it did last year, and likewise regarding the financial responsibility, where you also do not know who is bearing the burden, etc.:

Based on the above, at the very next meeting of the Reshet, you should present all of these points and your doubts regarding this matter. It is understood that there is no room for disruptions in the school as there were last year, for "a miracle does not occur every time." The same applies to the financial situation. Let them inform me of their clear decision, as mentioned above, in such a way that there will be no disruptions in the school, provided there is someone who will occupy themselves with the camp, and also that there is someone who can—at least estimate—the expenses of the camp, with a near-certain estimation. It is understood that if both of these matters remain in the negative, or even in doubt, then they should not hold a camp this year—until such time as members of Anash eventually bestir themselves and are able to do so without causing destruction to another institution.

Regarding what you wrote about the bicentennial year of the passing and Hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, and that this was discussed at meetings of educators, etc.—you surely know that already at the beginning of the school year there was an instruction regarding this from the Department of Education. Regarding appearances by Anash and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in this regard, it is understood that there is room for the aforementioned when there is no concern, or even a suspicion of a concern, regarding providing a "hechsher" for the venue where they are appearing. And it is understood that any additional noise about the matter increases the possibility of such a concern. Therefore, regarding this as well, they should consult among themselves—those who are familiar with the conditions of the institutions and the locations of the aforementioned question, etc.

It was pleasant for me to read at the end of your letter about the Bar Mitzvah celebration. I have already written to the administration of our institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and in Morocco, regarding the lack of order in this matter among our Sephardic brethren, who postpone the Bar Mitzvah celebration until it is possible to have a full family feast, etc., and along with this, some of them even postpone the beginning of the laying of Tefillin, etc., Heaven forbid. If only they would be awakened from here on in to rectify the aforementioned.

It is surprising that you are so brief regarding the gathering in the village and the farbrengen of the day of the Hillula. Surely you, or someone like you, will fill me in with detailed information about this. May it be the will [of Hashem] that they be joyous and result in good that is revealed and apparent.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings regarding all of the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 812

812

B”H, 2 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’ Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Shevat, and those preceding it,

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good news regarding all the matters about which you write. My hope is strong that, since we see that finally, even circles that previously opposed your work are now recognizing it—and not only that, but they themselves are assisting you—this recognition will add joy to all the workers and their leaders at the helm. This increase in joy will, in turn, increase the activities, diminish the concealments and hidden obstacles, and magnify the success.

At a time of favor, please mention all those about whom you write at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I look forward to hearing good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for good news and for a happy Purim holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

## 813

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received in due time the news regarding the state of your health and that you were admitted to the *beis harfuah* (I generally do not use the term that people call *beis hacholim*, as it is also illogical, for one enters there to be healed, and our Sages of blessed memory have said that a person should always speak in refined language). I was pleased to subsequently receive news of the success of the medical treatment and that you have already returned home.

At an auspicious time, I mentioned you at the *tziyun*.

And since we are approaching the time of our freedom, may it be His will that you have freedom from all matters that cause distraction, and that you utilize the talents with which you have been gifted by Divine Providence for the dissemination of traditional Judaism, and the wellsprings of Chassidus in particular.

Especially since, according to the information I received, you have taken upon yourself to be active in the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus in connection with the bicentennial year of the *histalkus*-*hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov this year.

With respect and blessings for a kosher and happy holiday and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8116

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5721, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs,
R' Yehoshua Schneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

We acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 7 Nissan, along with the enclosure. Enclosed herewith is the response to the young man... may he live.

Surely, if further explanation is needed, you will find the appropriate words.

However, what is surprising in your letter is that you mention every possible option, except for the one that must come first and foremost: namely, full-time Torah study throughout the entire day. This is especially pertinent now that the aforementioned individual has been released from the studies mandated by the government.

May it be the will of Hashem that, just as the enclosed response suggests that the aforementioned individual should influence the rest of Anash, he should also influence the administration of Yeshivas Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Melbourne, so that they, too, recognize the necessity and truth of the aforementioned order. Even if one were to argue that the time has not yet arrived for this in every location, ultimately, a beginning must be made.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

S. M. Simpson
Secretary

## Ch'riz

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and esteemed R' Chaim Zelig, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of pauses, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos was received.

I read with surprise and wonder that you (and someone else) are in doubt as to whether you should continue your work on the Kfar Chabad Vaad. The reason for my surprise is certainly understood, for it is clear that the Kfar Vaad—founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael—is such that anyone who can assist the Vaad in its establishment and development, fortunate is his portion, and it is a great merit for him. Furthermore, this also adds to and increases the blessing of Hashem in the personal matters of all those who act as stated.

Despite the simplicity of the answer, I am hastening to write clearly regarding this, as it seems that the "old and foolish king" is exerting his cunning, as is his wont with various strange temptations, to confuse those involved, including him, in this matter.

And according to the instruction of Chazal—from the positive you hear the negative—regarding those whose actions weaken the position of the Kfar, its establishment, and its development, there is no need to dwell on a distressing matter.

As we stand in the days of *Hagbalah* preceding the Giving of the Torah, whose ways are ways of pleasantness and peace, yet with the appropriate strength, my hope is strong that this is how he and his colleagues on the Vaad, may they live, will conduct themselves: as stated, in ways of pleasantness and peace, but while maintaining a strong guard over the material and spiritual matters of the Kfar together, without taking into account those who, for the sake of imagined personal gains—imagined in the extreme—do not care, Heaven forbid, about the aforementioned.

With blessings for good tidings, and in the phrasing of the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—for the reception of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

#### ***Ch'riz***

Published in "Kfar Chabad," issue 556 (3 Nissan, 5753), p. 24.

**R' Chaim Zelig:** Altein. Additional letters to him—above 7,904, and in the references in the notes there.

## 8118

8118

2 Menachem Av, 5721

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R’ Yaakov, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 14 Tammuz was received, and upon reading your letter, the wonder regarding the long silence is understood.

Regarding what you wrote about the necessity of the institution, etc., the doubt and the question regarding this is surprising. Especially in these days, following the auspicious days, the days of redemption 12 and 13 Tammuz, when it is known to what extent my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, sacrificed his life for the matter of education in purity and holiness, even when it involved actual danger to life, Heaven forbid. How much more so is the effort and exertion that must be invested in this when one is in a place where there is no such danger—and on the contrary.

And since, as mentioned above, the matter is good and necessary, and the merit of the public assists them, it will certainly be successful in both quantity and quality, provided that you continue the work in this with dedication and giving, as the Sages instructed: "You labored and you found."

With blessings for good news in all that was mentioned, and for increase in both quantity and quality, with joy and a glad heart, in the holy institution "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok," which you have merited and succeeded in founding in your camp,

**M. Schneerson**

From a photocopy of the letter published in *Kfar Chabad*, issue 539 (5 Elul 5792), p. 16.
